Makki Leaving Haram for Hajj: Dam Obligatory if Miqat Passed Without Ihram
Ruling on Makki leaving Haram for Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a Makki enters ihram outside the Haram and does not return, and identify the consequence of returning.

Core Idea
A Makki must enter ihram from within the Haram; passing it without ihram incurs a dam unless he returns before Arafah.

This passage clarifies the miqat obligation for a resident of Mecca (Makki) performing Hajj. Unlike non-Makkans whose miqat is a specific boundary outside Mecca, the Makki's miqat is the Haram itself. If he leaves the sanctuary and enters ihram in the surrounding area (Hil) without first returning to the Haram, he has violated the miqat and owes a sacrifice. However, if he returns to the Haram before standing at Arafah, the ruling follows the same difference of opinion as for a non-Makkan who passes his miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the legal consequence for a Makki who goes directly from Hil to Arafah without returning to Haram? The passage states: upon him is a sheep (dam).
2
Understand the reason
Why is a dam obligatory? Because the Haram is his miqat, and he passed it without ihram. The text explicitly says: 'because his miqat is the Haram and he has passed it without ihram.'
3
Recognize the exception
What if he returns to the Haram before Arafah? Then the ruling follows the previous ikhtilaf for the Afaqi (non-Makkan). This means the dam may be waived depending on the view adopted.
4
Connect to broader principle
The miqat is defined by residence: for Makkis, it is the Haram itself. This is unique to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may have different miqat regulations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمَكِّيُّ يُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ فَأَحْرَمَ وَلَمْ يُعِدُ إِلَى الْحَرَم وَوَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ لِأَنَّ وَقْتَهُ الْحَرَمُ وَ قَدْ جَاوَزَهُ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامِ فَإِن عَادَ إِلَى الْحَرَم وَلَبّى أو لَمْ يُلَبّ فَهُوَ عَلَى الاخْتِلَافِ الَّذِى ذَكَرُنَاهُ فِي الْأَفَاقِى أَوْ
ترجمہ اور اگر مکی حرم سے حل کی طرف نکلا دارنحالیکہ وہ حج کا ارادہ رکھتا ہے پس اس نے احرام باندھا اور حرم کی طرف نہیں لوٹا بلکہ وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر ایک بکری کی قربانی واجب ہے کیونکہ مکی کا میقات اور حرم ہے اور حال یہ کہ وہ اپنے میقات سے بغیر احرام تجاوز کر گیا پھر اگر مکی مذکور ( عرفات جانے سے پہلے ) حرم کی طرف لوٹا اور تلبیہ کہا یا نہیں کہا تو یہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو ہم نے آفاقی
کے حق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And when a Makki goes out intending Hajj, and he puts on ihram and does not return to the Haram, and he stops at Arafah, then upon him is a sheep because his miqat is the Haram and he has passed it without ihram. Then if he returns to the Haram and recites the talbiyah or does not recite it, then it is upon the difference that we mentioned for the Afaqi. Translation: And if a Makki goes out from the Haram to the Hil intending Hajj, then he puts on ihram and does not return to the Haram but rather stops at Arafah, then upon him is the sacrifice of one goat because the miqat of the Makki is the Haram and he has passed his miqat without ihram. Then if the mentioned Makki returns to the Haram (before going to Arafah) and recites talbiyah or not, then it is upon the difference that we mentioned regarding the Afaqi. The explanation is clear.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage states a rule: A resident of Mecca (Makki) intending Hajj must enter ihram from the Haram. If he goes out to the Hil (the area outside the Haram), puts on ihram there, and goes directly to Arafah without returning to the Haram, he owes a sheep (dam) because he passed his miqat (the Haram boundary) without ihram. However, if he returns to the Haram before standing at Arafah, the ruling follows the same ikhtilaf as for the Afaqi (non-Makkan) who passes the miqat and then returns. That earlier difference likely concerns whether the dam is dropped if he returns and re-enters ihram from the Haram. The text confirms the principle: the Haram is the miqat for Meccans.

Key Terms
مکی (Makki): A person who is a resident of Mecca (within the Haram).
حل (Hil): The area outside the Haram of Mecca, i.e., non-sanctuary territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Makki leaves the Haram for Hajj, puts on ihram in the Hil, and goes directly to Arafah without returning, what is required?
A) Nothing
B) A sheep (dam)
C) A camel
D) Only repentance

Key Takeaway
A Makki's miqat is the Haram; passing it without ihram obligates a dam unless he returns before Arafah, in which case the ikhtilaf applies.

Dam for Mutamatti' Leaving Haram After Umrah
Ruling on mutamatti' leaving Haram after Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who leaves the Haram after Umrah and identify the condition that exempts him from the dam.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' who leaves the Haram for Hajj ihram owes a dam unless he returns before Arafah.

After completing Umrah, a mutamatti' becomes like a Makki and his miqat for Hajj is the Haram. This lesson explains the ruling when he goes outside the Haram to put on ihram and the condition under which the dam is lifted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The mutamatti' finishes Umrah, then leaves the Haram, puts on ihram for Hajj, and stops at Arafah. The ruling is that a dam is wajib.
The dam is due to delaying ihram from the Haram.
2
Understand the legal analogy
After Umrah, the mutamatti' is treated like a Makki (a resident of Makkah). The ihram of a Makki for Hajj must be from the Haram.
This is based on the principle that the miqat for a Makki is the Haram.
3
Note the condition that removes the obligation
If the mutamatti' returns to the Haram before standing at Arafah and recites talbiyah, then no dam is due.
The condition is return to Haram plus talbiyah before Arafah.
4
Recognise the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
The ruling is subject to the same ikhtilaf as for the Afaqi (non-Makkan) who passes the miqat and returns. Some scholars hold that return alone suffices, others require talbiyah.
The relied-upon view is that return with talbiyah is necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُتَمَعُ إِذَا فَرَغَ مِنْ عُمَرَتِهِ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ فَأَحْرَمَ وَوَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ وَأتَى بِأَفَعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ صَارَ بِمَنزِلَةِ الْمَكِى وَالحَرامُ الْمَكِّيِّ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ لِمَا ذَكَرِنَا فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِتَاخِيرِهِ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَى الْحَرَمِ وَأَهَلَّ فِيهِ قَبْلَ أَن يَقِفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَلَا شَيَ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ فِي الْآفَاقِى
ترجمہ اور متمتع جب اپنے عمرہ سے فارغ ہوا پھر حرم سے باہر نکل کر حج کا احرام باندھا اور وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اس لئے کہ یہ شخص جب مکہ میں داخل ہوا اور افعال عمرہ ادا کئے تو یہ بمنزلہ مکی کے ہو گیا اور کی کا احترام حرم سے ہوتا ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی۔ اس لئے احرام کو حرم سے مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ پھر اگر تمتع مذکور وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے حرم کی طرف لوٹا اور ائیں تلبیہ کہا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں رہا۔ اور یہ مسئلہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو آفاقی کی صورت میں گذرا۔
تشریح محتاج بیان نہیں ہے۔
And the mutamatti', when he finishes his Umrah, then goes out from the Haram, puts on ihram and stops at Arafah, upon him is a dam because when he entered Mecca and performed the actions of Umrah, he becomes like a Makki, and the ihram of a Makki is from the Haram due to what we mentioned. So the dam becomes obligatory upon him due to delaying it (ihram) from it (the Haram). Then if he returns to the Haram and recites talbiyah in it before standing at Arafah, then nothing is upon him. And this is on the difference that preceded regarding the Afaqi. Translation: And the mutamatti', when he finishes his Umrah, then goes out from the Haram, puts on ihram for Hajj and stops at Arafah, then upon him is a dam because this person, when he entered Mecca and performed the actions of Umrah, becomes like a Makki, and the ihram of a Makki is from the Haram for the reason we mentioned. Therefore, due to delaying the ihram from the Haram, dam is obligatory upon him. Then if the mentioned mutamatti' returns to the Haram before standing at Arafah and recites talbiyah, then nothing is obligatory upon him. And this issue is on the same difference that passed in the case of the Afaqi. The explanation needs no elaboration.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage lays down the rule for a person performing Tamattu' Hajj (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break). After completing the Umrah, he becomes a resident of Makkah (like a Makki) for the purpose of Hajj ihram. Therefore, his miqat for Hajj is the Haram. If he goes out of the Haram to the Hil to put on ihram for Hajj and then goes directly to Arafah without returning to the Haram, he owes a dam. However, if he returns to the Haram before Arafah and enters ihram there (with talbiyah or without), he is exempt from the dam. This ruling is subject to the same internal Hanafi ikhtilaf as mentioned for the Afaqi (non-Makkan) who passes the miqat. The preferred view is that returning to the Haram removes the dam.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A pilgrim performing Tamattu' Hajj: performing Umrah first, then after a break performing Hajj in the same journey.
آفاقی (āfāqī): A pilgrim who comes from outside the miqat regions; a non-Makkan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a mutamatti' owe a dam for leaving the Haram to put on ihram for Hajj?
A) Always, regardless of return
B) Only if he does not return to the Haram before Arafah
C) Only if he returns to the Haram
D) Never, because he is not a Makki

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' must enter ihram for Hajj from the Haram; leaving without returning before Arafah incurs a wajib dam.

Ruling for a Meccan Leaving the Haram for Hajj Without Returning
Ruling for a Meccan who leaves Haram without returning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Meccan who leaves the Haram without returning, explain the dalil, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on returning and reciting talbiyah.

Core Idea
A Meccan’s miqat is the Haram; passing it without ihram requires a sacrifice.

This lesson examines the ruling for a resident of Makkah (Makki) who intends Hajj but leaves the Haram boundary without returning. The Hanafi school holds that a sacrifice (shaat) is wajib because the miqat for a Makki is the Haram itself. Additionally, a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn arises if the person returns and recites talbiyah before 'Arafah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A Meccan (resident of Haram) goes out to Hil intending Hajj, dons ihram, and does not return to the Haram before standing at 'Arafah.
The miqat for a Makki is the Haram itself.
2
State the ruling
Upon him is a sheep (shaat) as wajib.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because it's a compensation for passing the miqat without ihram.
3
Analyse the dalil
The proof: 'because his miqat is the Haram and he has passed it without ihram.' This establishes a legal cause (illah) for the obligation.
The illah is passing the designated miqat (Haram) without ihram.
4
Consider the return scenario
If the Makki returns to the Haram before 'Arafah and recites talbiyah (or not), the ruling follows the ikhtilaf mentioned for an Afaaqi (non-Meccan).
This refers to a dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa: no dam if he returns and recites talbiyah. Sahibayn: dam still required. The mufta bihi is Imam Abu Hanifa's view.
The practical consequence is whether a sacrifice is owed after returning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکی حرم سے حل کی طرف حج کے احرام کے لئے نکلا احرام باندھا اور حرم کی طرف نہیں لوٹا بلکہ وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر ایک بکری کی قربانی لازم ہے
وَإِذَا خَرَجَ الْمَكِّيُّ يُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ فَأَحْرَمَ وَلَمْ يُعِدُ إِلَى الْحَرَم وَوَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ لِأَنَّ وَقْتَهُ الْحَرَمُ وَ قَدْ جَاوَزَهُ بِغَيْرِ إِحْرَامِ فَإِن عَادَ إِلَى الْحَرَم وَلَبّى أو لَمْ يُلَبّ فَهُوَ عَلَى الاخْتِلَافِ الَّذِى ذَكَرُنَاهُ فِي الْأَفَاقِى أَوْ
ترجمہ اور اگر مکی حرم سے حل کی طرف نکلا دارنحالیکہ وہ حج کا ارادہ رکھتا ہے پس اس نے احرام باندھا اور حرم کی طرف نہیں لوٹا بلکہ وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر ایک بکری کی قربانی واجب ہے کیونکہ مکی کا میقات اور حرم ہے اور حال یہ کہ وہ اپنے میقات سے بغیر احرام تجاوز کر گیا پھر اگر مکی مذکور ( عرفات جانے سے پہلے ) حرم کی طرف لوٹا اور تلبیہ کہا یا نہیں کہا تو یہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو ہم نے آفاقی
کے حق میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
A Meccan went out to Hil intending Hajj, donned ihram and did not return to the Haram but stood at Arafah, so upon him is one goat. And if a Meccan goes out intending Hajj and dons ihram and does not return to the Haram and stands at Arafah, upon him is a sheep because his miqat is the Haram and he has passed it without ihram. Then if he returns to the Haram and says talbiyah or does not, then it is upon the difference we mentioned for the Afaaqi. Translation: And if a Meccan goes out from Haram to Hil while intending Hajj, then he dons ihram and does not return to the Haram but stands at Arafah, then upon him is one goat wajib because the miqat of a Meccan is the Haram and he has passed his miqat without ihram. Then if the mentioned Meccan returns to the Haram (before going to Arafat) and says talbiyah or not, then it is upon the same difference we mentioned for the Afaaqi. Commentary is clear.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a Meccan who intends Hajj and leaves the Haram area (to Hil) and dons ihram there without returning to the Haram to begin ihram from within it. The ruling is that he must sacrifice a sheep (one goat) because his designated miqat is the Haram itself. By passing beyond the Haram boundary without ihram, he has violated the prescribed limit. However, if before standing at Arafah he returns to the Haram and recites talbiyah (or even without talbiyah), then the ruling follows the same ikhtilaf (disagreement) that was mentioned earlier for the non-Meccan (Afaaqi) who passes his miqat. That earlier difference was between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether a dam is wujub or not when returning and reciting talbiyah. The commentary clarifies that the principle is straightforward: the miqat for a Meccan is the Haram, so leaving it without ihram necessitates a sacrifice.

Key Terms
مکی (Makki): A person residing within the Haram of Makkah or within the miqat boundaries, for whom the Haram itself is the miqat for Hajj.
وقوف عرفہ (Woquf 'Arafah): Standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, which is a pillar (rukn) of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a Meccan who leaves the Haram, dons ihram for Hajj at Hil, and does not return to the Haram before standing at Arafah?
A) No sacrifice is required
B) A sheep is wajib
C) A camel is wajib
D) Hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
A Meccan's miqat is the Haram; leaving it without returning necessitates a sacrificial sheep (wajib), with an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of returning and reciting talbiyah.

Mutamatti' Leaving the Haram After Umrah: Ruling and Ikhtilaf
Ruling for a mutamatti' who leaves the Haram after Umrah to begin Hajj ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mutamatti' who leaves the Haram after Umrah for Hajj ihram, explain when a dam is required, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the waiver condition.

Core Idea
A mutamatti' leaving the Haram for Hajj ihram owes a dam; returning and reciting talbiyah before Arafah may waive it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario for a mutamatti' pilgrim: after completing Umrah, he leaves the Haram to begin his Hajj ihram. The passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the ruling and the reasoning behind it, and also highlights a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. By understanding the underlying analogy, you will grasp why the dam is owed and how it can be avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act: a mutamatti' finishes Umrah, leaves the Haram, dons Hajj ihram from outside, and stands at Arafah. The ruling: a dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib.
The ruling is clear from the opening statement.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The rationale: after performing Umrah in Makkah, the mutamatti' becomes like a Meccan (Makki). For a Meccan, the miqat for Hajj is the Haram itself. Delaying the ihram from the proper place (the Haram) necessitates a dam.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to the Meccan.
3
Identify the waiver condition
If the mutamatti' returns to the Haram and recites the talbiyah (proclamation of ihram) there before standing at Arafah, nothing is due from him. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The condition: returning and reciting talbiyah inside the Haram before Arafah.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the dam is still wajib even if he returns and recites talbiyah. This ikhtilaf is the same as the one previously mentioned for the Afaaqi (non-Meccan) pilgrim.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متمتع جب عمرہ سے فارغ ہوا پھر حرم سے باہر نکل کر حج کا احرام باندھا اور وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے
وَالْمُتَمَعُ إِذَا فَرَغَ مِنْ عُمَرَتِهِ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ فَأَحْرَمَ وَوَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمْ لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا دَخَلَ مَكَّةَ وَأتَى بِأَفَعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ صَارَ بِمَنزِلَةِ الْمَكِى وَالحَرامُ الْمَكِّيِّ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ لِمَا ذَكَرِنَا فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِتَاخِيرِهِ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ رَجَعَ إِلَى الْحَرَمِ وَأَهَلَّ فِيهِ قَبْلَ أَن يَقِفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَلَا شَيَ عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ عَلَى الْخِلَافِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ فِي الْآفَاقِى
ترجمہ اور متمتع جب اپنے عمرہ سے فارغ ہوا پھر حرم سے باہر نکل کر حج کا احرام باندھا اور وقوف عرفہ کیا تو اس پر دم واجب ہے اس لئے کہ یہ شخص جب مکہ میں داخل ہوا اور افعال عمرہ ادا کئے تو یہ بمنزلہ مکی کے ہو گیا اور کی کا احترام حرم سے ہوتا ہے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی۔ اس لئے احرام کو حرم سے مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے اس پر دم لازم ہوگا۔ پھر اگر تمتع مذکور وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے حرم کی طرف لوٹا اور ائیں تلبیہ کہا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں رہا۔ اور یہ مسئلہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو آفاقی کی صورت میں گذرا۔
تشریح محتاج بیان نہیں ہے۔
The mutamatti' when he finishes his Umrah, then goes out from the Haram and dons ihram for Hajj and stands at Arafah, then upon him is a dam. And the mutamatti' when he finishes his Umrah, then goes out from the Haram and dons ihram and stands at Arafah, then upon him is a dam because when he entered Makkah and performed the actions of Umrah, he became like a Meccan, and the ihram of a Meccan is from the Haram for the reason we mentioned, so the dam is necessary for delaying it from him. Then if the mentioned mutamatti' returns to the Haram and recites talbiyah therein before standing at Arafah, then nothing is upon him, and it is upon the difference that preceded for the Afaaqi. Translation: And the mutamatti' when he finishes his Umrah, then goes out from the Haram and dons ihram for Hajj and stands at Arafah, then upon him is a dam wajib because this person when he entered Makkah and performed the actions of Umrah, he becomes like a Meccan, and the ihram of a Meccan is from the Haram due to the reason we mentioned. Therefore, by delaying the ihram from the Haram, the dam becomes necessary. Then if the mentioned mutamatti' before standing at Arafah returns to the Haram and recites talbiyah therein, then nothing remains wajib upon him. And this issue is upon the same difference that occurred in the case of the Afaaqi. Commentary does not need explanation.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage addresses the mutamatti' (one who performs Umrah during the Hajj season and then Hajj separately). After completing his Umrah, if he leaves the Haram area to don ihram for Hajj and proceeds to stand at Arafah without returning to the Haram for ihram, he becomes liable for a dam (sacrifice of a sheep or goat). The reason is that upon entering Makkah and performing Umrah, he attains the status of a Makki (Meccan) for the purpose of Hajj ihram. Just as a Meccan's miqat is the Haram, so this mutamatti' must initiate his Hajj ihram from within the Haram. By failing to do so, he has delayed his ihram from the proper place, necessitating a dam. However, if before standing at Arafah he returns to the Haram and recites the talbiyah (the proclamation of ihram) there, then nothing is required from him. This scenario is subject to the same ikhtilaf previously mentioned for the Afaaqi (non-Meccan) regarding whether the dam is waived by returning and reciting talbiyah. The commentary notes that this is clear.

Key Terms
متمتع (Mutamatti'): A pilgrim who performs Umrah during the Hajj months and then performs Hajj in the same year, with a break in between, requiring a sacrifice.
دم (Dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for violating a rule of Hajj or Umrah.
آفاقی (Afaaqi): A pilgrim who comes from outside the miqat regions (i.e., from beyond the miqat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a mutamatti' leaves the Haram after Umrah to don Hajj ihram and goes directly to Arafah?
A) His Hajj is invalid.
B) He must offer a dam.
C) He must repeat Umrah.
D) He may continue without penalty.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who delays Hajj ihram from the Haram owes a dam, but returning and reciting talbiyah within the Haram before Arafah waives it per Abu Hanifa.

Meccan Combining Umrah and Hajj: Which Ihram to Abandon?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on which ihram to annul when a Meccan combines Umrah and Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on which ihram a Meccan should abandon when combining Umrah and Hajj, and apply the preferred (mufta bihi) ruling.

Core Idea
When a Meccan combines both ihrams, he must abandon one; the preferred view is to abandon Umrah due to its lower rank and ease of makeup.

The chapter on Idafat al-Ihram addresses a unique case: a Meccan who, after initiating Umrah with one tawaf, also dons ihram for Hajj. Since combining both is not prescribed for a Meccan, he must annul one. This lesson examines the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two senior students on which ihram to drop and the consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal problem
A Meccan begins Umrah with one tawaf, then intends Hajj by donning a separate ihram. Combining both is a jinayah (transgression) for a Meccan, so one must be abandoned.
The act of adding one ihram to another is called Idafat al-Ihram.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the Meccan should abandon the Hajj ihram, pay a dam, and later perform a full Hajj and Umrah as qada.
He prioritizes the partially completed Umrah (one tawaf done).
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that it is better to abandon the Umrah ihram, pay a dam, and make up only the Umrah later.
They consider Umrah lower in rank and easier to make up.
4
Analyze the reasoning (talil) of each side
Abu Hanifa: Hajj ihram is abandoned because Umrah already started. Sahibayn: Umrah is less significant (fewer actions, no fixed time) so more suitable to drop.
Both agree a dam is wajib for the abandonment.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
Later Hanafi jurists preferred the Sahibayn's view due to ease. The ruling: abandon Umrah, pay dam, perform a separate Umrah later (qada).
The dam is wajib in either case.

مکی نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور ایک چکر طواف کیا پھر حج کا احرام باندھا ج چھوڑ دے اور اس کے چھوڑنے سے دم ہے اور ایک حج اور عمرہ لازم ہے

ترجمہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے کہا کہ اگر مکی نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور اس کا ایک شوط طواف کر لیا پھر حج کا احرام باندھا تو وہ حج کو ترک کر دے۔ اور اس پر حج ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک قربانی واجب ہو گی ۔ اور اس پر ایک حج و عمرہ واجب ہوگا اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ ہمارے نزد یک عمر و چھوڑنا بہتر ہے اور عمرہ کی قضا کرے اور عمرہ چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے اس پر دم لازم ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو چھوڑنا ضروری ہے اس لئے کہ مکی کے حق میں حج و عمرہ کو جمع کرنا مشروع نہیں ہے۔ اور چھوڑنے کے واسطے عمر ہ زیادہ لائق ہے کیونکہ عمرہ رتبہ میں کمتر ہے اور اعمال میں تھوڑا ہے اور قضاء کی راہ سے زیادہ آسان ہے۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کسی وقت کے ساتھ موقت نہیں ہے۔

Chapter on Adding the Ihram. Translation: This chapter is about adding ihram. A Meccan donned ihram for Umrah and performed one tawaf for it, then donned ihram for Hajj, so he should abandon it (the Hajj) and upon him for abandoning it is a dam, and upon him is a Hajj and an Umrah. Abu Hanifa said: When a Meccan dons ihram for Umrah and performs one tawaf for it, then dons ihram for Hajj, then he abandons the Hajj, and upon him for abandoning it is a dam, and upon him is a Hajj and an Umrah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Abandoning the Umrah is more beloved to us, and he should make it up, and upon him is a dam for abandoning it, because he must abandon one of them, for combining them in the case of a Meccan is not prescribed. And the Umrah is more deserving of being abandoned because it is lower in rank, fewer in actions, and easier to make up because it is not time-bound. Translation: Imam Abu Hanifa said that if a Meccan dons ihram for Umrah and performs one tawaf for it, then dons ihram for Hajj, then he should abandon the Hajj, and upon him for abandoning Hajj is one sacrifice wajib, and upon him is one Hajj and one Umrah wajib. And the Sahibayn said that in our view it is better to abandon the Umrah and make it up later, and upon him is a dam for abandoning it because it is necessary to abandon one of them because combining them in the case of the Meccan is not prescribed. And the Umrah is more suitable for abandonment because it is lower in rank, fewer in actions, and easier in terms of making up because it is not time-bound. Commentary: Combining the ihrams of Hajj and Umrah is not permissible for a Meccan; rather it is a transgression (jinayah) for him. Similarly, adding the ihram of Umrah to the ihram of Hajj is a transgression for an Afaaqi, but adding the ihram of Hajj to the ihram of Umrah is not a transgression for an Afaaqi. Since for the people of Makkah it is a transgression, it has been placed after the chapter on transgression. Issue: Imam Abu Hanifa said that if a Meccan dons ihram for Umrah and performs one tawaf for Umrah, then dons ihram for Hajj (i.e., intends the ihram of Hajj), then he should abandon the Hajj, and due to abandoning Hajj, a sacrifice becomes wajib, and upon him is a Hajj and an Umrah as qada. Note that this Umrah is not qada, rather there is an Umrah with every qada of Hajj. The Sahibayn said that the preferable action is to abandon the Umrah and make it up later, but due to abandoning the Umrah, a dam becomes wajib. Their proof is that it is necessary to abandon one of them because combining both is not prescribed for a Meccan. Therefore, to avoid committing what is not prescribed, abandoning one is necessary. And it is more virtuous to abandon the Umrah because it is lower in rank than Hajj, fewer in actions (only tawaf and sa'i), while Hajj has more actions, and it is easier to make up because Umrah is not time-bound; it is permissible throughout the year except for the two Eids and the days of Tashriq.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter 'Bab Idafat al-Ihram' concerning a Meccan who combines two ihrams in one journey. The primary dispute is between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The scenario: a Meccan first dons ihram for Umrah and performs one tawaf (shout). Then, before completing the Umrah, he intends and dons ihram for Hajj. Since for a Meccan, combining Hajj and Umrah ihrams in this manner is not prescribed (ghayru mashru'), he must abandon one of the two. Imam Abu Hanifa's position: he should abandon the Hajj ihram. He owes a dam (sacrificial animal) for abandoning the Hajj, and he is obligated to perform a complete Hajj and a complete Umrah (as qada). The Sahibayn's position: it is better to abandon the Umrah ihram, and he must make it up later (qada). He also owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah. Their reasoning: since combining both is not permitted, one must be dropped. Umrah is preferred to be dropped because: 1) it is lower in rank (adna halan) than Hajj, 2) it has fewer actions (only tawaf and sa'i), and 3) it is easier to make up because it has a fixed time (ghayr muwaqqatah) and can be performed anytime except for the prohibited days (Eid and Tashriq). The commentary explains that this act is considered a jinayah (transgression) for a Meccan, similar to an Afaaqi adding Umrah to Hajj, but not vice versa. Since it is a jinayah for Makki, the chapter is placed after the chapter on jinayat. The note clarifies that the Umrah performed as qada is not a separate qada; rather, every qada of Hajj includes an Umrah.

Key Terms
اضافہ الاحرام (Idafat al-Ihram): The act of adding one ihram to another before completing the first, specifically for a Meccan combining Umrah and Hajj.
رفض (Rafd): Abandoning or annulling an ihram that has already been initiated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi), what should a Meccan do if he dons ihram for Umrah, performs one tawaf, then dons ihram for Hajj?
A) Abandon the Hajj and perform a full Hajj and Umrah later
B) Abandon the Umrah and make it up later, with a dam
C) Continue both ihrams together
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a Meccan combines Umrah and Hajj ihrams, the preferred ruling is to abandon Umrah, pay a dam, and make it up later.

Ruling on a Meccan Combining Hajj and Umrah
Ruling on Meccan combining Hajj and Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a Meccan combining Hajj and Umrah, distinguish between dam jibr and dam shukr, and explain the Hanafi principle that prohibition does not nullify an act.

Core Idea
A Meccan's combining Hajj and Umrah is valid but sinful, requiring a compensatory dam; a non-Meccan's combination is a blessing requiring a thanksgiving dam.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a Meccan (resident within the Mīqāt) who performs both Hajj and Umrah under a single Ihrām. While the acts are validly performed, combining them is prohibited for the Meccan, and a blood sacrifice is required as compensation. The ruling highlights a key Hanafi usul principle: a prohibition (nahy) does not invalidate the act itself. The type of sacrifice differs between a Meccan and a non-Meccan (Afāqī), reflecting whether the act is a sin or a blessing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its overall ruling
The act is a Meccan combining Hajj and Umrah in one Ihrām. The ruling: it suffices (valid) but is prohibited and requires a dam.
Validity means the acts are discharged; prohibition means it is sinful.
2
Apply the Hanafi usul principle on prohibition
According to Hanafi principles, a prohibition (nahy) does not prevent the realization or validity of the act. Thus, the combination remains valid despite being prohibited.
This differs from other schools that may consider the act invalid due to the prohibition.
3
Differentiate between dam jibr and dam shukr
For a Meccan, the dam is dam jibr (compensatory) – he may not eat from it; it is given to the poor. For an Afāqī, the dam is dam shukr (thanksgiving) – he may eat from it.
The classification depends on whether the act is a sin (Meccan) or a blessing (non-Meccan).
4
Identify the reason for the difference
The Meccan is prohibited from combining, so his act incurs a deficiency requiring compensation. The Afāqī is not prohibited; combining is a blessing (since he enters the state of Ihrām once for both), so the dam is a thanksgiving.
The same physical act has different rulings based on the performer's status.

وَإِنْ مَضَى عَلَيْهِمَا أَجْزَاهُ لِأَنَّهُ أَدَّى أَفْعَالَهُمَا كَمَا الْتَزَمَهُمَا غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ مَنْهِيٌّ عَنْهُمَا وَالنَّهْيُ لَا يَمْنَعُ تَحَقُّقَ الْفِعْلِ عَلَى مَا عُرِفَ مِنْ أَصْلِنَا وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّهُ تَمَكَّنَ النَّقْصَانُ فِي عَمَلِهِ لِارْتِكَابِهِ الْمَنْهِيَّ عَنْهُ وَهَذَا فِي حَقِّ الْمَكِّيِّ دَمُ جَبْرٍ وَفِي حَقِّ الْآفَاقِيِّ دَمُ شُكْرٍ. ترجمہ: اور اگر مکی نے دونوں کو پورا کر لیا تو کافی ہے کیونکہ اس نے دونوں کے افعال کو جیسا کہ ان دونوں کا التزام کیا تھا ادا کر لیا مگر یہ کہ ان دونوں کو جمع کرنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے اور نہی تحقق فعل سے مانع نہیں ہے جیسا کہ ہمارا اصول معلوم ہے البتہ اس پر ایک قربانی لازم ہے کیونکہ اس نے ان دونوں کو جمع کیا ہے کیونکہ اس کے منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کے عمل میں نقصان پیدا ہو گیا ہے اور یہ مکی کے حق میں دم جبر ہے اور آفاقی کے حق میں دم شکر ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکی نے حج یا عمرہ کو ترک نہیں کیا بلکہ دونوں کو ادا کر دیا تو دونوں ادا ہو گئے کیونکہ اس نے دونوں کے افعال کو جس طرح اپنے اوپر لازم کیا تھا اسی طرح ادا کر لیا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ہے کہ مکی کو احرام حج اور احرام عمرہ جمع کرنے سے منع کیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن نہی تحقق فعل کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی۔ جیسا کہ اصول فقہ میں مذکور ہے۔ البتہ اس پر مذکور ہے۔ البتہ اس کے محرم پر دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کے عمل میں نقصان پیدا ہو گیا ہے۔ اور نقصان اس لئے پیدا ہوا کہ اس نے فعل منہی عنہ کا ارتکاب کیا ہے۔ یہ دم مکی کے حق میں دم جبر ہے یعنی نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے ہے لہذا اس میں سے خود اس کا کھانا جائز نہیں ہے یہ تو فقراء کا حق ہے اور آفاقی کے حق میں دم شکر ہے چنانچہ اس میں سے اس کا کھانا جائز ہے۔ یہ عجیب بات ہے کہ حج وعمرہ کو اگر مکی جمع کرتا ہے تو معصیت ہے اور اگر آفاقی جمع کرتا ہے تو نعمت ہے۔ قربانی دونوں پر واجب ہوتی ہے مگر مکی پر واجب ہوئی پیدا شدہ نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے اور آفاقی پر واجب ہوئی شکران نعمت کے طور پر۔ اللہ اللہ ایک ہی چیز ایک کے حق میں معصیت ہے اور ایک کے حق میں نعمت ہے۔
And if he performed both (Hajj and Umrah), it suffices him because he performed their acts as he obligated himself to them, except that he is prohibited from combining them, and prohibition does not prevent the realization of the act as is known from our principle. And upon him is a dam for combining them because deficiency occurred in his act due to his commission of the prohibited. And this in the right of the Meccan is a dam of jibr (compensation), and in the right of the non-Meccan (Afāqī) is a dam of shukr (thanksgiving).
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about a Meccan who combines Hajj and Umrah in one Ihrām. The matn states that if he performs both, it suffices (ajzā), meaning both are validly performed. The proof: he has fulfilled the acts as he obligated himself. However, combining them is prohibited for a Meccan. According to Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) does not nullify the validity of the act itself—it remains valid but sinful. Therefore, he owes a dam (blood sacrifice) as a compensation for the deficiency caused by committing the prohibited act. The dam differs: for a Meccan (one residing within the Mīqāt), it is dam jibr—compensatory, and he may not eat from it; it is given to the poor. For an Afāqī (one from outside the Mīqāt), it is dam shukr—a thanksgiving sacrifice, and he may eat from it. The commentary explains that the same act is a sin for a Meccan but a blessing for an Afāqī, because the Meccan is prohibited from combining, while the Afāqī is not.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jibr): A compensatory blood sacrifice required from a Meccan for combining Hajj and Umrah, symbolizing reparation for the deficiency caused by the prohibited act.
دم شكر (dam shukr): A thanksgiving blood sacrifice required from a non-Meccan (Afāqī) for combining Hajj and Umrah, which may be eaten by the offerer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of dam is required from a Meccan who combines Hajj and Umrah?
A) Dam shukr
B) Dam jibr
C) No dam
D) Dam of tarkhīs

Key Takeaway
A Meccan's combination of Hajj and Umrah is valid but sinful, requiring a compensatory dam jibr; the Afāqī's combination is a blessing requiring dam shukr.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Second Hajj Ihram on Yawm al-Nahr: Validity and Dam Obligation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam obligation for combined Hajj Ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on the validity and dam obligation when a person enters a second Hajj Ihram on Yawm al-Nahr without having shaved from the first, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A second Ihram on Yawm al-Nahr is valid but may require a dam; Abu Hanifa always requires it, the Sahibayn only if hair is cut.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in Hajj: a person who, while still in Ihram for one Hajj, enters a second Ihram on the Day of Sacrifice for the following year. The ruling hinges on whether he has already performed the exit ritual (halq/taqsir) from the first. We will explore the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and see how their different starting points lead to different practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Recall that the case involves a person already in Ihram for Hajj who, on Yawm al-Nahr, enters a second Ihram for another Hajj intended for the next year.
The second Ihram is valid and binding in all scenarios according to the text.
2
Identify the two situations based on prior halq
Distinguish whether the person has performed halq (shaving) from the first Ihram before entering the second. If yes, no dam; if no, then a dam is disputed.
Halq from the first Ihram is the exit ritual that allows the second Ihram to be separate.
3
Contrast Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on the dam requirement
When no prior halq, Abu Hanifa holds that a dam is obligatory regardless of whether he later performs taqsir (trimming) or not. The Sahibayn hold that a dam is only obligatory if he performs taqsir after the second Ihram.
Both agree that if he performs halq before the second Ihram, no dam is due.
4
Trace the reasoning
Analyze the principle that combining two Hajj Ihrams is a bid'ah. Abu Hanifa sees any hair removal (halq or taqsir) after the second Ihram as an aggression because it is untimely. The Sahibayn see the bid'ah as not fully realized without taqsir, so no penalty without it.
The delay of halq from the first Ihram also factors in: Abu Hanifa penalizes the delay itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, if the pilgrim does not perform taqsir after the second Ihram, Abu Hanifa says a dam is due, Sahibayn say no dam. If taqsir is performed, both require a dam.
The difference only appears when no hair removal occurs after the second Ihram.

وَ مَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ بِحَجَّةٍ أُخْرَى فَإِنْ حَلَقَ فِي الْأُولَى لَزِمَتْهُ الْأُخْرَى وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلِقْ فِي الْأُولَى لَزِمَتْهُ الْأُخْرَى وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ قَصَّرَ أَوْ لَمْ يُقَصِّرْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا إِنْ لَمْ يُقَصِّرْ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ بَيْنَ إِحْرَامَيِ الْحَجِّ أَوْ إِحْرَامَيِ الْعُمْرَةِ بِدْعَةٌ فَإِذَا حَلَقَ فَهُوَ وَإِنْ كَانَ نُسُكًا فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْأَوَّلِ فَهُوَ جِنَايَةٌ عَلَى الثَّانِي لِأَنَّهُ فِي غَيْرِ أَوَانِهِ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلِقْ حَتَّى حَجَّ فِي الْعَامِ الْقَابِلِ فَقَدْ أَخَّرَ الْحَلْقَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْأَوَّلِ وَذَلِكَ يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٌ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَلِهَذَا سَوَّى بَيْنَ التَّقْصِيرِ وَعَدَمِهِ عِنْدَهُ وَشَرَطَ التَّقْصِيرَ عِنْدَهُمَا. ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے حج کا احرام باندھا پھر دسویں ذی الحجہ میں دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا پس اگر پہلے حج میں حلق کر لیا ہو تو دوسرا حج لازم ہو گا اور اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر پہلے حج میں حلق نہیں کیا تب بھی دوسرا حج لازم ہوگا اور اس پر ایک قربانی واجب ہے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کترائے یا نہ کترائے۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اگر قصر نہیں کیا تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ حج کے دو احرام اور عمرہ کے دو احرام جمع کرنا بدعت ہے۔ پھر جب اس نے حلق کیا تو وہ اگر چہ احرام اول میں نسک ہے لیکن احترام ثانی پر جنایت ہے کیونکہ یہ حلق اس کے وقت کے علاوہ میں ہے اس لئے اس پر بالاجماع دم لازم ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے حلق نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ آئندہ سال حج دوم کیا تو حلق احترام اول میں اپنے وقت سے مؤخر ہو گیا اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ بھی دم واجب کرتا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تاخیر سے کچھ لازم نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ ہم نے ذکر کر دیا ہے۔ پس اسی اصل کی وجہ سے امام صاحب کے نزدیک منڈوانے اور نہ منڈانے میں یکساں حکم کیا گیا ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک قصر کرنا شرط کیا گیا ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ، اگر کسی شخص نے حج کا احرام باندھا پھر دسویں ذی الحجہ کو آئندہ سال کے لئے دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھ لیا۔ اب اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں کیونکہ دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھنے سے پہلے حج اول سے نکلنے کے لئے حلق کیا ہے یا نہیں۔ اگر پہلے حج سے نکلنے کے لئے حلق کیا پھر یوم نحر کو دوسرے سال کے لئے حج کا احرام باندھا تو اس پر دوسرا حج لازم ہوگا اور یہ دوسرا حج آئندہ سال کرے اس وقت تک محرم رہے گا اور اس پر دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے دو احرام جمع نہیں کئے بلکہ حلق کے ذریعہ پہلے احرام سے نکل گیا تھا حالانکہ دو احرام جمع کرنا ہی بدعت ہے۔ پس جب اس نے بدعت کا ارتکاب نہیں کیا تو اس پر دم جنایت بھی واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر دوسرے احترام سے پہلے اپنے پہلے حج سے نکلنے کے لئے حلق نہیں کیا تو اس پر دوسرا حج لازم ہوگا اور اس پر دم واجب ہوگا خواہ دوسرے حج کے احرام کے بعد حلق کرے یا حلق نہ کرے۔ یہ امام صاحب کا مذہب ہے اور صاحبین کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اگر دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد حلق نہیں کیا تو اس پر دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔ دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حج کے دو احرام یا عمرہ کے دو احرام جمع کرنا بالاتفاق بدعت ہے۔ پس اب دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھنے کے بعد اگر حلق کیا تو احرام اول سے نکلنے کے لئے اگر چہ حج کا ایک فعل ہے لیکن دوسرے احرام پر جنایت ہے کیونکہ یہ حلق دوسرے حج کے اعمال پورے ہونے سے پہلے ہوا یعنی بے وقت ہوا۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ قبل از وقت سر منڈانا موجب دم ہوتا ہے۔
And whoever enters into Ihram for Hajj, then on Yawm al-Nahr enters into Ihram for another Hajj: if he shaved (halq) in the first, the second is binding upon him and there is nothing upon him. And if he did not shave in the first, the second is binding upon him and upon him is a dam, whether he trimmed (qassara) or not, according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Sahibayn) said: if he did not trim, then nothing is upon him because the combination of two Ihrāms for Hajj or two Ihrāms for Umrah is an innovation (bid'ah). Then when he shaved, even though it is a rite (nusuk) in the first Ihram, it is an aggression upon the second because it is at other than its proper time, so the dam is obligatory by consensus. And if he did not shave until he performed Hajj in the following year, then he delayed the shaving from its time in the first Ihram, and that necessitates a dam according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (the Sahibayn), nothing becomes obligatory upon him, as we have mentioned. Therefore, he (Abu Hanifa) equated between trimming and not trimming, while they made trimming a condition.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a person who enters Ihrām for Hajj and then on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) enters a second Ihrām for another Hajj intended for the following year. The matn states two scenarios: (1) If he has already performed halq (shaving) from the first Hajj before entering the second, then the second Hajj is valid and binding, and no dam is required. (2) If he has not shaved from the first, the second Hajj is still binding, but a dam is required. Abu Hanifa holds that a dam is required regardless of whether he later trims (qassara) or not. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if he does not trim (i.e., perform any hair removal) from the second Ihram, no dam is owed. The reasoning: Combining two Ihrāms for Hajj or for Umrah is a bid'ah. If he shaves (halq) from the first before the second, it is a valid act for the first but becomes an aggression on the second because it is performed at an improper time (i.e., before the second's own halq time). Hence, a dam is obligatory by consensus. If he delays shaving until after performing the second Hajj the following year, Abu Hanifa says the delay itself necessitates a dam, while the Sahibayn say it does not. The commentary explains the two scenarios in detail: if he shaved before the second Ihram, no dam; if not, the second Ihram is binding and there is disagreement on the dam if he does not cut hair for the second.

Key Terms
إحرام الحج (ihrām al-hajj): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj, which involves intention and wearing of specific garments.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, one of the exit rituals from Ihrām.
قصر (qasr/taqsir): Trimming the hair (not shaving completely), also a valid way to exit Ihrām.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when is a dam obligatory on a person who enters a second Hajj Ihrām on Yawm al-Nahr without having shaved from the first?
A) Only if he performs taqsir
B) In all cases, whether he trims or not
C) Only if he does not perform taqsir
D) No dam is obligatory

Key Takeaway
The second Hajj Ihrām on Yawm al-Nahr is valid, but the obligation of a dam depends on prior halq and, according to the Sahibayn, on subsequent taqsir.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Dam for Second Hajj Ihram on Yawm al-Nahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dam obligation for combined ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the obligation of dam when a second Hajj ihram is entered on Yawm al-Nahr without cutting hair, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Combining two Hajj ihrams is a bid'ah; the ikhtilaf is whether delaying the first's hair-cutting itself necessitates a dam.

This passage presents a case where someone, already in ihram for Hajj, enters a second ihram on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) for the following year. While the second ihram is binding, the scholars differ on whether a dam (sacrificial compensation) is wajib if the person does not cut his hair after the second ihram. Abu Hanifa holds that a dam is always wajib in this scenario, while the Sahibayn condition the dam on cutting hair after the second ihram. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school handles ritual violations (jinayat) and the role of time in determining compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage to understand the scenario: a person already in ihram for Hajj enters a second ihram on Yawm al-Nahr. Note that combining two Hajj (or Umrah) ihrams is considered a bid'ah.
2
State the agreed ruling
If the person shaves (halq) or trims (taqsir) after the second ihram, all agree a dam is due because the act, though intended for the first ihram, is performed out of its proper time for the second and thus constitutes an offense.
The text says 'بِالْإِجْمَاعِ' (by consensus).
3
Isolate the ikhtilaf
The dispute arises when the person does NOT cut hair after the second ihram. Identify the positions: Abu Hanifa says a dam is wajib; the Sahibayn say no dam is due.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa considers the delay of the first ihram's hair-cutting until the following year itself a violation (jinayah) that requires a dam, regardless of whether hair is cut after the second ihram.
Key phrase: 'فَقَدْ أَخَّرَ الْحَلْقَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْأَوَّلِ وَذَلِكَ يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ'.
5
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn hold that no violation occurs unless the hair-cutting is actually performed after the second ihram, because only then is it out of time for the second ihram. Merely delaying the first ihram's hair-cutting without performing it is not a dam-worthy offense.
They condition the dam on taqsir (hair-cutting) after the second ihram.
6
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: In practice, if a pilgrim enters a second Hajj ihram on Yawm al-Nahr and does not cut hair, Abu Hanifa requires a dam; the Sahibayn do not. A mufti must know which position to follow based on the preferred view in the school.
The text does not specify the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ بِحَجَّةٍ أُخْرَى فَإِنْ حَلَقَ فِي الْأُولَى لَزِمَتْهُ الْأُخْرَى وَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلِقْ فِي الْأُولَى لَزِمَتْهُ الْأُخْرَى وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ قَصَّرَ أَوْ لَمْ يَقَصِّرْ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا إِنْ لَمْ يَقَصِّرْ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ بَيْنَ إِحْرَامَيِ الْحَجِّ أَوْ إِحْرَامَيِ الْعُمْرَةِ بِدْعَةٌ فَإِذَا حَلَقَ فَهُوَ إِنْ كَانَ نُسُكًا فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْأَوَّلِ فَهُوَ جِنَايَةٌ عَلَى الثَّانِي لِأَنَّهُ فِي غَيْرِ أَوَانِهِ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْلِقْ حَتَّى حَجَّ فِي الْعَامِ الْقَابِلِ فَقَدْ أَخَّرَ الْحَلْقَ عَنْ وَقْتِهِ فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْأَوَّلِ وَذَلِكَ يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٌ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا فَلِهَذَا سَوَّى بَيْنَ التَّقْصِيرِ وَعَدَمِهِ عِنْدَهُ وَشَرَطَ التَّقْصِيرَ عِنْدَهُمَا
And whoever enters ihram for Hajj, then on Yawm al-Nahr enters ihram for another Hajj: if he shaved his head in the first, the second becomes binding upon him and nothing is due from him. But if he did not shave in the first, the second becomes binding upon him and a dam is due from him, whether he trimmed his hair or did not trim, according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If he did not trim, then nothing is due from him, because combining two ihrams for Hajj or two ihrams for Umrah is a bid'ah. When he shaved, although it is a ritual act in the first ihram, it is an offense against the second because it is out of its time. So by consensus a dam is due. If he did not shave until he performed Hajj the following year, then he delayed the shaving from its time for the first ihram, and that necessitates a dam according to Abu Hanifa. According to them, nothing is due as we mentioned. Therefore, he (Abu Hanifa) equated between trimming and not trimming, and they conditioned trimming.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who enters ihram for Hajj and then, on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul-Hijjah), enters a second ihram for Hajj for the following year. The ruling is divided based on whether the person has completed the first Hajj by shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir). Abu Hanifa holds that regardless of whether one trims after the second ihram, a dam is wajib. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that if one does not trim after the second ihram, no dam is due. The reasoning: combining two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams is a bid'ah. If one shaves after the second ihram, that shave is a ritual act for the first ihram but an offense against the second because it occurs before its proper time (since the second Hajj is for the next year). On this point, both sides agree a dam is due. The ikhtilaf arises when one delays shaving until the following year; Abu Hanifa considers this delay itself a dam-worthy offense, while the Sahibayn do not. Hence, Abu Hanifa makes no distinction between trimming and not trimming—both require a dam—while the Sahibayn make trimming (after the second ihram) a condition for the dam.

Key Terms
إحرام (ihram): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, initiated by the intention and recitation of talbiyah.
دم (dam): A ritual sacrifice (damm) wajib as compensation for a violation (jinayah) in Hajj or Umrah.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, a required act for exiting ihram after completing Hajj or Umrah.
تقصير (taqsir): Trimming the hair, an alternative to shaving for exiting ihram.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religious matters; here, combining two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams is considered a blameworthy innovation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a person enters a second Hajj ihram on Yawm al-Nahr and does not cut hair after it?
A) The second Hajj is invalid and no dam is due.
B) The second Hajj is binding and a dam is wajib.
C) The second Hajj is binding only if hair is cut.
D) No ruling due to ikhtilaf.

Key Takeaway
When a second Hajj ihram is entered on Yawm al-Nahr without cutting hair, Abu Hanifa imposes a dam for the delay, while the Sahibayn require no dam unless hair is cut after the second ihram.

Ruling on Entering a Second Umrah Ihram Before Completing the First
States ruling on second Umrah ihram before completing first

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and conditions under which a dam becomes wajib when entering a second Umrah ihram before completing the first.

Core Idea
If one completes all Umrah acts except taqsir and enters a second ihram, a dam is wajib.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Umrah where a person, having almost completed the first Umrah but not yet performed the final hair-cutting (taqsir), enters into a second Umrah ihram. The Hanafi school rules that this act is makruh and necessitates a compensating sacrifice (dam). Let us break down the precise ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act described
The act is entering ihram for a second Umrah after completing all rites of the first Umrah except for the taqsir (hair-cutting).
The first Umrah is not fully exited until taqsir is performed; until then, one remains in the state of ihram.
2
Determine the ruling on the act
The text states that this act is makruh (disliked) because it combines two Umrah ihrams without a valid interval.
In Hanafi fiqh, makruh that necessitates a dam is considered makruh tahrimi.
3
Identify the legal consequence
Because the act is makruh and invalidates the proper separation of Umrahs, a dam (sacrifice) is wajib as compensation (jabr) and expiation (kaffarah).
The dam is due 'because he entered ihram before the time' – i.e., before the first Umrah was officially completed.
4
Understand the type of dam
This is a dam jabr (compensatory sacrifice), distinct from dam shukr (thanksgiving). It remedies the deficiency in performing the second Umrah prematurely.
The dam is to be offered in the Haram (Makkah) and distributed to the poor.
5
Apply the ruling to practical cases
If the pilgrim performs taqsir of the first Umrah before entering the second ihram, no dam is required. The condition is the omission of taqsir only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ فَرَغَ مِنْ عُمْرَتِهِ إِلَّا التَّقْصِيرَ فَأَحْرَمَ بِأُخْرَى فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِإِحْرَامِهِ قَبْلَ الْوَقْتِ لِأَنَّهُ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ إِحْرَامَيِ الْعُمْرَةِ وَهَذَا مَكْرُوهٌ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ وَهُوَ دَمُ جَبْرٍ وَكَفَّارَةٌ
And whoever finishes his Umrah except for the taqsir, then enters ihram for another, then a dam is due from him because he entered ihram before the time, as he combined two ihrams for Umrah. This is makruh, so a dam is necessary for him, and it is a dam of compensation and expiation.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This is a clear ruling: one who completes all the acts of Umrah except for the final hair-cutting (taqsir) and then enters ihram for a second Umrah has committed a makruh act by combining two Umrah ihrams. Since the first Umrah is not yet fully exited (because taqsir remains), entering the second ihram is premature. Therefore, a dam is wajib as jahr (compensation) and kaffarah (expiation). This dam is obligatory according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory sacrifice offered to remedy a deficiency or violation in Hajj/Umrah.
تقصير (taqsir): The act of shortening or trimming the hair as the final step of Umrah to exit ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When someone performs two Umrahs in one journey.
B) When someone enters a second Umrah ihram after completing the first except for taqsir.
C) When someone delays taqsir for more than a day.
D) When someone combines Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway
If a person completes all Umrah acts except the final tahallul (hair-cutting) and enters ihram for another Umrah, a compensatory dam is wajib.

Ruling on Afaqi Combining Hajj and Umrah Ihrams
States ruling on Afaqi combining Hajj and Umrah ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an Afaqi who enters ihram for Hajj then Umrah, explain why he becomes a Qarin but is sinful, and apply the condition that standing at Arafat without Umrah acts constitutes abandonment.

Core Idea
Entering Umrah after Hajj ihram is binding but sinful; after Arafat, Umrah is abandoned.

The Hajj and Umrah have prescribed sequences. When an Afaqi (one from outside the Miqat) first enters ihram for Hajj and then later for Umrah, a unique situation arises. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that both ihrams are binding, but the order violates the Sunnah, incurring sin. It also addresses the critical moment when the Umrah becomes impossible due to standing at Arafat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actor and His Actions
Recognize that the ruling concerns an Afaqi (a person from beyond the Miqat). He first enters ihram for Hajj (by pronouncing the talbiyah), then later enters a second ihram for Umrah before completing Hajj.
The Sunnah for an Afaqi is to perform Umrah first, then Hajj (Tamattu') or to enter both simultaneously (Qiran).
2
Determine Legal Consequences: Binding, Qarin, Error
Both Hajj and Umrah become binding (lazimah) because combining them is prescribed for the Afaqi. He becomes a Qarin (one performing both together). However, he has erred from the Sunnah by reversing the order, making him a wrongdoer (musi'). The acts themselves are valid but sinful in method.
This is a case of ikhtilaf: the Hanafi school deems the order a sin, while others may not.
3
Analyze the Case of Standing at Arafat without Umrah Acts
If the pilgrim proceeds to stand at Arafat (the main Hajj ritual) without having performed the Umrah acts (tawaf, sa'y), then the Umrah becomes impossible because its time has passed. He is considered to have abandoned (rafid) the Umrah.
Abandoning an obligatory Umrah generally requires a dam (sacrificial penalty), though not mentioned here explicitly.
4
Note the Condition for Abandonment
The passage clarifies that merely traveling towards Arafat does not constitute abandonment; one becomes an abandoner only after actually standing at Arafat. Until then, he could still perform Umrah.
This nuance prevents premature ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَهَلَّ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمْرَةٍ لَزِمَاهُ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَشْرُوعٌ فِي حَقِّ الْآفَاقِيِّ وَالْمَسْأَلَةُ فِيهِ فَيَصِيرُ بِذَلِكَ قَارِنًا لَكِنَّهُ أَخْطَأَ السُّنَّةَ فَيَصِيرُ مُسِيئًا فَلَوْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَاتٍ وَلَمْ يَأْتِ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ فَهُوَ رَافِضُ الْعُمْرَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَدَاؤُهَا إِذْ هِيَ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى الْحَجِّ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعَةٍ فَإِنْ تَوَجَّهَ إِلَيْهَا لَمْ يَكُنْ رَافِضًا حَتَّىٰ يَقِفَ وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ
And whoever pronounces the talbiyah for Hajj, then enters ihram for Umrah, both are binding upon him, because combining them is prescribed for the Afaqi, and the issue applies to him. Thus he becomes a Qarin thereby, but he has erred from the Sunnah, so he becomes a wrongdoer. If he stands at Arafat without performing the acts of Umrah, then he is one who abandons his Umrah, because its performance becomes impossible for him, since it is built upon Hajj and is not prescribed. If he sets out towards it (Hajj), he is not considered an abandoner until he stands (at Arafat), and we have mentioned this before.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage addresses an Afaqi (a person from outside the Miqat boundaries) who first enters ihram for Hajj and later, before completing Hajj, enters ihram for Umrah. The ruling: both are binding – he becomes a Qarin (performer of Hajj and Umrah in one state of ihram). However, since the correct Sunnah for an Afaqi is to enter ihram for Umrah first and then for Hajj (Tamattu' or Qiran in proper order), doing Hajj first then Umrah is an error and he is considered sinful (musi'). If he proceeds to stand at Arafat without having performed the Umrah acts (tawaf, sa'y), then the Umrah becomes impossible because the time for its acts has passed, and he is considered to have abandoned (rafid) the Umrah. If he goes towards Arafat intending to perform Umrah later, he is not an abandoner until he actually stands at Arafat. This is based on the principle that Umrah acts are built upon Hajj and not prescribed after standing at Arafat.

Key Terms
آفاقي (afaqi): A person who resides outside the Miqat boundaries (i.e., beyond the appointed stations for ihram).
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single state of ihram, entering with the intention of both.
رافض (rafid): One who abandons his Umrah; here, due to impossibility of performing its acts after standing at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both are valid and he completes Umrah after Hajj.
B) He must perform Umrah after Hajj with a dam.
C) He is considered to have abandoned Umrah.
D) The Umrah ihram is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
For an Afaqi, entering Umrah after Hajj ihram is binding but sinful; standing at Arafat without Umrah acts results in abandonment of the Umrah.

Ruling on Combining Two Umrahs: Dam Required
States a ruling on combining two Umrahs without completing the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two Umrahs without completing the first, and identify the type of dam required as wajib.

Core Idea
Combining two Umrahs before completing the first is makruh and requires a dam of compensation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a person completes all acts of Umrah except the final taqsir (hair shortening) and then enters a second Umrah. The act is considered makruh, and a sacrificial dam becomes wajib. The reasoning is that the second ihram was entered before the permissible time, effectively combining two ihrams without completing the first. The dam is classified as dam jabr (compensatory) and kaffarah (expiation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its deficiency
The person has finished all Umrah rituals except the taqsir, meaning they have not fully exited ihram. Then they enter a new Umrah.
Taqsir is the final act that ends the ihram for Umrah.
2
Determine the ruling on the act
The text states that this act (combining two ihrams without completing the first) is makruh (disliked).
Makruh here likely means makruh tanzihi, but still triggers a wajib compensation.
3
Identify the consequence
Because it is makruh, a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib upon the person.
4
Understand the reason for the dam
The dam is due to entering the second ihram before the proper time (waqt) – i.e., before the first Umrah is completely finished.
Combining two ihrams is the cause of the makruh and the dam.
5
Classify the dam
The dam is a dam jabr (compensatory) and also kaffarah (expiation), not a dam of thanks.
This distinguishes it from voluntary sacrifices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ فَرَغَ مِنْ عُمَرَتِهِ إِلَّا التَّقْصِيرَ فَأَحْرَمَ بِأُخْرَى فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِإِحْرَامِهِ قَبْلَ الْوَقْتِ لِأَنَّهُ جَمَعَ بَيْنَ إِحْرَامَيِ الْعُمْرَةِ وَهذَا مَكْرُوهٌ فَيَلْزَمُهُ الدَّمُ وَهُوَ دَمُ جَبْرٍ وَكَفَّارَةٍ
And whoever finishes his Umrah except the shortening (of hair) and then enters into another Umrah, then a dam is due upon him because of his ihram before the time, for he has combined two ihrams of Umrah, and this is makruh, so the dam becomes obligatory upon him, and it is a dam of compensation and expiation.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi matn. It states that if a person performs Umrah but does not complete it by shortening or shaving the hair (i.e., does not exit ihram fully), and then enters into another Umrah, it is makruh because it combines two Umrah ihrams. As a consequence, a dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib. This dam is classified as dam jabr (compensatory) and kaffarah (expiation), not a dam of thanks. The ruling applies because the second ihram was entered before the proper time for the first Umrah had ended.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory sacrifice required to make up for a deficiency or violation in the rituals.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked but not forbidden; in this context, it triggers a wajib dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Tawaf al-Qudum Then Umrah: Dam for Combining
Ruling on one who performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj then enters Umrah and performs both.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an Afaqi performs Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj then enters Umrah, and identify the type of dam required.

Core Idea
Performing Tawaf al-Qudum (sunnah) before Umrah makes the combination valid but requires a dam of expiation and compensation.

In this passage, we encounter a pilgrim who arrives in Makkah for Hajj and performs the greeting tawaf (Tawaf al-Qudum) as a sunnah. Later, he decides to perform Umrah before Hajj. The text clarifies the legal status of this action: the combination is valid, but a compensatory sacrifice (dam) is required because he performed a Hajj-related act before Umrah, reversing the preferred order. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Hanafi approach to sequence in Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial act
Recognize that the tawaf performed is Tawaf al-Tahiyyah (greeting tawaf), which is sunnah for the one intending Hajj. Confirm its legal status (sunnah, not rukn or wajib).
Tawaf al-Tahiyyah is also known as Tawaf al-Qudum.
2
Determine the sequence
The pilgrim performed this sunnah act of Hajj before entering into Umrah. Note that this reverses the recommended sunnah order where Umrah should precede Hajj acts.
3
Assess validity of the combination
Because combining Hajj and Umrah is legislated for the Afaqi, the ihram for both is valid. The earlier tawaf does not invalidate the Umrah since it is not a pillar.
The passage states 'fa-sahha al-ihramu bihima'.
4
Identify the required compensation
The text imposes a dam for combining them in this manner. This dam is not a thanksgiving sacrifice but a compensatory expiation (dam kaffarah wa jabr).
The phrase 'huwa al-sahih' indicates the relied-upon view.
5
Explain the rationale
The dam is due because the pilgrim 'built the acts of Umrah upon the acts of Hajj in one respect'—the Umrah acts follow a Hajj act, even though the combination is valid.
The rationale is that the order was partially reversed, necessitating compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ طَافَ لِلْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَةٍ فَمَضَى عَلَيْهِمَا أَيْ أَدَّاهُمَا وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَشْرُوعٌ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ فَصَحَّ الْإِحْرَامُ بِهِمَا وَالْمُرَادُ بِهَذَا الطَّوَافِ طَوَافُ التَّحِيَّةِ وَإِنَّهُ سُنَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِرُكْنٍ حَتَّى لَا يَلْزَمُهُ بِتَرْكِهِ شَيْءٌ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَأْتِ بِمَا هُوَ رُكْنٌ يُمْكِنُهُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ ثُمَّ بِأَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ فَلِهَذَا لَوْ مَضَى عَلَيْهِمَا جَازَ وَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَهُوَ دَمُ كَفَّارَةٍ وَجَبْرٍ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّهُ بَنَى أَفْعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ مِنْ وَجْهٍ
For if he performs tawaf for Hajj then enters into Umrah and then performs both (i.e., completes them), then a dam is due upon him for combining them, because combining them is legislated as previously mentioned, so the ihram for both is valid. By this tawaf is meant Tawaf al-Tahiyyah (greeting tawaf), and it is sunnah, not a pillar, so nothing is incumbent upon him for leaving it. And when he has not performed what is a pillar, it is possible for him to perform the acts of Umrah then the acts of Hajj. Therefore, if he performs both, it is valid, and a dam is due upon him for combining them, and it is a dam of expiation and compensation; this is the correct view, because he has built the acts of Umrah upon the acts of Hajj in one respect.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where an Afaqi performs the Tawaf al-Qudum (greeting tawaf) for Hajj, which is a sunnah act, and then enters into Umrah, subsequently performing both Hajj and Umrah. The ruling is that the combination is valid because combining Hajj and Umrah is legislated for the Afaqi. However, since he performed a Hajj act (tawaf) before Umrah, he has reversed the sunnah order. Therefore, a dam is wajib as compensation (dam kaffarah wa jabr). The dam is not a dam shukr (thanksgiving) because he has built the Umrah acts on the Hajj acts in a sense. The key is that Tawaf al-Qudum is not a pillar (rukn), so it does not prevent the sequence; but because it is a sunnah act of Hajj performed before Umrah, the combination is considered imperfect and requires a compensatory dam.

Key Terms
طواف التحية (tawaf al-tahiyyah): The greeting tawaf performed upon entering Makkah; it is sunnah for the one intending Hajj.
دم كفارة وجبر (dam kaffarah wa jabr): A sacrificial animal that serves both as expiation (kaffarah) and compensation (jabr) for a ritual deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of performing Tawaf al-Qudum for Hajj then entering Umrah and performing both, what is the nature of the required dam?
A) Dam shukr (thanksgiving) because the person succeeded in performing both.
B) Dam of expiation and compensation (kaffarah wa jabr), because he built Umrah acts on Hajj acts.
C) No dam is required because the combination is allowed.
D) Dam for violating a pillar, since Tawaf al-Qudum is a rukn.

Key Takeaway
Performing Tawaf al-Qudum (sunnah) before Umrah makes the combination valid but requires a dam of expiation and compensation.

Ruling on Performing Hajj Tawaf Then Umrah Ihram
Explains ruling when Hajj tawaf is performed before Umrah ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a pilgrim performs tawaf al-qudum for Hajj before entering ihram for Umrah, and explain why a dam is wajib.

Core Idea
Performing sunnah Hajj tawaf before Umrah does not invalidate Umrah but requires a dam as compensation.

This lesson examines a scenario where a pilgrim performs the sunnah tawaf al-qudum upon arrival for Hajj and then enters ihram for Umrah. The Hanafi school holds that both acts are valid and binding, but a dam is wajib because the actions of Umrah become based on the actions of Hajj, creating a disliked combination. Understanding the distinction between sunnah and rukn is key to grasping the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its status
The act is tawaf al-qudum, which is sunnah, not a rukn of Hajj. Its omission does not incur any penalty.
This distinction is crucial for the ruling.
2
Determine the legal consequence of performing sunnah before Umrah ihram
Since no rukn has been performed, it remains possible to perform Umrah actions first and then Hajj actions.
The order is valid but disliked.
3
Understand the basis (talil) for the dam
The actions of Umrah are 'built upon' the actions of Hajj (because tawaf al-qudum is already a Hajj act), so combining them in this order requires compensation.
The dam is of expiation and compensation, not of thanks.
4
Conclude the ruling
Both Hajj and Umrah are valid and binding, but a dam is wajib for the disliked combination.
No additional penalty if both are completed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ طَافَ لِلْحَقِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَةٍ فَمَضَى عَلَيْهِمَا إِرَمَاهُ وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمْ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ بَيْنَهُمَا مَشْرُوع عَلى مَا مَرَ فَصَحَ الْإِحْرَامُ بِهِمَا وَالْمُرَادُ بِهَذَا الطَّوَافِ طَوَافُ التَّحِيَّةِ وَإِنَّهُ سُنَةٌ وَ لَيْسَ يُركَنِ حَتَّى لَا يَلْزِمُهُ بشركه شَئ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَأْتِ بِمَا هُوَ رُكُنَّ يُمْكِنُهُ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمَرَةِ ثُمَّ بِافْعَالَ الْحَجِّ فَلِهَذَا لَوْ مَضَى عَلَيْهِمَا جَازَ وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمَّ لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا وَهُوَ دَمُ كَفَّارَةٍ وَجَبْرٍ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّهَ بَانَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَقِّ مِنْ وَجْهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر طواف قدوم حج کے لئے کیا پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا پھر ان دونوں کو کر گزرا تو اس پر دونوں لازم ہوں گے ۔ اور اس پر دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہے کیونکہ ان دونوں کا جمع کرنا مشروع ہے اس بنا پر جو گذرا پس دونوں کا احرام صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور اس طواف سے مراد طواف قدوم ہے اور یہ سنت ہے رکن نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کے ترک سے کچھ لا زم ہو۔ اور جب اس نے ایسا فعل نہیں کیا جو رکن ہو تو اس کے لئے ممکن ہے کہ وہ افعال عمرہ ادا کرے پھر افعال حج ادا کرے۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر ان دونوں کو کر گذرا تو جائز ہے اور اس پر دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک قربانی لازم ہے۔ اور یہ قربانی کفارہ اور جبر نقصان کی ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ من وجہ افعال عمرہ کو افعال حج پر مبنی کرنے والا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی آفاقی نے حج کا طواف قدوم کیا پھر عمرہ کا احرام باندھا پھر ان دونوں کو ادا کر دیا تو دونوں لازم ہوں گے اور دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آفاقی کے حق میں حج اور عمرہ دونوں کو جمع کرنا مشروع ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں کا احرام درست ہو گیا۔ اور متن میں طواف سے مراد طواف قدوم ہے اور طواف قدوم سنت ہے رکن نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ طواف قدوم ترک کرنے سے کچھ لازم نہیں ہوتا ۔ ہر حال جب اس نے ابھی تک حج کا کوئی رکن ادا نہیں کیا تو اس کے واسطے ممکن ہے کہ پہلے افعال عمرہ ادا کرے اور پھر افعال حج ادا کرے۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر دونوں کو پورا کر لیا تو جائز ہے البتہ دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہوگا۔ اور یہ دم کفارہ اور نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے ہے۔ دم شکر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ شخص من وجہ افعال عمرہ افعال حج پر بنا کرنے والا ہے کیونکہ طواف قدوم اگر چہ سنت ہے مگر افعال حج میں سے ہے۔ پس اس اعتبار سے طواف قدوم کے بعد افعال عمرہ کوادا کرنا مکروہ ہو گا۔ اور اس کراہت کی تلافی کے لئے یہ دم واجب کیا گیا ہے۔
And if he performed tawaf for Hajj, then entered ihram for Umrah, and performed both, they are binding upon him, and he owes a dam for combining them, because combining them is legislated as previously mentioned, so the ihram for both is valid. The intended tawaf here is the tawaf of greeting (tawaf al-qudum), and it is sunnah, not a pillar, so that he is not obliged by its omission anything. And when he has not performed what is a pillar, it is possible for him to perform the actions of Umrah and then the actions of Hajj. Therefore, if he performed both, it is valid, and he owes a dam for combining them. And this dam is of expiation and compensation; that is correct, because he has, in some respect, based the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and commentary. It addresses the scenario where a person performing Hajj (an afaqi) performs the tawaf al-qudum (the sunnah tawaf upon arrival) and then enters ihram for Umrah and completes both. The ruling is that both ihrams are valid and both are binding. However, because the person has already initiated Hajj actions (even though tawaf al-qudum is sunnah, not rukn), the actions of Umrah become based upon the actions of Hajj, which is contrary to the preferred order (sunnah) where Umrah should come before Hajj. Therefore, a dam (sacrificial animal) is wajib as a compensation for this dislikeable combining. The dam is a dam of kaffarah and jabar (expiation and compensation), not a dam of shukr (thanksgiving). The text explains that since no rukn of Hajj has been performed yet, it is possible to perform Umrah actions first, then Hajj actions, but the order is still considered a combining requiring dam.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The sunnah tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah for Hajj.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) that becomes wajib for certain violations in Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Both are valid but a dam is wajib.
C) Both are valid and no dam is required.
D) Only the Hajj is valid.

Key Takeaway
Performing tawaf al-qudum for Hajj before Umrah does not invalidate Umrah, but a dam is wajib as compensation for combining them in a disliked order.
