Recommendation to Abandon Umrah After Hajj Actions
Ruling on abandoning Umrah after Hajj actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on abandoning Umrah when Hajj actions have been performed, and identify the conditions and consequences.

Core Idea
It is mustahab to abandon Umrah after performing Hajj actions, but dam and qada are wajib.

When a person enters ihram for Umrah but then performs certain Hajj actions, the Hanafi school recommends abandoning the Umrah to avoid mixing the actions. However, because the Umrah has been validly commenced, it must be made up later, and a dam is required as compensation. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is rafd (abandoning) of Umrah ihram. It is a voluntary nullification of a valid act.
2
Locate the primary ruling
The text states it is mustahab (recommended) — not wajib — to abandon Umrah in this scenario.
The ruling is explicitly mustahab in the matn.
3
Identify the condition that triggers the recommendation
The condition is that the pilgrim has performed at least one Hajj action (e.g., tawaf al-qudum), which strengthens the Hajj ihram.
Without this condition, the recommendation does not apply.
4
Determine the legal consequences if acted upon
If the pilgrim abandons Umrah, two obligations arise: qada (make up) of that Umrah, and dam (sacrifice) as compensation for breaking the ihram.
Both qada and dam are wajib.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Other schools (e.g., Shafiʿi) may not require dam for abandoning Umrah; this is a Hanafi specificity.
The Hanafi view relies on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حج کے احرام کی وجہ سے عمرہ کا احرام چھوڑ دے
وَيُسْتَحَب أَنْ يَرْفَضَ عُمَرَتَهُ لِأَنَّ إحْرَامَ الْحَجِّ قَدْ تَأَكَدَ بِشَى مِنْ أَعْمَالِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا لَمْ يَطْفُ لِلْحَقِّ وَإِذَا رَفَضَ عُمَرَتَهُ يَقْضِيهَا لِصِحَةِ الشُّرُوعِ فِيهَا وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِرِفْضِهَا
ترجمہ اور مستحب ہے کہ اپنے عمرہ کو توڑ دے کیونکہ حج کا کچھ عمل کرنے سے احرام حج مؤکد ہو گیا ہے برخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ حج کے واسطے طواف قدوم نہ کیا ہو اور جب عمرہ کوتوڑ دیا تو اس کی قضاء کرے۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کو شروع کر ناصحیح ہو چکا ہے۔ اور اس پر عمرہ کو توڑنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہے۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
It is recommended that he abandons his Umrah, because the ihram of Hajj has been strengthened by something of its actions, contrary to when he did not perform tawaf for Hajj. And when he abandons his Umrah, he makes it up (qada) because the commencement in it was valid, and he owes a dam for abandoning it.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn. It discusses a person who has entered ihram for Umrah but has also performed some action in Hajj (like tawaf al-qudum), thereby strengthening his Hajj ihram. In such a case, it is mustahab (recommended) for him to abandon (rafd) his Umrah ihram. The reason is that continuing with Umrah would mean basing Umrah actions on Hajj actions, which is contrary to the preferred order. If he abandons it, he must perform qada (make up) of that Umrah later, because his commencement into Umrah was valid. Additionally, he owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah. The commentary notes this explanation is clear.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandoning or nullifying the ihram of Umrah voluntarily.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal wajib as compensation for abandoning Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib to complete the Umrah.
B) It is mustahab to abandon the Umrah.
C) The Umrah becomes invalid automatically.
D) He must perform Hajj first then Umrah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it is mustahab to abandon Umrah after performing Hajj actions, but this necessitates qada and a dam.

Ruling on Entering Umrah Ihram During Days of Nahr and Tashriq
Ruling on entering Umrah ihram during Hajj days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person enters ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or the days of Tashriq, explain the requirement to abandon the Umrah (rafd), and identify the penalties involved.

Core Idea
If you enter ihram for Umrah during Hajj days, you must abandon it and owe a dam and a replacement Umrah.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a pilgrim who has already performed the standing at Arafah (a rukn of Hajj) and then enters ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or during the days of Tashriq. What should he do? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling that balances the prohibition of combining Umrah with Hajj actions in a disfavored manner and the validity of the ihram itself. You will learn the obligations, the penalties, and an internal scholarly difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the ruling applies to someone who has already completed the rukn of Hajj (standing at Arafah) and then enters ihram for Umrah specifically on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the days of Tashriq (11th-13th).
This does not apply before Arafah.
2
State the primary ruling
The Umrah is binding (lazim), but he must abandon it (rafd). This is wajib. He cannot continue with the Umrah actions because they would be based on Hajj actions, which is disliked.
The reasoning is talil: he has already performed a rukn of Hajj.
3
Determine the consequences of abandoning
If he abandons (rafd) the Umrah, he owes a dam (kaffarah) for abandoning and must perform a replacement Umrah later (qada).
The dam is wajib.
4
Consider if he proceeds with the Umrah
If he ignores the rafd and completes the Umrah, it is valid (because the ihram was valid) but he still owes a dam for combining Hajj and Umrah actions in these days.
The dam is also for kaffarah.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference: if he had already shaved for Hajj (halq) before entering Umrah ihram, some say he does not need to abandon based on the apparent meaning of al-Asl, but the preferred view (mufta bihi) of the later mashayikh is to abandon to avoid the prohibition.
The tarjih is by al-Faqih and the mashayikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا یوم النحر میں یا ایام تشریق میں اس پر عمرہ لازم ہے
وَمَنْ أَهَلَّ بِعَمَرَةٍ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ أَوْ فِي أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيْقِ لَزِمَنَهُ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَيَرْفُضُهَا أَى يَلْزَمُهُ الرَّفْضُ لِأَنَّهُ فَدَادَى رُكْنَ الْحَج فَيَصِيرَ بَانِيَا أَفَعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجَّ مِنْ كُلَّ وَجْهِ وَ قَدْ كَرِهَتِ الْعُمْرَةُ فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا نَذَكُو فَلِهَذَا يَلْزَمُهُ رَفُضْهَا
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا یوم نحر میں یا ایام تشریق میں تو اس پر عمرہ لازم ہوگا اس کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ اور اس عمرہ کو توڑ دے یعنی اس پر توڑ دینا واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے رکن حج کو ادا کیا ہے۔ پس وہ من وجہ افعال عمرہ کو افعال حج پر بنا کر نے والا ہوگا۔ اور ان ایام میں عمرہ مگر وہ بھی ہے۔ اس بناء پر کہ ہم اس کو ذکر کریں گے ۔ پس اسی وجہ سے اس پر عمرہ ترک کرنا لازم ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ جس شخص نے یوم نحر میں یا ایام تشریق میں حلق سے پہلے یا طواف زیارت سے پہلے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا تو اس پر عمر ولا زم ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کا شروع کرنا صحیح ہے البتہ ا عمرہ کو ترک کرنا لازم ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ شخص حج کارکن یعنی وقوف عرفہ ادا کر چکا ہے، اب اگر یہ افعال عمرہ ادا کرے گا تو افعال عمرہ کو افعال حج پر مبنی کرنے والا ہو گا اور یہ خلاف سنت ہے۔ نیز ان ایام میں عمرہ ہی مکروہ ہے جیسا کہ ذکر کریں گے۔ اس لئے اس عمرہ کو چھوڑ نا ہی واجب ہے۔
فَإِنْ رَفَضَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَّ لِرَفْضِهَا وَعُمَرَةٌ مَكَانَهَا لِمَا بَيَّنَا فَإِنْ مَضَى عَلَيْهَا أجْزَاهُ لأن الكَرَاهَةَ لِمَعْنَى فِى غَيْرِ وَهُوَ كُونُهُ مَشْعُولًا فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ بِأَدَاءِ بَقِيَّةِ اعْمَالِ الْحَج فَيَجِبُ تَخْلِيصُ الْوَقْتِ لَمْ تَعْظِيمًا وَ عَلَيْهِ دَم لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا إِمَّا فِى الْإِحْرَامِ أَو فِي الْأَعْمَالِ الْبَاقِيَةِ قَالُوا وَهَذَا دَمَ كَفَّارَةِ أَيْضًا وَقِيلَ إِذَا حَلَقَ لِلْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أحْرَمَ لَا يَرْفُضُهَا عَلى ظَاهِرِ مَاذُکِرَ فِي الأصل وَقِيلَ يَرْفُضُهَا اِحْتِرَازًا عَنِ النَّهْي قَالَ الْفَقِيهُ أ. مَشَايِخُنَا عَلَى هَذَا
ترجمہ اور اگر عمرہ کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر عمرہ چھوڑنے کی قربانی اور اس کی جگہ ایک عمرہ واجب ہے جیسا کہ بیان کیا۔ اور اگر اس کو ادا کر لیا تو اسے کافی ہے کیونکہ کراہت کسی اور وجہ سے ہے اور وہ یہ کہ وہ ان ایام میں حج کے بقیہ اعمال سے مشغول ہے، پس وقت کو خالی کرنا واجب ہے عظمت کے لئے۔ اور اس پر دونوں کو جمع کرنے کی وجہ سے ایک دم واجب ہے یا تو احرام میں یا بقیہ اعمال میں۔ انہوں نے کہا یہ بھی کفارے کا دم ہے۔ اور کہا گیا جب حج کے لئے حلق کر لیا پھر احرام باندھا تو اسے نہیں چھوڑے گا ظاہر روایت کے مطابق جو اصل میں مذکور ہے۔ اور کہا گیا اسے چھوڑے گا نہی سے بچنے کے لئے۔ فقیہ [؟] ابو[؟] نے کہا ہمارے مشائخ اسی پر ہیں۔
And whoever entered ihram for Umrah on the day of Nahr (sacrifice) or on the days of Tashriq (drying of meat), it becomes binding upon him for what we have said, and he abandons it, i.e., he must abandon it, because he has performed the rukn of Hajj, so he becomes, in every respect, one who bases the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj. And Umrah is disliked in these days as well, as we will mention, so for this reason he must abandon it.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on entering ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or the days of Tashriq (11th-13th). The ruling is that the Umrah is binding (lazim) because the person has already performed a rukn of Hajj (the standing at Arafah), but he is required to abandon (rafd) the Umrah. This is because performing Umrah actions after Hajj rukn would mean basing Umrah on Hajj, which is contrary to the preferred order, and also because Umrah itself is disliked during these days. If he abandons it, he owes a dam and must make up (qada) the Umrah later. If he proceeds to complete the Umrah, it is valid but he still owes a dam for combining. The text also mentions a ikhtilaf about whether to abandon if he has shaved (halq) for Hajj. The preferred view of the mashayikh is to abandon to avoid prohibition. The commentary further explains the reasoning.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandoning or nullifying the ihram of Umrah; wajib in this context.
دم كفارة (dam kaffarah): A sacrificial animal as expiation for abandoning or combining in a prohibited manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person enters ihram for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr and then abandons (rafd) it, what is required?
A) He owes a dam and must repeat the Umrah later.
B) He owes nothing; rafd cancels all obligations.
C) He must perform Hady (sacrifice) but no qada.
D) The Umrah becomes invalid and must be started again.

Key Takeaway
Entering Umrah ihram after the rukn of Hajj on Yawm al-Nahr or Tashriq makes the Umrah binding but requires that you abandon it and pay a dam, with a later qada; if you proceed, you still owe a dam for combining.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Abandoning 'Umrah After Hajj Actions
Ruling with rational proof on istihbab of rafd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on abandoning an 'Umrah after starting Hajj actions and explain the istihbab reasoning based on the strength of Hajj ihram.

Core Idea
Abandoning a valid 'Umrah to prioritize Hajj is recommended, not forbidden, when Hajj ihram becomes strong.

This passage addresses a unique situation in Hajj where a pilgrim has entered ihram for 'Umrah but then begins performing the rites of Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that it is mustahabb (recommended) to abandon the 'Umrah and focus on Hajj, subject to compensation. Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal priority between the two pilgrimages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is abandoning a validly entered 'Umrah. The ruling is 'yustahab' meaning it is recommended (mustahabb).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): because the ihram of Hajj has become strong (ta'akkada) by performing some of its actions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'ta'akkada' indicates emphasis and strength, meaning the Hajj ihram now takes priority over the 'Umrah ihram.
4
Note the condition and contrast
This ruling applies only after performing some Hajj actions (e.g., wuquf at 'Arafah). In contrast, if one has not performed tawaf for Hajj, the recommendation does not apply.
5
Identify the consequences
If the 'Umrah is abandoned, it must be made up (qada) because the ihram was valid, and a dam (sacrificial animal) is owed as a penalty for abandoning it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُسْتَحَب أَنْ يَرْفَضَ عُمَرَتَهُ لِأَنَّ إحْرَامَ الْحَجِّ قَدْ تَأَكَدَ بِشَى مِنْ أَعْمَالِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا لَمْ يَطْفُ لِلْحَقِّ وَإِذَا رَفَضَ عُمَرَتَهُ يَقْضِيهَا لِصِحَةِ الشُّرُوعِ فِيهَا وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمُ لِرِفْضِهَا
And it is recommended that he abandon his 'Umrah because the ihram of Hajj has become strong by some of its actions, unlike when he has not performed tawaf for Hajj. And if he abandons his 'Umrah, he must make it up because he has validly entered into it, and upon him is a dam for abandoning it.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Hanafi madhhab regarding a person who has entered ihram for 'Umrah and later performed some actions of Hajj (such as standing at 'Arafah). The text states that it is recommended (mustahabb) to abandon the 'Umrah because the ihram of Hajj has become emphasized by those actions. This is contrasted with a situation where one has not yet performed tawaf al-qudum for Hajj. If the 'Umrah is abandoned, one must perform a makeup 'Umrah (qada') and also offer a dam (sacrificial animal) as a penalty for abandoning the valid ihram. The reasoning is that continuing the 'Umrah would lead to combining two acts of worship in a disapproved manner.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandonment of an 'Umrah that has been validly entered into.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as a penalty for abandoning a valid 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on abandoning an 'Umrah if one has already performed some acts of Hajj?
A) It is prohibited (haram).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb) but one must make it up and pay a dam.
C) It is obligatory (wajib).
D) It is permissible without any penalty.

Key Takeaway
It is recommended (mustahabb) to abandon a valid 'Umrah when Hajj actions have commenced, with the obligation to make up the 'Umrah and offer a dam.

Ruling on 'Umrah Ihram during Yawm al-Nahr and Tashriq
Ruling that 'Umrah ihram on these days is binding but must be abandoned

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person who enters ihram for 'Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or Tashriq, explain why it must be abandoned, and identify the intra-Hanafi variant regarding prior shaving.

Core Idea
Umrah ihram on these days is binding but must be abandoned, with a dam and a makeup Umrah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with a scenario that may seem contradictory: a valid 'Umrah that one is required to cancel. The key lies in the legal reason ('illah) of having already performed the pillar of Hajj, coupled with the dislike (karahah) of 'Umrah during these days. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing between obligations that cannot be combined and those that can be deferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering ihram for 'Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) or any day of Tashriq (11th-13th). The ruling is that it is binding (lazim) on the person, but he must abandon it (rafd wajib).
Note that 'binding' (lazim) means the ihram is valid and must be dealt with, but the required action is abandonment.
2
Locate the dalil (the legal reason)
The text gives two reasons: (a) the person has already performed the pillar of Hajj (rukn al-hajj), making his 'Umrah actions built upon Hajj actions; (b) performing 'Umrah on these days is disliked (makruh).
The dislike is not inherent but due to being occupied with remaining Hajj acts.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The combination of having performed the Hajj pillar and the dislike leads to the obligation of rafd. The 'Umrah cannot be properly completed without conflicting with the ongoing Hajj duties, so the only way to honor the time is to cancel the 'Umrah.
This is a based on istihsan or public interest, not a direct textual command.
4
Note the consequences of abandonment vs. proceeding
If he abandons (wajib), he owes a dam (sacrificial animal) and must perform a makeup 'Umrah later. If he proceeds and completes it, the 'Umrah suffices, but he still owes a dam for combining the two (either in ihram or in the remaining acts). This dam is of the kaffarah type.
The dam for proceeding is a penalty for violating the recommended sequence, not for invalidating the act.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a dispute among Hanafis regarding a person who shaved his head for Hajj (tahallul) and then entered ihram for 'Umrah on these days. The original position from al-Asl says he does not abandon, while later scholars (mashayikh) say he does abandon to avoid the prohibition. The mufta bihi is the view of abandonment.
This shows that even within the same school, later authorities may prefer a different view based on ihtiyat (caution).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَهَلَّ بِعَمَرَةٍ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ أَوْ فِي أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيْقِ لَزِمَنَهُ لِمَا قُلْنَا وَيَرْفُضُهَا أَى يَلْزَمُهُ الرَّفْضُ لِأَنَّهُ فَدَادَى رُكْنَ الْحَج فَيَصِيرَ بَانِيَا أَفَعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجَّ مِنْ كُلَّ وَجْهِ وَ قَدْ كَرِهَتِ الْعُمْرَةُ فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ أَيْضًا عَلَى مَا نَذَكُو فَلِهَذَا يَلْزَمُهُ رَفُضْهَا فَإِنْ رَفَضَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَّ لِرِفْضِهَا وَعُمَرَةٌ مَكَانَهَا لِمَا بَيَّنَا فَإِنْ مَضَى عَلَيْهَا أجْزَاهُ لأن الكَرَاهَةَ لِمَعْنَى فِى غَيْرِ وَهُوَ كُونُهُ مَشْعُولًا فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ بِأَدَاءِ بَقِيَّةِ اعْمَالِ الْحَج فَيَجِبُ تَخْلِيصُ الْوَقْتِ لَمْ تَعْظِيمًا وَ عَلَيْهِ دَم لِجَمْعِهِ بَيْنَهُمَا إِمَّا فِى الْإِحْرَامِ أَو فِي الْأَعْمَالِ الْبَاقِيَةِ قَالُوا وَهَذَا دَمَ كَفَّارَةِ أَيْضًا وَقِيلَ إِذَا حَلَقَ لِلْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ لَا يَرْفُضُهَا عَلى ظَاهِرِ مَاذُكِرَ فِي الأصل وَقِيلَ يَرْفُضُهَا اِحْتِرَازًا عَنِ النَّهْي قَالَ الْفَقِيهُ أ. مَشَايِخُنَا عَلَى هَذَا
And whoever enters ihram for 'Umrah on the day of Nahr or on the days of Tashriq, it becomes binding upon him for what we have said, and he must abandon it, i.e., he must abandon it because he has performed the pillar of Hajj, so he becomes one who builds the actions of 'Umrah upon the actions of Hajj in every way, and the 'Umrah is also disliked on these days as we will mention, so for this reason he must abandon it. So if he abandons it, upon him is a dam for its abandonment and a 'Umrah in its place for what we have stated. But if he goes through with it, it suffices him because the dislike is due to a meaning in other than it, which is being occupied in these days with performing the remaining acts of Hajj, so it is obligatory to free up the time for its veneration, and upon him is a dam for combining the two, either in the ihram or in the remaining acts. They said: This is also a dam of expiation. And it was said: When he shaves for Hajj then enters ihram, he does not abandon it according to the apparent meaning of what is mentioned in al-Asl. And it was said: He abandons it to avoid the prohibition. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far said: Our mashayikh are upon this.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation of a person who, after performing the essential rites of Hajj (such as standing at 'Arafah), enters ihram for 'Umrah on the day of Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah) or the days of Tashriq (11th-13th). The ruling is that this 'Umrah is valid and binding (lazim), but it must be abandoned (rafd) because the person has already performed the pillar of Hajj, so his 'Umrah actions would be built upon Hajj actions, which is improper. Additionally, performing 'Umrah on these days is itself disliked. Therefore, he must cancel it. If he cancels, he owes a dam and must perform a makeup 'Umrah. If he does not cancel and completes it, it suffices, but he still owes a dam for combining the two. The dam is considered a kaffarah (expiation). There is a difference of opinion regarding a person who shaved his head for Hajj (i.e., did tahallul) and then entered ihram: one view, based on al-Asl, says he does not abandon; another view says he does abandon to avoid the prohibition. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani reports that our mashayikh adopt the latter view (he abandons).

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandonment of a valid 'Umrah ihram, which is obligatory in this context.
دم كفارة (dam kaffarah): A sacrificial animal offered as expiation for a violation in Hajj, as opposed to a shukr (thanksgiving) sacrifice.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head as part of tahallul (exiting ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone enters ihram for 'Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr after performing the essential rites of Hajj, what is the ruling?
A) The 'Umrah is invalid and must be abandoned without penalty.
B) The 'Umrah is binding but must be abandoned; he owes a dam and a makeup 'Umrah.
C) He must complete the 'Umrah and then offer a dam for combining.
D) He may choose whether to continue or abandon without any obligation.

Key Takeaway
When 'Umrah ihram on Yawm al-Nahr or Tashriq conflicts with remaining Hajj duties, the Hanafi school requires abandonment (rafd) with a compensatory dam and makeup 'Umrah.

Abandoning a Second 'Umrah or Hajj When the First Hajj is Missed
Ruling with qiyas proof for abandoning new ihram after fawat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person whose Hajj is missed enters a new ihram, and explain the qiyas reasoning that makes it wajib to abandon.

Core Idea
If Hajj is missed, any new ihram must be abandoned to avoid combining two 'Umrahs in action.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario after Hajj is missed (fawat). After missing the standing at 'Arafah, a person must perform 'Umrah to exit ihram. If he then enters a new ihram for another 'Umrah or Hajj before completing that exit, he creates a prohibited combination. We'll explore the ruling, the qiyas proof, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
First, understand the context: a person's Hajj is missed (fawat). Then he enters ihram for a new 'Umrah or Hajj. The ruling is: he must abandon (yarfudhu) that new ihram.
The abandonment is immediate; he does not need to perform any actions for the new ihram.
2
Understand the reason for the ruling
The person who missed Hajj becomes halal by performing the actions of 'Umrah, but his original ihram does not convert into 'Umrah ihram. So if he enters a new 'Umrah, he will effectively combine two 'Umrahs in actions (one for the missed Hajj and the new one).
The combination in actions (jam' fi'l-an) is what makes it prohibited.
3
Analyze the qiyas proof
The author likens this to entering ihram for two 'Umrahs simultaneously, which is impermissible. Just as one must abandon one of them, here he must abandon the new ihram.
The qiyas is explicit: 'kama law ahrama bi-'umratayn'.
4
Determine the hukm level
According to the Hanafi school, this abandonment is wajib, not merely recommended. This is because the new ihram leads to a prohibited act (combining two 'Umrahs).
The hukm level is derived from the necessity to avoid prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ فَانهُ الْحَقُّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَةٍ أَوْ بِحَجَةٍ فَإِنَّهُ يَرْفُضُهَا لِأَنَّ فَانتَ الْحَجِّ يَتَحَلَّلْ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمَرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَنْقَلِبَ إحْرَامَهُ إحْرَامَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِيكَ فِى بَابِ الْفُوَاتِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ فَيَصِيرُ جَامِعاً بَيْنَ الْعُمْرَتَيْنِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الأفعالِ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَرْفُضَهَا كَمَا لَوْ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَتَيْنِ
For if Hajj is missed, then he enters ihram for 'Umrah or for Hajj, then he abandons it because the one whose Hajj is missed becomes in a state of tahallul by the actions of 'Umrah without his ihram being converted into the ihram of 'Umrah, as will come in the chapter of Fawat, God willing. So he becomes one who combines two 'Umrahs in terms of actions, so he must abandon it just as if he had entered ihram for two 'Umrahs.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a person's Hajj has been missed (fawat), meaning he failed to perform the standing at 'Arafah and thus cannot complete Hajj. To exit ihram, he must perform 'Umrah. If, after realizing the Hajj is missed, he enters a new ihram for 'Umrah or for another Hajj, he must abandon it. The reason is that the person who missed Hajj becomes halal by performing the actions of 'Umrah, but his original ihram does not change into 'Umrah ihram. Therefore, if he now enters a new ihram for 'Umrah, he will effectively be combining two 'Umrahs in terms of actions (one for the missed Hajj and the new one). This is analogous to entering ihram for two 'Umrahs simultaneously, which is prohibited. Hence, he must abandon the new ihram. The ruling applies whether the new ihram is for 'Umrah or for Hajj.

Key Terms
فوات (fawat): The situation where a person misses the essential rite of Hajj (standing at 'Arafah) and thus cannot complete Hajj.
تحلل (tahallul): The state of exiting ihram, achieved by performing 'Umrah in the case of fawat.
يرفض (yarfudhu): He abandons; in this context, he must leave the new ihram without performing any of its actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if, after missing his Hajj (fawat), he enters ihram for a new 'Umrah?
A) Complete the 'Umrah and then perform Hajj later.
B) Abandon the new 'Umrah because it would combine two 'Umrahs in actions.
C) Continue with the 'Umrah and offer an additional sacrifice.
D) It is permissible; no action is required.

Key Takeaway
A person who misses Hajj must perform 'Umrah to exit ihram; any further ihram entered before completing that 'Umrah must be abandoned.

Ruling on Umrah During Ayyam al-Tashriq: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on Umrah during Hajj days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on performing Umrah during Yawm al-Nahr/Ayyam al-Tashriq and identify the operative fatwa from the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Umrah during Hajj days is valid but makruh tahrīmī; combining both requires a dam of kaffārah.

This passage from a later Hanafi text discusses the ruling for someone who makes ihrām for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or the days of Tashriq. The key legal issue is whether one should abandon the Umrah to avoid occupying time meant for Hajj actions. The author presents an intra-Hanafi dispute, with the relied-upon position being to abandon the Umrah if made after shaving from Hajj.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the subject: a pilgrim who makes ihrām for Umrah during Yawm al-Nahr or Ayyam al-Tashriq. Note the two possible outcomes: complete or abandon the Umrah.
The scenario distinguishes between those who made ihrām before or after shaving from Hajj.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling categories
Determine the ruling for each outcome. If abandoned: a dam and a make-up Umrah are wajib. If completed: it is valid but a dam is due for combining.
The dam is considered kaffārah, not shukr.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
Why is Umrah makruh tahrīmī? Because it occupies time needed for remaining Hajj actions. The karāhah is not in the act itself but in the context.
This is a key analytical distinction: 'karāhah li ghayrih'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Some Hanafis (based on al-Mabsūt) say do not abandon; others (mashāyikh, as reported by Faqīh Abu Ja'far) say abandon to avoid the prohibition.
The dispute hinges on whether the prohibition overrides the validity.
5
Determine the muftā bihi
Faqīh Abu Ja'far reports that the mashāyikh are upon the abandonment view. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The alternative view is not entirely rejected but is considered less authoritative.

جو نبی وارد ہوئی ہے اس سے بچ سکے۔ فقیہ ابو جعفر کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ اسی قول پر ہیں۔
So when he left the Umrah, then upon him is a sacrifice for leaving Umrah and instead of it, one Umrah is obligatory. Because of what we have already explained. But if he completed that Umrah, it suffices. Because the prohibition is due to a meaning external to Umrah. And that meaning is his engagement with the remaining actions of Hajj in those days. So out of respect, it is obligatory to free time for it. And upon him, due to combining both, one sacrifice is incumbent. Either the combining is in the ihrām or in the remaining actions of Hajj. And the mashāyikh have said that this dam is also a dam of kaffārah. And it was said: When he shaved for Hajj then made ihrām for Umrah, he should not leave it according to the apparent wording of al-Mabsūt. And it was said: Leave it to avoid the prohibition. Faqīh Abu Ja‘far said: Our mashāyikh are upon this statement. Explanation of the issue: The person who made ihrām for Umrah on Yawm al-Nahr or the days of Tashrīq, if he left the Umrah, then due to leaving Umrah, one dam becomes obligatory upon him, and instead of the left Umrah, one Umrah is obligatory. The reason is that combining Hajj and Umrah is prescribed for the āfāqī. And if he did not leave Umrah but completed it, it suffices. Because there is no prohibition in the essence of Umrah, rather the prohibition is due to a meaning external to it, and that external meaning is engagement with the remaining acts of Hajj in those days. Meaning, in those days, since he has to perform the remaining acts of Hajj, it is obligatorily respectful to keep time free for the acts of Hajj. So when it is obligatory to keep time free for the actions of Hajj, then engaging in Umrah is makruh tahrīmī. Yes, due to combining Hajj and Umrah, one sacrifice is obligatory upon him. Either the combining is in the ihrām or in the remaining actions. Combining in the ihrām occurs when he made ihrām for Umrah before becoming halāl from the ihrām of Hajj through shaving. And if he made ihrām for Umrah after shaving, he will be combining in the remaining actions of Hajj. The mashāyikh said that this dam is also a dam of kaffārah, not a dam of shukr. Some people say: When he shaved for Hajj then made ihrām, he should not abandon Umrah, as is apparent from the wording of al-Mabsūt. And some said: In that case too he should abandon Umrah so that he can avoid the prohibition that came regarding Umrah in these days. Faqīh Abu Ja‘far said: Our mashāyikh are upon this statement.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a person who makes ihrām for 'umrah during Yawm al-Nahr or the days of Tashrīq should complete it or abandon it. The ruling is presented: if he abandons the 'umrah, he owes a dam (kaffārah) and must make up an 'umrah. If he completes it, it is valid. The Karāhah is not in the 'umrah itself but in occupying time needed for Hajj actions. Therefore, combining both Hajj and 'umrah in these days requires a dam. The mashāyikh consider this dam as kaffārah, not shukr. Then a dispute arises: if he has already shaved for Hajj and then makes ihrām for 'umrah, should he abandon it? According to al-Mabsūt, he does not abandon. Others say he should abandon to avoid the prohibition. Faqīh Abu Ja‘far reports that the majority of our mashāyikh are upon the latter view. The passage provides the reasoning and indicates the muftā bihi position is to abandon.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) offered as compensation for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrīmī): An action that is prohibitively disliked, close to haram, but not established by a definitive proof.
کفارہ (kaffārah): Expiation; a religious compensation for an offense or omission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is valid but makruh tahrīmī, and no dam is required.
C) It is valid and recommended.
D) It is valid but a dam is required for combining Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Performing Umrah during Ayyam al-Tashriq is valid but makruh tahrīmī, and combining Hajj and Umrah requires a dam of kaffārah; the muftā bihi is to abandon the Umrah if made after shaving.

Ruling on Making Ihrām for Another Hajj or Umrah After Missing Hajj
Explains ruling to abandon second ihrām after fawt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person after missing Hajj (fawt) makes ihrām for a second Hajj or 'umrah, and explain why he must abandon it and what penalties apply.

Core Idea
Must abandon second ihrām after missed Hajj, because it combines duas.

In this lesson, we explore a specific scenario in Hajj rulings: when someone misses the essential standing at Arafat (fawt) and then makes a new ihrām for another Hajj or 'umrah. The Hanafi ruling is clear—he must abandon the new ihrām and still owes qada and dam. The reasoning hinges on the principle that a person who missed Hajj already becomes halal through performing 'umrah actions, so a second ihrām creates an impermissible combination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: fawt al-hajj
The person has missed the standing at Arafat, so the Hajj is considered missed (fawt). He must complete the actions of 'umrah and make up the Hajj later.
2
Understand the legal effect of fawt
After fawt, the person becomes halal by performing tawaf, sa'y, and halq for 'umrah, without changing his ihrām to an 'umrah ihrām.
This is covered in the chapter of Fawt.
3
Apply to second ihrām for 'umrah
If he then makes ihrām for an 'umrah, he effectively performs two 'umrahs in actions, which is impermissible.
Analogy: like making zwei ihrāms for 'umrah.
4
Apply to second ihrām for Hajj
If he makes ihrām for a second Hajj, he combines two Hajjs in ihrām, also impermissible.
Analogy: like making zwei ihrāms for Hajj.
5
Derive the ruling and penalties
He must abandon the second ihrām (wajib). Because the commencement was valid, he owes qada; and because he becomes halal before the proper time, he owes a dam.
Qada is for the valid start; dam is for premature halal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حج فوت ہو گیا پھر عمرہ یا حج کا احرام باندھا تو دوسرے کو ترک کر دے
فَإِنْ فَانهُ الْحَقُّ ثُمَّ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَةٍ أَوْ بِحَجَةٍ فَإِنَّهُ يَرْفُضُهَا لِأَنَّ فَانتَ الْحَجِّ يَتَحَلَّلْ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمَرَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَنْقَلِبَ إحْرَامَهُ إحْرَامَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِيكَ فِى بَابِ الْفُوَاتِ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ فَيَصِيرُ جَامِعاً بَيْنَ الْعُمْرَتَيْنِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الأفعالِ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَرْفُضَهَا كَمَا لَوْ أَحْرَمَ بِعُمَرَتَيْنِ
ترجمہ اور اگر حج فوت ہو چکا پھر اس نے عمرہ کا یا حج کا احرام باندھا تو اس کو ترک کر دے۔ کیونکہ حج فوت کرنے والا افعال عمرہ سے حلال ہو جاتا ہے بغیر اس کے کہ اسکا احرام عمرہ کا احرام ہو جائے اس بنا پر کہا باب الفوات میں انشاء اللہ آئے گا۔ پس وہ باعتبار فعل کے دو عمروں کا جمع کرنے والا ہوگا۔ پس اس پر لازم ہے کہ عمرہ کو ترک کر دے جیسے اگر دو عمروں کا احرام باندھا ہو۔
تشریح اور اگر حج کا احرام فوت ہو گیا پھر عمرہ یا حج کا احرام باندھا تو یہ شخص دوسرے کو ترک کر دے خواہ وہ عمرہ ہو یا حج ہو۔ کیونکہ حج فوت کرنے والا افعال عمرہ ادا کر کے حلال ہو جاتا ہے بغیر اس کے کہ اس کا احرام منقلب ہو کر عمرہ کا احرام ہو جائے ۔ پس باعتبار افعال کے یہ شخص دو عمروں کا جمع کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عمرہ کو ترک کر دے۔ جیسے اس وقت کہ وہ دو عمروں کا احرام باندھے۔
حج فوت ہونے کے بعد دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا تو احرام میں دوج جمع کرنے والا ہوگا وَإِنْ أَحْرَمَ بِحَجَّةٍ يَصِيرُ جَامِعَا بَيْنَ الْحَجَّتَيْنِ إِحْرَامًا فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَرْفَضُهَا كَمَا لَوْ أَحْرَمَ بِحَدَّتَيْنِ وَ عَلَيْهِ قَصَا وَهَا لِصِحَةِ الشَّروع فِيهَا وَ دَم لِرَفْضِهَا بِالتَّحَلَّلَ قَبْلَ أَوَ إِنه
ترجمہ اور اگر دوسرا احرام حج کا باندھا ہو تو احرام میں دوج جمع کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ تو اس پر دوسرے حج کو ترک کرنا واجب ہے۔ ، اگر دو حج کا احرام باندھا ہو۔ اور اسپر اس کی قضاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں شروع کرنا صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور دم واجب ہے اس کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے ۔ اس کے وقت سے پہلے حلال ہو کر ۔
تشریح اگر حج فوت ہونے کے بعد دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا تو اس صورت میں احرام کے اندر دو حج جمع کرنے والا ہو گیا اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دوسرے حج کو ترک کرنا واجب ہے۔ جیسے اگر دو حج کا احرام باندھے تو ان میں سے ایک کا ترک کرنا واجب ہے البتہ اس پر اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اسکا شروع کرنا صحیح ہے اور ایک دم واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے وقت سے پہلے ہی حلال ہو کر اس کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
If Hajj is missed, then he made ihrām for 'umrah or for Hajj, then he abandons it. Because the one who misses Hajj becomes halāl through the actions of 'umrah without his ihrām changing to the ihrām of 'umrah, as will come in the chapter of Fawt, inshaAllah. So he becomes a combiner of two 'umrahs from the perspective of actions. So he must abandon it, just as if he made ihrām for two 'umrahs. Translation: And if Hajj has been missed, then he made ihrām for 'umrah or Hajj, he abandons it. Because the one who misses Hajj becomes halāl by performing the actions of 'umrah without his ihrām turning into the ihrām of 'umrah, as will come in the chapter of Fawt, inshaAllah. So he becomes a combiner of two 'umrahs in terms of actions. So it is incumbent upon him to abandon the 'umrah, just as if he made ihrām for two 'umrahs. Explanation: And if the ihrām of Hajj is missed, then he makes ihrām for 'umrah or Hajj, this person abandons the second, whether it be 'umrah or Hajj. Because the one who misses Hajj becomes halāl by performing the actions of 'umrah without his ihrām changing to the ihrām of 'umrah. So in terms of actions, this person becomes a combiner of two 'umrahs. And this is not permissible. So he abandons the 'umrah. Just as when he makes ihrām for two 'umrahs. If he makes ihrām for a (second) Hajj after Hajj is missed, then he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs in ihrām. And if he makes ihrām for a Hajj, he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs in ihrām, so he must abandon it, as if he made ihrām for two Hajjs. And upon him is its qada because the commencement was valid, and a dam for abandoning it by becoming halāl before its time. Explanation: If he makes ihrām for a second Hajj after Hajj is missed, then in this case he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs in ihrām, and this is impermissible. So it is wajib upon him to abandon the second Hajj, just as if he made ihrām for two Hajjs, abandoning one of them is wajib. However, qada of it is necessary because his commencement was valid, and one dam becomes wajib because he became halāl before its time and abandoned it.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage discusses the case of one who misses Hajj (fawat al-hajj) and then makes ihrām for another 'umrah or Hajj. The ruling is that he must abandon the second ihrām. The reasoning: a person who misses Hajj becomes halāl by performing the actions of 'umrah (i.e., tawaf, sa'y, halq) without changing the ihrām. So if he makes ihrām for an 'umrah, he effectively combines two 'umrahs in actions, which is impermissible. Similarly, if he makes ihrām for another Hajj, he combines two Hajjs in ihrām. Therefore he must abandon the second. If he abandons, he must make qada of it because the commencement was valid, and he owes a dam for becoming halāl before the proper time. The commentary provides the detailed reasoning and confirms the ruling with an analogy to making zwei ihrāms for the same type.

Key Terms
فوات (fawt): Missing the essential part of Hajj (standing at Arafat) so that the Hajj is considered missed and must be made up.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory religious act.
دم (dam): A penalty sacrifice (usually a sheep) required for violations of Hajj/Umrah rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if, after missing Hajj (fawt), he makes ihrām for another 'umrah?
A) Complete the 'umrah and it will suffice.
B) He must abandon the 'umrah and owes qada and dam.
C) He must continue the 'umrah but it is makruh.
D) Only a dam is required, no need to abandon.

Key Takeaway
After missing Hajj, any new ihrām for Hajj or 'umrah must be abandoned, and the person owes qada and dam.

Definition of Ihsar: Does Illness Count as Prevention?
Opens the chapter on Ihsar and presents the Hanafi proof that illness counts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ihsar, explain the linguistic distinction between ihsar and hasr, and apply the ruling to illness-based prevention.

Core Idea
Ihsar includes illness and enemy; hasr is enemy only – a Qur'anic word choice that changes fatwa.

This lesson opens the chapter on ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah) and presents a key dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. While the Shafi'i school restricts ihsar to enemy action, the Hanafis include illness based on a precise linguistic analysis of the Qur'anic verse. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the ruling on taḥallul (early release from ihram).

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the specific legal question? Does ihsar only occur when prevented by an enemy, or also by illness?
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that ihsar is established by either enemy or illness. Both justify taḥallul with a sacrifice.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that taḥallul with sacrifice was legislated for deliverance from the enemy, not from illness. Therefore illness does not qualify.
4
Analyse the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response cites the verse of ihsar (Qur'an 2:196) and the consensus of linguists: the word ihsar is used for illness, while hasr is used for the enemy. The Qur'an chose ihsar.
Note the linguistic argument is central to the Hanafi position.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a pilgrim is ill, Hanafis allow taḥallul with a sacrifice; Shafi'is require staying in ihram or later makeup. This difference can affect many pilgrims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الإِحْصَارِ
ترجمہ یہ باب محصر ہو جانے کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح احصار کے معنی روکنا۔ شریعت کی اصطلاح میں احصار یہ ہے کہ محرم کسی خوف یا دشمن یا بیماری کی وجہ سے افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ پورا کرنے سے رک جائے ۔ احصار چونکہ محرم پر جنایت ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو علیحدہ باب میں باب الجنایات کے بعد ذکر کیا۔ محرم دشمن یا مرض کی وجہ سے مصر ہو جائے اور جانے سے رک جائے تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
وَإِذَا أَحْصِرَ الْمُحْرِمُ بِعَدَةٍ أَوْ أَصَابَهُ مَرَضٌ فَمَنَعَهُ مِنَ الْمَضَى جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلَّلُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَكُونُ الْاَحْصَارُ الا بالعَدُ لأَنَّ التَّحَلَّلَ بِالهُدَى شُرِعَ فِى حَقِّ الْمُحْصَرِ لِتَحْصِيلِ النَّجَاةِ وَ بِالْإِحْلَالِ يَنْجُو مِنَ الْعَدُوِّ لَا مِن الْمَرْضِ وَلَنَا أنَّ أيَةَ الْإِحْصَارِ وَ رَدَتْ فِى الإِحْصَارِ بِالْمَرَضِ بِإِجْمَاعِ أَهْلِ اللَّغَةِ فَإِنَّهُمْ قَالُوا الْإِحْصَارُ بِالْمَرَضِ وَالْحَصْرُ بِالْعَدُو وَالتَحَلَّلَ قَبْلُ أوَاللَّهِ لِدَفْعِ الْحَوْجِ الْأَتِى مِنْ قَبْلِ امْتِدَادِ الْإِحْرَامِ وَالْحَرَجُ فِي الْاَصْطِبَارِ عَلَيْهِ معَ الْمَرَضِ أَعْظَمُ
ترجمہ اور جب محرم روکا گیا دشمن کی وجہ سے یا اسے کوئی ایسا مرض لاحق ہوا جس نے اس کو پورا کرنے سے روک دیا، تو اس کے لئے حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ احصار صرف دشمن سے ہوتا ہے کیونکہ تحلل بہدی محصر کے حق میں مشروع کیا گیا نجات حاصل کرنے کے لئے اور احلال سے دشمن سے نجات ملتی ہے مرض سے نہیں ملتی۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت احصار مرض کے احصار میں وارد ہوئی ہے اہل لغت کے اجماع سے، پس انہوں نے کہا احصار مرض کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے اور حصر دشمن کے ساتھ۔ اور تحلل پہلے (وقت سے پہلے) اس لئے جائز ہے کہ اس وجہ سے جو احرام کے طول کھینچنے کی وجہ سے آتی ہے اس کو دور کیا جائے اور مرض کے ساتھ اس پر صبر کرنے میں مشقت زیادہ ہے۔
Chapter of Iḥṣār. Translation: This chapter is about becoming Muḥṣar. Explanation: The meaning of iḥṣār is prevention. In Sharī‘ah, iḥṣār is that a Muḥrim stops from completing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah due to some fear, enemy, or illness. Since iḥṣār is an offense upon the Muḥrim, it is mentioned separately after the chapter of Jināyāt. When a Muḥrim becomes muḥṣar due to enemy or illness and is prevented from proceeding, it is permissible for him to become halāl. Imām Shāfi‘ī's viewpoint: and when the Muḥrim is prevented by an enemy or is afflicted with an illness that prevents him from proceeding, it is permissible for him to become halāl. Imām Shāfi‘ī said: iḥṣār occurs only by the enemy, because taḥallul with a sacrifice is legislated for the muḥṣar to achieve deliverance, and by iḥlāl he is delivered from the enemy, not from illness. And our evidence: that the verse of iḥṣār was revealed regarding iḥṣār by illness, by consensus of the people of language, for they said: iḥṣār is with illness, and ḥaṣr is with the enemy. And taḥallul before (the proper time) is to repel the distress that comes from the prolongation of the ihrām, and the hardship of patiently bearing it with illness is greater.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on iḥṣār (prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah) and presents a dispute between the Hanafis and Imām al-Shāfi‘ī. The Hanafi position: iḥṣār is established by both enemy and illness. al-Shāfi‘ī restricts iḥṣār to enemy only because the verse about iḥṣār (Qur'an 2:196) mentions fear, and taḥallul via sacrifice is for deliverance from enemy, not illness. The Hanafi response: the verse and linguistic consensus show that iḥṣār is used for illness, while ḥaṣr is used for enemy. Additionally, the reason for allowing taḥallul before completion is to remove distress from prolonged ihrām, and with illness the hardship is greater, making it more deserving of relief.

Key Terms
احصار (iḥṣār): Prevention from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah due to an external cause such as enemy or illness.
تحلل (taḥallul): Ending the state of ihrām and becoming permissible to do previously prohibited acts.
حصر (ḥaṣr): Confinement or prevention specifically by an enemy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is sufficient to establish iḥṣār?
A) Only an enemy preventing access to Mecca.
B) Only an illness that prevents completing Hajj.
C) Either an enemy or an illness that prevents completing Hajj/Umrah.
D) Any hardship that makes completion difficult.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school includes illness as a valid cause of iḥṣār, allowing taḥallul with a sacrifice, based on the linguistic distinction between iḥṣār and ḥaṣr in the Qur'an.

6 min
Ruling on Combining Two Hajjs in One Ihram
Ruling statement: consequences of entering a second Hajj ihram after missing the first.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who enters a second Hajj ihram after missing the first, and explain the required actions: rafd, qada', and dam.

Core Idea
Combining two Hajjs in one ihram is impermissible; the second ihram is valid but must be rejected, requiring both qada' and a dam.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj: what happens when someone, after missing their first Hajj, enters a new ihram for another Hajj in the same season? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling involving three obligations: rejection of the second ihram, making it up later, and a compensatory sacrifice. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the principle that each Hajj requires its own distinct ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and note the key situation: a person has already entered ihram for one Hajj but missed it (the Hajj became fā'it). Then, he enters a second ihram for another Hajj. This creates a combination of two Hajjs in one ihram.
The Urdu commentary also mentions the analogous case of two Umrahs.
2
Recognize the prohibition
Combining two Hajjs in one ihram is not permissible. The passage explicitly states it is 'jā'iz nahīṇ' (not permissible). This is the basis for the required action.
Each Hajj must be performed with a separate ihram.
3
Determine the remedy: rafd
The person must reject (rafḍ) the second Hajj by exiting ihram for it. This is wajib (obligatory). The manner of rafd is to make the intention to leave ihram, which results in premature tahallul.
Rafd is not a cancellation of the ihram but a voluntary exit.
4
Identify subsequent obligations: qada' and dam
Because the second ihram was validly entered (sahīḥ al-shurū'), the person owes qada' (making up the Hajj later). Additionally, since he left ihram prematurely (tahallul before its time), he must offer a dam (sacrifice) as expiation.
The dam is required even if the exit was for a valid reason (the prohibition of combining).
5
Relate to analogous cases
The passage compares this to entering ihram for two Hajjs simultaneously: in that case too, one must be rejected. The same ruling applies to two Umrahs in one ihram.
This reinforces the principle that only one Hajj or Umrah can be intended in a single ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
افعال کے یہ شخص دو عمروں کا جمع کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عمرہ کو ترک کر دے۔ جیسے اس وقت کہ وہ دو عمروں کا احرام باندھے۔ حج فوت ہونے کے بعد دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا تو احرام میں دو حج جمع کرنے والا ہوگا وَإِنْ أَحْرَمَ بِحَجَّةٍ يَصِيرُ جَامِعَا بَيْنَ الْحَجَّتَيْنِ إِحْرَامًا فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَرْفَضُهَا كَمَا لَوْ أَحْرَمَ بِحَدَّتَيْنِ وَ عَلَيْهِ قَصَا وَهَا لِصِحَةِ الشَّروع فِيهَا وَ دَم لِرَفْضِهَا بِالتَّحَلَّلَ قَبْلَ أَوَ إِنه ترجمہ اور اگر دوسرا احرام حج کا باندھا ہو تو احرام میں دو حج جمع کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ تو اس پر دوسرے حج کو ترک کرنا واجب ہے۔ ، اگر دو حج کا احرام باندھا ہو۔ اور اسپر اس کی قضاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں شروع کرنا صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور دم واجب ہے اس کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے ۔ اس کے وقت سے پہلے حلال ہو کر ۔ تشریح اگر حج فوت ہونے کے بعد دوسرے حج کا احرام باندھا تو اس صورت میں احرام کے اندر دو حج جمع کرنے والا ہو گیا اور یہ نا جائز ہے۔ اس لئے اس پر دوسرے حج کو ترک کرنا واجب ہے۔ جیسے اگر دو حج کا احرام باندھے تو ان میں سے ایک کا ترک کرنا واجب ہے البتہ اس پر اس کی قضا لازم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اسکا شروع کرنا صحیح ہے اور ایک دم واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے وقت سے پہلے ہی حلال ہو کر اس کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
This person combining two Umrahs became a combiner. And this is not permissible. So he should abandon the Umrah, like when he had entered ihram for two Umrahs. If after the Hajj is missed he enters ihram for another Hajj, then in the ihram he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs. And if he enters ihram for a Hajj, he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs in ihram, so he must reject it, just as if he had entered ihram for two Hajjs. And upon him is qada' because the commencement in it was valid, and a dam for abandoning it by becoming halal before its time. Translation: And if he enters ihram for a Hajj, he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs in ihram. So it is obligatory upon him to abandon the second Hajj. And if he entered ihram for two Hajjs, then qada' is obligatory upon him because the commencement was valid, and a dam is obligatory for abandoning it by becoming halal before its time. Explanation: If after the Hajj is missed he enters ihram for another Hajj, then in this case he becomes a combiner of two Hajjs within the ihram, and this is not permissible. Therefore, it is obligatory upon him to abandon the second Hajj, just as if he entered ihram for two Hajjs, it is obligatory to abandon one of them. However, qada' of it will be obligatory upon him because its commencement was valid, and a dam will be obligatory because he abandoned it by becoming halal before its time.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah, explained in Urdu. The issue: a person who had already entered ihram for Hajj and missed it (i.e., the Hajj became fā'it) then enters a second ihram for another Hajj. This results in combining two Hajjs in one ihram, which is impermissible. The remedy: he must reject (rafḍ) the second Hajj, i.e., exit ihram for it. Since entering the second ihram was valid, he owes qada' (making it up later) and also a dam (sacrifice) for leaving ihram before completing the rituals (tahallul before its proper time). The Urdu commentary clarifies that the ruling is analogous to simultaneously entering ihram for two Hajjs, where one must be abandoned.

Key Terms
رفض (rafḍ): Rejecting or abandoning the second Hajj by exiting ihram for it.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up the missed Hajj (the second one) because entering ihram for it was valid.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (shāh) wajib for prematurely leaving ihram (tahallul before time).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what obligations arise when a person enters a second Hajj ihram after the first was missed?
A) Only rejection (rafḍ) is required, no further obligations.
B) Rejection, qada', and dam are all wajib.
C) The second ihram is invalid, so nothing is required.
D) He must continue both Hajjs and offer a dam for each.

Key Takeaway
Combining two Hajjs in one ihram is impermissible; the second ihram is valid so it requires rejection, qada', and a dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
5 min
Definition and Legal Nature of Ihsar
Defines ihsar and states its two causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of ihsar, identify its two causes (enemy and illness), and explain the permissible ruling for tahallul.

Core Idea
Ihsar: prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah by enemy or illness, permitting tahallul with a sacrifice.

The chapter on Ihrār addresses the situation where a pilgrim is obstructed from completing rituals. The Hanafi school defines ihsar comprehensively, including both enemy and illness as valid causes. This lesson establishes that foundational definition and the consequential ruling of permissible tahallul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic meaning
Begin with the literal meaning of ihsar: prevention or hindrance. The text states 'al-ihsār al-ma‘nā al-man‘u' – the basic sense is to prevent.
Linguistic roots help understand the shar‘ī extension.
2
Note the shar‘ī definition from the text
The shar‘ī definition: the muhrim is prevented by fear, enemy, or illness from completing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah. Write down the three causes mentioned.
The text explicitly includes both 'khawf' (fear) and 'marad' (illness).
3
Distinguish between ihsar and hasr
The passage notes that linguists distinguish: ihsar is used for illness, hasr for enemy. This distinction is important for the later dispute.
Hanafi school uses both terms interchangeably for the legal ruling.
4
State the ruling: jawaz al-tahallul
The text concludes: 'jāza lahu al-taḥallul' – it is permissible for him to become halal. Understand that this is a rukhsah (concession), not an obligation.
The muhsar may also wait if he hopes to proceed.

پہلے حلال ہو جانا اس حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے جو احرام دراز ہونے کی وجہ سے آنے والا ہے حالانکہ مرض کے ساتھ احرام پر صبر کرنے کا حرج بہت بڑھ کر ہے۔ تشریح اگر محرم دشمن کے خوف کی وجہ سے افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ ادا کرنے سے روک دیا گیا یا کسی مرض کی وجہ سے احصار پایا گیا تو اس کے واسطے بغیر افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ ادا کرے حلال ہونا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ احصار صرف دشمن سے ہوتا ہے مرض وغیرہ سے احصار نہیں ہوتا ۔ یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِنْ أُحْصِرُتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (البقرة: ۱۹۲) یعنی (اگر تم روک دیئے جاؤ تو جو قربانی آسانی سے میسر ہو ) احصار کے بارے میں نازل ہوا ہے۔ یعنی جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ کو دشمنان اسلام نے حدیبیہ میں روک دیا۔ تو یہ آیت نازل ہوئی ، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہدی کے جانور ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جاؤ ، چنانچہ ایسا ہی ہوا۔ اس شان نزول سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ احصار دشمن کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مرض کی وجہ ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصر کے حق میں ہدی ذبح کر کے حلال ہونا اس لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے تا کہ نجات حاصل ہو ۔ اور حلال ہو جانے سے دشمن سے نجات ملتی ہے نہ کہ مرض سے کیونکہ حلال ہونے کی وجہ سے مرض زائل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ دشمن سے حفاظت ہو جاتی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ احصار دشمن کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت احصار، احصار بالمرض کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور اس پر تمام اہل لغت کا اجماع ہے۔ چنانچہ اہل زبان نے کہا کہ احصار کا لفظ مرض کی وجہ سے رکنے کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے اور حصر کا لفظ دشمن کی وجہ سے رکنے کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے۔ پس مرض کی وجہ سے منحصر ہونا تو آیت سے ثابت ہے اور دشمن کی وجہ سے مصر ہونا حدیث یعنی واقعہ حدیبیہ سے ثابت ہے۔ پس احصار دشمن کیساتھ خاص نہ رہا، جیسا کہ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں بلکہ دشمن اور مرض دونوں کی وجہ سے احصار ہوتا ہے۔ وَالتَّحَلُلُ قَبْلَ أو ايه .... الخ سے دوسری دلیل ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ آیت احصار دشمن کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے لیکن مرض دشمن کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا۔ بایں طور کہ مصر کو قبل از وقت حلال ہونے کی اجازت اس حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے جو امتداد اجرام اور درازگی احرام کی وجہ سے پیدا ہو گا اور مرض کے ساتھ احترام پر صبر کرنے کا حرج بڑھ کر ہے بہ نسبت دشمن کے احصار کے۔ کیونکہ مرض میں دو او علاج کی کثرت اور ہاتھ پاؤں سے مجبوری ظاہر ہے۔ پس جب ادنیٰ حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے دشمن کے احصار کو تسلیم کر لیا گیا۔ تو اعلیٰ درجہ کے حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے مرض کے احصار کا اعتبار بدرجہ اولیٰ ہوگا۔ محصر کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، اور اس کی صورت وَإِذَا جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلُلُ يُقَالُ لَهُ إِبْعَثُ شَاةً تُذْبَحُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَوَاعِدُ مَنْ تَبْعَثُهُ بِيَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ يَذْبَحُ فِيْهِ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْعَثُ
Chapter of Ihrār. Translation: This chapter is about being prevented. Explanation: The meaning of ihsār is to prevent. In sharī‘ah terminology, ihsār is that the muhrim is prevented by fear, enemy, or illness from completing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah. Since ihsār is an injury upon the muhrim, it is mentioned in a separate chapter after the chapter of injuries. If the muhrim is prevented by enemy or illness, it is permissible for him to become halāl. Imam Shāfi‘ī’s view: And when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or illness befalls him and prevents him from proceeding, becoming halāl is permissible for him. And Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār is only by an enemy, because becoming halāl with a hady was legislated for the muhsar to achieve deliverance. And by becoming halāl he is delivered from the enemy, not from illness. Our proof: The verse of ihsār came regarding ihsār by illness, by consensus of the people of language. Indeed they said: ihsār is by illness, and hasr is by enemy. And becoming halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that comes from the prolongation of ihram; and the hardship of patient endurance with illness is greater. Translation: And when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or illness that prevents him from proceeding, becoming halāl is permissible for him. Imam Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār is only by an enemy, because for the muhsar, becoming halāl with a hady was legislated to achieve deliverance. And by becoming halāl, deliverance from the enemy is achieved, not from illness. And our proof is that by consensus of the people of language, the verse of ihsār came regarding ihsār occurring by illness. Because the people of language said: ihsār is by illness, and hasr is by enemy. And becoming halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that comes from the prolongation of ihram, and the hardship of patient endurance with illness is much greater. Explanation: If the muhrim is prevented by fear of an enemy or by illness from performing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah, it is permissible for him to become halāl without performing those actions. Imam Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār occurs only from an enemy, not from illness. This is also the saying of Imam Mālik. The proof of Imam Shāfi‘ī is the saying of Allah Most High: ‘But if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] what is easy of the hady’ (al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse was revealed regarding ihsār – that is, when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and his companions were prevented by the enemies of Islam at Hudaybiyyah, this verse was revealed. Its meaning is: slaughter the hady animal and become halāl. This occasion of revelation indicates that ihsār is caused by an enemy, not by illness. A second proof: For the muhsar, becoming halāl with a hady was legislated to achieve deliverance. And deliverance from the enemy is achieved by becoming halāl, not from illness, because illness is not removed by becoming halāl. Rather, protection from the enemy is achieved. From this too it is known that ihsār is specific to the enemy. Our proof: The verse of ihsār was revealed regarding ihsār by illness, and there is consensus of all the linguists on this. Thus, the people of language said: the word ihsār is used for being prevented by illness, and the word hasr is used for being prevented by an enemy. So being prevented (muhsar) by illness is established from the verse, and being prevented by an enemy is established from the hadith (the incident of Hudaybiyyah). Therefore, ihsār is not specific to the enemy, as Imam Shāfi‘ī says; rather, ihsār occurs from both enemy and illness. The phrase ‘and becoming halāl before its time...’ is a second proof. Its summary: We accept that the verse of ihsār was revealed regarding the enemy, but illness is analogous [literally: joined] to the enemy. In that giving permission to the muhsar to become halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that is caused by the prolongation of the ihram. And the hardship of patient endurance with illness is greater than that of ihsār by an enemy. Because in illness, the difficulty of treatment and physical helplessness are obvious. So when ihsār by an enemy is accepted for repelling a lesser hardship, then for repelling a greater hardship, the consideration of ihsār by illness takes priority. It is permissible for the muhsar to become halāl, and its manner: And when becoming halāl is permissible for him, he is told: send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and appoint someone you send for a specific day to slaughter in it, then become halāl. And he sends only...
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on ihrār (being prevented from completing Hajj or ‘Umrah). It first defines ihsār in Hanafi terminology: prevention by enemy or illness. Then it presents a dispute with Imam Shāfi‘ī, who restricts ihsār to enemy only. The Hanafi response has two arguments: (1) Linguistic consensus that the word ihsār is used for illness, while hasr is for enemy; the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) about Hudaybiyyah establishes ihsār by enemy, but the linguistic usage and another interpretation show illness also qualifies. (2) The purpose of permitting tahallul is to remove hardship; the hardship of remaining in ihram while ill is even greater than that of an enemy, so by qiyas awlā (priority analogy), illness is a valid cause.

Key Terms
احصار (iḥṣār): Being prevented from completing Hajj or ‘Umrah by an enemy or illness, allowing tahallul with a sacrifice.
حصر (ḥaṣr): Being prevented by an enemy, distinguished from iḥṣār (illness) in linguistic usage.
تحلل (taḥallul): Leaving the state of ihram before completing Hajj/‘Umrah, permitted for the muhsar.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for the muhsar to slaughter to become halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what are the causes of ihsār?
A) Only enemy
B) Only illness
C) Both enemy and illness
D) Only in the case of a woman giving birth

Key Takeaway
Ihsar in the Hanafi school is prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah by enemy or illness, leading to the permissibility of tahallul with a sacrifice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
7 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute: Is Illness a Valid Cause of Ihsar?
Presents Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on whether illness causes ihsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on illness as a cause of ihsar, and explain the Hanafi proofs: linguistic consensus and qiyas awla.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school extends ihsar to illness, using linguistic consensus and the principle that the greater hardship (illness) deserves the concession a fortiori.

This lesson delves into the classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether illness is a valid cause of ihsar. The Hanafi school presents two powerful arguments: the linguistic usage of the Quranic term and the priority analogy (qiyas awla) that when a lesser hardship (enemy) permits tahallul, a greater hardship (illness) permits it even more.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The contested matter: does ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj/‘Umrah) occur only by an enemy, or also by illness? Write down both positions.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Shafi'i holds that ihsar is only by enemy. Their proof: the verse of ihsar 'fa in uhsirtum...' was revealed at Hudaybiyyah due to enemy prevention. Also, tahallul is for deliverance from enemy, not illness.
Note the second proof: deliverance (najāh) is from enemy, not illness.
3
State the Hanafi position
Hanafi holds that ihsar occurs by both enemy and illness. The ruling of tahallul applies in both cases.
4
Explain the Hanafi linguistic proof
The Hanafi school cites ijma‘ of linguists: the word ihsār is used for illness, while hasr is used for enemy. Therefore, the Quranic verse encompasses illness.
The verse itself is general (āmm) and not restricted to the occasion of revelation.
5
Explain the qiyas awla argument
Even if we accept the verse was revealed regarding the enemy, the hardship of illness is greater than the hardship of enemy. Since tahallul is permitted to relieve hardship, it is even more justified for illness. This is qiyas awla (priority analogy).
Qiyas awla: the secondary case (illness) is more deserving of the ruling than the primary case (enemy).

بَابُ الإِحْصَارِ ترجمہ یہ باب محصر ہو جانے کے بیان میں ہے تشریح احصار کے معنی روکنا۔ شریعت کی اصطلاح میں احصار یہ ہے کہ محرم کسی خوف یا دشمن یا بیماری کی وجہ سے افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ پورا کرنے سے رک جائے ۔ احصار چونکہ محرم پر جنایت ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو علیحدہ باب میں باب الجنایات کے بعد ذکر کیا۔ محرم دشمن یا مرض کی وجہ سے مصر ہو جائے اور جانے سے رک جائے تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر وَإِذَا أَحْصِرَ الْمُحْرِمُ بِعَدَةٍ أَوْ أَصَابَهُ مَرَضٌ فَمَنَعَهُ مِنَ الْمَضَى جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلَّلُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَكُونُ الْاَحْصَارُ الا بالعَدُ لأَنَّ التَّحَلَّلَ بِالهُدَى شُرِعَ فِى حَقِّ الْمُحْصَرِ لِتَحْصِيلِ النَّجَاةِ وَ بِالْإِحْلَالِ يَنْجُو مِنَ الْعَدُوِّ لَا مِن الْمَرْضِ وَلَنَا أنَّ أيَةَ الْإِحْصَارِ وَ رَدَتْ فِى الإِحْصَارِ بِالْمَرَضِ بِإِجْمَاعِ أَهْلِ اللَّغَةِ فَإِنَّهُمْ قَالُوا الْإِحْصَارُ بِالْمَرَضِ وَالْحَصْرُ بِالْعَدُو وَالتَحَلَّلَ قَبْلُ أوَاللَّهِ لِدَفْعِ الْحَوْجِ الْأَتِى مِنْ قَبْلِ امْتِدَادِ الْإِحْرَامِ وَالْحَرَجُ فِي الْاَصْطِبَارِ عَلَيْهِ معَ الْمَرَضِ أَعْظَمُ ترجمہ اور جب محرم روکا گیا دشمن کی وجہ سے یا اسے کوئی ایسا مرض لاحق ہوا جس نے اس کو پورا کرنے سے روک دیا، تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ احصار نہیں ہوگا مگر دشمن کی وجہ سے۔ کیونکہ محصر کے حق میں ہدی ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جانا نجات حاصل کرنے کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے۔ اور حلال ہو جانے سے دشمن سے نجات حاصل ہوگی نہ کہ بیماری سے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ با جماع اہل لغت آیت احصار مرض کی وجہ سے احصار واقع ہونے میں وارد ہوئی ہے کیونکہ اہل لغت نے کہا کہ احصار تو مرض کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور حصر دشمن کی وجہ سے۔ اور وقت سے کیساتھ خاص نہ رہا، جیسا کہ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں بلکہ دشمن اور مرض دونوں کی وجہ سے احصار ہوتا ہے۔ وَالتَّحَلُلُ قَبْلَ أو ايه .... الخ سے دوسری دلیل ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ آیت احصار دشمن کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے لیکن مرض دشمن کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا۔ بایں طور کہ مصر کو قبل از وقت حلال ہونے کی اجازت اس حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے جو امتداد اجرام اور درازگی احرام کی وجہ سے پیدا ہو گا اور مرض کے ساتھ احترام پر صبر کرنے کا حرج بڑھ کر ہے بہ نسبت دشمن کے احصار کے۔ کیونکہ مرض میں دو او علاج کی کثرت اور ہاتھ پاؤں سے مجبوری ظاہر ہے۔ پس جب ادنیٰ حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے دشمن کے احصار کو تسلیم کر لیا گیا۔ تو اعلیٰ درجہ کے حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے مرض کے احصار کا اعتبار بدرجہ اولیٰ ہوگا۔ محصر کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، اور اس کی صورت وَإِذَا جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلُلُ يُقَالُ لَهُ إِبْعَثُ شَاةً تُذْبَحُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَوَاعِدُ مَنْ تَبْعَثُهُ بِيَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ يَذْبَحُ فِيْهِ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْعَثُ
Chapter of Ihrār. Translation: This chapter is about being prevented. Explanation: The meaning of ihsār is to prevent. In sharī‘ah terminology, ihsār is that the muhrim is prevented by fear, enemy, or illness from completing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah. Since ihsār is an injury upon the muhrim, it is mentioned in a separate chapter after the chapter of injuries. If the muhrim is prevented by enemy or illness, it is permissible for him to become halāl. Imam Shāfi‘ī’s view: And when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or illness befalls him and prevents him from proceeding, becoming halāl is permissible for him. And Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār is only by an enemy, because becoming halāl with a hady was legislated for the muhsar to achieve deliverance. And by becoming halāl he is delivered from the enemy, not from illness. Our proof: The verse of ihsār came regarding ihsār by illness, by consensus of the people of language. Indeed they said: ihsār is by illness, and hasr is by enemy. And becoming halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that comes from the prolongation of ihram; and the hardship of patient endurance with illness is greater. Translation: And when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or illness that prevents him from proceeding, becoming halāl is permissible for him. Imam Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār is only by an enemy, because for the muhsar, becoming halāl with a hady was legislated to achieve deliverance. And by becoming halāl, deliverance from the enemy is achieved, not from illness. And our proof is that by consensus of the people of language, the verse of ihsār came regarding ihsār occurring by illness. Because the people of language said: ihsār is by illness, and hasr is by enemy. And becoming halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that comes from the prolongation of ihram, and the hardship of patient endurance with illness is much greater. Explanation: If the muhrim is prevented by fear of an enemy or by illness from performing the actions of Hajj or ‘Umrah, it is permissible for him to become halāl without performing those actions. Imam Shāfi‘ī said: Ihrār occurs only from an enemy, not from illness. This is also the saying of Imam Mālik. The proof of Imam Shāfi‘ī is the saying of Allah Most High: ‘But if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] what is easy of the hady’ (al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse was revealed regarding ihsār – that is, when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and his companions were prevented by the enemies of Islam at Hudaybiyyah, this verse was revealed. Its meaning is: slaughter the hady animal and become halāl. This occasion of revelation indicates that ihsār is caused by an enemy, not by illness. A second proof: For the muhsar, becoming halāl with a hady was legislated to achieve deliverance. And deliverance from the enemy is achieved by becoming halāl, not from illness, because illness is not removed by becoming halāl. Rather, protection from the enemy is achieved. From this too it is known that ihsār is specific to the enemy. Our proof: The verse of ihsār was revealed regarding ihsār by illness, and there is consensus of all the linguists on this. Thus, the people of language said: the word ihsār is used for being prevented by illness, and the word hasr is used for being prevented by an enemy. So being prevented (muhsar) by illness is established from the verse, and being prevented by an enemy is established from the hadith (the incident of Hudaybiyyah). Therefore, ihsār is not specific to the enemy, as Imam Shāfi‘ī says; rather, ihsār occurs from both enemy and illness. The phrase ‘and becoming halāl before its time...’ is a second proof. Its summary: We accept that the verse of ihsār was revealed regarding the enemy, but illness is analogous [literally: joined] to the enemy. In that giving permission to the muhsar to become halāl before its time is to repel the hardship that is caused by the prolongation of the ihram. And the hardship of patient endurance with illness is greater than that of ihsār by an enemy. Because in illness, the difficulty of treatment and physical helplessness are obvious. So when ihsār by an enemy is accepted for repelling a lesser hardship, then for repelling a greater hardship, the consideration of ihsār by illness takes priority. It is permissible for the muhsar to become halāl, and its manner: And when becoming halāl is permissible for him, he is told: send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and appoint someone you send for a specific day to slaughter in it, then become halāl. And he sends only...
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on ihrār (being prevented from completing Hajj or ‘Umrah). It first defines ihsār in Hanafi terminology: prevention by enemy or illness. Then it presents a dispute with Imam Shāfi‘ī, who restricts ihsār to enemy only. The Hanafi response has two arguments: (1) Linguistic consensus that the word ihsār is used for illness, while hasr is for enemy; the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:196) about Hudaybiyyah establishes ihsār by enemy, but the linguistic usage and another interpretation show illness also qualifies. (2) The purpose of permitting tahallul is to remove hardship; the hardship of remaining in ihram while ill is even greater than that of an enemy, so by qiyas awlā (priority analogy), illness is a valid cause.

Key Terms
احصار (iḥṣār): Being prevented from completing Hajj or ‘Umrah by an enemy or illness, allowing tahallul with a sacrifice.
حصر (ḥaṣr): Being prevented by an enemy, distinguished from iḥṣār (illness) in linguistic usage.
تحلل (taḥallul): Leaving the state of ihram before completing Hajj/‘Umrah, permitted for the muhsar.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for the muhsar to slaughter to become halal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The consensus of linguists that ihsar is used for illness
B) The verse of Hudaybiyyah was abrogated
C) Qiyas on the case of a woman giving birth
D) Ijma of the companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's inclusion of illness as a cause of ihsar is grounded in linguistic consensus and the principle of priority analogy (qiyas awla).

Tahallul of the Muhsar: Procedure and Conditions
Ruling on the muhsar's tahallul procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for the muhsar's tahallul and identify the conditions that must be fulfilled for it to be valid.

Core Idea
The muhsar must send a sacrifice to the Haram and appoint a specific day to become halal.

This short passage from al-Hidayah gives the essential ruling on how a person prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar) can leave ihrām. The text instructs him to send a sheep to the Haram to be slaughtered on a predetermined day, after which he becomes halāl. We will unpack the conditions and sequence of this legal process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'tahallul' (leaving ihrām) for the muhsar. The text says 'when tahallul is permissible for him' – i.e., once he is excused from continuing Hajj, he may proceed with the tahallul procedure.
The permissibility itself is based on being prevented (ihsār).
2
List the required elements
The muhsar is told to: (1) send (yab‘ath) a sheep (shāh), (2) to be slaughtered (tudhbah) in the Haram (Mecca), (3) appoint a specific day (bi-yawm bi-‘aynihi), (4) for his deputy to slaughter on that day.
The animal must be a sheep; a larger animal is better but not required.
3
Understand the sequence
The order is: send the animal (or its value) → appoint a person and a day → slaughter takes place on that day in the Haram → then the muhsar becomes halāl. The tahallul occurs after the slaughter, not before.
The text uses 'thumma' (then) to indicate the sequence.
4
Recognize the scope of the ruling
The passage begins to discuss what else may be sent ('wa innamā yab‘ath...') but is cut off. The full Hanafi ruling permits sending the price of the animal if one cannot find a sacrifice.
The missing text continues with details about sending the value or a substitute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلُلُ يُقَالُ لَهُ إِبْعَثُ شَاةً تُذْبَحُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَوَاعِدُ مَنْ تَبْعَثُهُ بِيَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ يَذْبَحُ فِيْهِ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْعَثُ

Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on how the muhsar performs tahallul. Once it is permissible for him to leave ihram, he is instructed to send a sheep (shāh) to the Haram (Mecca or its precincts). He must appoint a specific day on which the sacrifice will be slaughtered. On that day, after the sacrifice, he becomes halal (leaves ihram). The text then begins to discuss what he sends, but is cut off. The full ruling from the Hidayah would continue: he sends the price of the animal if he cannot find one, etc.

Key Terms
يبعث (yab‘ath): To send (a sacrifice or its price) to the Haram for the muhsar.
شاة (shāh): A sheep, the minimum sacrifice for the muhsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The muhsar must send a sheep (or its value) to the Haram to be slaughtered on a specific day before he can become halal.
