The Definition of Ihsar: Illness vs. Enemy
Dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'i on cause of ihsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ihsar and explain the linguistic and analogical evidence that includes illness.

Core Idea
Ihsar includes illness because the Quran's general word and greater hardship demand it.

The concept of ihsar—being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah—is debated between schools. The Hanafi school holds that both enemy and illness trigger the concession of tahallul (exiting ihram early). This lesson examines the proofs from both sides, focusing on the linguistic distinction between 'ihsar' and 'hasr' and the analogical reasoning that places illness at a higher level of hardship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: tahallul is permitted for a muhrim prevented by either enemy or illness.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Recognize that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik restrict ihsar to enemy prevention only.
Their position is based on the occasion of revelation of verse 2:196.
3
Examine the Hanafi linguistic proof
Understand the consensus of lexicographers: 'ihsar' is used for illness, 'hasr' for enemy. The Quranic term 'uhsirtum' thus includes illness.
This is a dalil naqli from language.
4
Analyze the qiyas awlawi
Follow the analogy: if tahallul is allowed for the lesser hardship (enemy), it is even more warranted for the greater hardship (illness).
This is a rational proof (qiyas jali).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: Hanafis allow a sick pilgrim to exit ihram; Shafi'is do not and require him to wait or perform later.
This affects real-world fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہونا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ احصار نہیں ہوگا مگر دشمن کی وجہ سے۔ کیونکہ محصر کے حق میں ہدی ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جانا نجات حاصل کرنے کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے۔ اور حلال ہو جانے سے دشمن سے نجات حاصل ہوگی نہ کہ بیماری سے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ با جماع اہل لغت آیت احصار مرض کی وجہ سے احصار واقع ہونے میں وارد ہوئی ہے کیونکہ اہل لغت نے کہا کہ احصار تو مرض کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ اور حصر دشمن کی وجہ سے۔ اور وقت سے پہلے حلال ہو جانا اس حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے جو احرام دراز ہونے کی وجہ سے آنے والا ہے حالانکہ مرض کے ساتھ احرام پر صبر کرنے کا حرج بہت بڑھ کر ہے۔ تشریح اگر محرم دشمن کے خوف کی وجہ سے افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ ادا کرنے سے روک دیا گیا یا کسی مرض کی وجہ سے احصار پایا گیا تو اس کے واسطے بغیر افعال حج یا افعال عمرہ ادا کرے حلال ہونا جائز ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ احصار صرف دشمن سے ہوتا ہے مرض وغیرہ سے احصار نہیں ہوتا ۔ یہی قول امام مالک کا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِنْ أُحْصِرْتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْي (البقرة: ۱۹۲) یعنی (اگر تم روک دیئے جاؤ تو جو قربانی آسانی سے میسر ہو ) احصار کے بارے میں نازل ہوا ہے۔ یعنی جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ کو دشمنان اسلام نے حدیبیہ میں روک دیا۔ تو یہ آیت نازل ہوئی ، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہدی کے جانور ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جاؤ ، چنانچہ ایسا ہی ہوا۔ اس شان نزول سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ احصار دشمن کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مرض کی وجہ ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مصر کے حق میں ہدی ذبح کر کے حلال ہونا اس لئے مشروع کیا گیا ہے تا کہ نجات حاصل ہو ۔ اور حلال ہو جانے سے دشمن سے نجات ملتی ہے نہ کہ مرض سے کیونکہ حلال ہونے کی وجہ سے مرض زائل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ دشمن سے حفاظت ہو جاتی ہے اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ احصار دشمن کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ آیت احصار، احصار بالمرض کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور اس پر تمام اہل لغت کا اجماع ہے۔ چنانچہ اہل زبان نے کہا کہ احصار کا لفظ مرض کی وجہ سے رکنے کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے اور حصر کا لفظ دشمن کی وجہ سے رکنے کے لئے بولا جاتا ہے۔ پس مرض کی وجہ سے منحصر ہونا تو آیت سے ثابت ہے اور دشمن کی وجہ سے مصر ہونا حدیث یعنی واقعہ حدیبیہ سے ثابت ہے۔ پس احصار دشمن کے ساتھ خاص نہ رہا، جیسا کہ امام شافعی کہتے ہیں بلکہ دشمن اور مرض دونوں کی وجہ سے احصار ہوتا ہے۔ وَالتَّحَلُلُ قَبْلَ أو [؟] .... الخ سے دوسری دلیل ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ آیت احصار دشمن کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے لیکن مرض دشمن کے ساتھ لاحق ہو گا۔ بایں طور کہ مصر کو قبل از وقت حلال ہونے کی اجازت اس حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے ہے جو امتداد اجرام اور درازگی احرام کی وجہ سے پیدا ہو گا اور مرض کے ساتھ احترام پر صبر کرنے کا حرج بڑھ کر ہے بہ نسبت دشمن کے احصار کے۔ کیونکہ مرض میں دواؤ اور علاج کی کثرت اور ہاتھ پاؤں سے مجبوری ظاہر ہے۔ پس جب ادنیٰ حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے دشمن کے احصار کو تسلیم کر لیا گیا۔ تو اعلیٰ درجہ کے حرج کو دور کرنے کے لئے مرض کے احصار کا اعتبار بدرجہ اولیٰ ہوگا۔
It is permissible. Imam Shafi'i said that ihsar will not occur except due to an enemy. Because for the muhsar, slaughtering a hady and becoming halal is legislated to attain deliverance. And becoming halal gives deliverance from the enemy, not from illness. And our proof is that, according to the consensus of the people of language, the verse of ihsar was revealed concerning ihsar due to illness, because the people of language said that ihsar occurs due to illness, and hasr due to an enemy. And becoming halal before the time is to remove the hardship that will come due to the prolongation of ihram, while the hardship of forbearance upon ihram with illness is much greater. Explanation: If a muhrim is prevented from performing the acts of Hajj or Umrah due to fear of an enemy, or is afflicted with ihsar due to some illness, then it is permissible for him to become halal without performing the acts of Hajj or Umrah. And Imam Shafi'i said that ihsar only occurs from an enemy, not from illness etc. This is also the saying of Imam Malik. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is the saying of Allah ta'ala: 'But if you are prevented, then [send] whatever offering is easy' (al-Baqarah 2:196), meaning (If you are prevented, then whatever sacrifice is easily available). This was revealed concerning ihsar. That is, when the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and his Companions were prevented by the enemies of Islam at Hudaybiyyah, then this verse was revealed, the summary of which is to slaughter a sacrificial animal and become halal. This occasion of revelation indicates that ihsar occurs due to an enemy, not due to illness. The second proof is that for the muhsar, slaughtering a hady and becoming halal is legislated so that deliverance is attained. And becoming halal gives deliverance from the enemy, not from illness, because becoming halal does not remove illness. Rather, protection from the enemy is achieved; thus it is known that ihsar is specific to the enemy. Our proof is that the verse of ihsar was revealed concerning ihsar due to illness, and there is consensus of all the people of language on this. The people of language said: the word ihsar is used for being prevented due to illness, and the word hasr is used for being prevented due to an enemy. Thus, being prevented due to illness is established by the verse, and being prevented due to an enemy is established by the hadith (the incident of Hudaybiyyah). So ihsar did not remain specific to the enemy, as Imam Shafi'i says; rather, ihsar occurs due to both enemy and illness. And from [the phrase] 'and becoming halal before...' etc. there is a second proof. Its summary is that we accept that the verse of ihsar was revealed concerning the enemy, but illness is annexed to the enemy. That is, the permission for the muhsar to become halal before the time is to remove the hardship that arises from the prolongation of the term and the length of ihram, and the hardship of forbearance upon ihram with illness is greater than the hardship of ihsar due to the enemy. Because in illness, the abundance of medicine and treatment and the helplessness of limbs are apparent. So when ihsar due to the enemy was accepted to remove the lesser hardship, then consideration of ihsar due to illness to remove the greater hardship is all the more appropriate.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the definition of ihsar (being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah). The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: it is permissible for a muhrim to become halal (exit ihram) if prevented by an enemy or by illness. Then he presents the view of Imam Shafi'i (and also Imam Malik) that ihsar only applies to prevention by an enemy, not by illness. The Shafi'i proof is that the verse 'fa-in uhsirtum' was revealed regarding the incident of Hudaybiyyah, where the Prophet and his Companions were blocked by the Quraysh. The Shafi'is argue that tahallul is a rukhsa (concession) to escape the enemy, and illness does not provide a similar escape. The Hanafi response is threefold: (1) According to the consensus of lexicographers, the word 'ihsar' in Arabic is used for prevention due to illness, while 'hasr' is used for prevention by an enemy. Thus the verse includes illness. (2) The verse's occasion of revelation does not restrict its general meaning ('ibrah bi 'umum al-lafz la bi khusus al-sabab). (3) By logical analogy (qiyas awlawi): if tahallul is permitted for the lesser hardship of enemy prevention, it is even more warranted for the greater hardship of illness. The passage concludes that the Hanafi view is stronger.

Key Terms
احصار (ihsar): Being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah, whether by enemy or illness, according to Hanafis.
حصر (hasr): Prevention by an enemy, distinguished from 'ihsar' by some linguists.
تحلل (tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram before completing the rites, permitted for a muhsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic distinction between 'ihsar' and 'hasr' according to the Hanafi school?
A) Ihsar is used for prevention by illness; hasr for prevention by enemy.
B) Ihsar is used for prevention by enemy; hasr for prevention by illness.
C) Both terms are synonymous and mean prevention by any cause.
D) Ihsar refers to prevention inside the Haram; hasr outside.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines ihsar broadly to include both enemy and illness, using linguistic consensus and qiyas awlawi as proofs, contrary to the Shafi'i view.

The Muhsar's Path to Tahallul: Sending the Hady and the Ruling on Shaving
Ruling on sending hady to Haram and dispute on shaving for muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the wajib procedure for a muhsar to become halal, distinguish the Hanafi majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) from Abu Yusuf's view on shaving, and apply the evidence from the Quran and the nature of qurbah.

Core Idea
The muhsar must send a hady to the Haram; shaving is not wajib.

When a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah (muhsar), the path to release (tahallul) involves sending a sacrificial animal to the Haram. But what exactly is required? Must the animal be sent specifically to Mecca? Is shaving the head also obligatory? In this passage, the commentator unfolds the procedure, citing the Quran, responding to Imam al-Shafi'i, and detailing an internal Hanafi difference between the two imams and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances textual evidence with the concession of tahallul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling for the muhsar
Read the first part: 'It is permissible for the muhsar to become halal... Send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram.' Note that sending a hady to the Haram is the key wajib action for tahallul. Why must it be in the Haram?
The phrase 'ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ' (then become halal) appears after sending the hady, not after shaving.
2
Trace the evidence for sending to the Haram
The commentary cites Surah al-Baqarah 2:196 'until the hady reaches its place of sacrifice'. Understand the Hanafi argument: 'hady' means what is sent to the Haram, so the animal must reach the Haram. Also, the act of slaughter (damm al-ihsar) is a qurbah that only takes effect in a sacred time or place.
Compare with the Shafi'i counter-argument that tahallul is a concession and should not be restricted.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i dispute and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argued that restriction defeats the purpose of alleviation. The Hanafi response: the essence of alleviation is preserved, not the limit. The concession still applies, but the qurbah must be valid. This exemplifies a usul principle: rukhsah does not override the nature of the act of worship.
The disagreement is about the definition of rukhsah and its scope.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on shaving
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that shaving/trimming is not wajib for the muhsar. Abu Yusuf says it is wajib, but if omitted, nothing is due (i.e., it is a strong sunnah). The majority view is based on shaving being a devotion that follows the acts of Hajj, not preceding them. The Prophet's shaving at Hudaybiyyah was to demonstrate resolve, not a legal requirement.
Note the practical difference: a muhsar following Abu Hanifa only sends the hady; one following Abu Yusuf would also shave (but without penalty if omitted).
5
Extract practical details: type of animal and sending value
Any animal valid for sacrifice (sheep, cow, camel) suffices; the lowest (sheep) is mentioned. Also, you may send the value (price) of the animal to be bought and slaughtered at the Haram, not the exact animal itself, due to difficulty.
This shows the school's practicality: qiyas with udhiyah (sacrificial animals) and concession for hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محصر کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے، اور اس کی صورت وَإِذَا جَازَلَهُ التَّحَلُلُ يُقَالُ لَهُ إِبْعَثُ شَاةً تُذْبَحُ فِي الْحَرَمِ وَوَاعِدُ مَنْ تَبْعَثُهُ بِيَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ يَذْبَحُ فِيْهِ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ وَإِنَّمَا يَبْعَثُ إِلَى الْحَرَمِ لِأَنَّ دَمَ الْإِحْصَارِ قُرُبَةٌ وَالْإِرَاقَةُ لَمْ تُعْرَفْ قُرْبَةً إِلَّا فِي زَمَانٍ أَوْ مَكَانٍ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ فَلَا يَقَعُ قُرْبَةً دُونَهُ فَلَا يَقَعُ بِهِ التَّحَلُلْ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى (وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُؤُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى مَحِلَّهُ) فَإِنَّ الْهَدَى اسْمٌ لِمَا يُهْدَى إِلَى الْحَرَمِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُتَوَفَّتُ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ رُخْصَةً وَالتَّوْقِيتُ يُبْطِلُ التَّخْفِيفَ قُلْنَا الْمُرَاعَى أَصْلُ التَّخْفِيفِ لَا نِهَايَتُهُ وَيَجُوزُ الشَّاةُ لِأَنَّ الْمَنْصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ الْهَدَى وَ الشَّاةُ أَدْنَاهُ وَتُجْزِيْهِ الْبَقَرَةُ وَالْبُدْنَةُ كَمَا فِي الصَّحَايَا وَلَيْسَ الْمُرَادُ بِمَا ذَكَرْنَا بَعْتُ الشَّاةِ بِعَيْنِهَا لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ قَدْ يَتَعَذَّرُ بَلْ لَهُ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِالْقِيمَةِ حَتَّى تُشْتَرَى الشَّاةُ هُنَالِكَ وَتُذْبَحُ عَنْهُ وَقَوْلُهُ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَلْقُ أَوِ التَّقْصِيرُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَفْعَلُ لَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حَلَقَ عَامَ الْحَدِيبِيَّةِ وَ كَانَ مُحْصَرًا بِهَا وَأَمَرَ أَصْحَابَهُ بِذَلِكَ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْحَلْقَ إِنَّمَا عُرِفَ قُرْبَةً مُرَتَّبًا عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ فَلَا يَكُونُ نُسُكًا قَبْلَهَا وَفِعْلُ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَا مُ وَ أَصْحَابِهِ لِيُعْرَفَ اسْتِحْكَامُ عَزِيمَتِهِمْ عَلَى الْانْصِرَامِ
It is permissible for the muhsar to become halal, and its form: When tahallul is permissible for him, he is told: Send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and appoint with the one you send a specific day on which he will slaughter it, then become halal. And he sends it to the Haram because the blood of ihsar is a devotion, and the shedding of blood is not known as devotion except in a time or place, as has passed; so it does not occur as devotion without it, and tahallul does not occur with it. And to this is the indication in the saying of Allah ta'ala: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place of sacrifice.' For 'hady' is a name for what is sent to the Haram. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not restricted by time, because it is legislated as a concession, and restriction nullifies the alleviation. We say: The consideration is the essence of alleviation, not its limit. And a sheep is permissible because the prescribed thing is hady, and a sheep is its lowest [form]. And a cow and a camel suffice for him, as in the case of sacrifices. And what we mentioned is not intended to be sending the exact sheep, because that may be difficult; rather, he may send its value so that a sheep is bought there and slaughtered on his behalf. And his saying 'then become halal' indicates that he is not obligated to shave or shorten [hair]. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He is obligated to do that, and if he does not do it, nothing is upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved in the year of Hudaybiyyah while he was muhsar there, and he commanded his Companions to do that. And for the two of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), shaving is only known as a devotion arranged upon the acts of Hajj, so it is not a ritual before them, and the action of the Prophet and his Companions was so that their firm resolve to depart would be known.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed ruling of what a muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah) must do to become halal. It begins by quoting Al-Quduri's text (the matn): 'When tahallul is permissible for him, he is told: Send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram...' Then the commentary expands. First, it explains that the sacrificial animal must be sent to the Haram (Mecca or its vicinity) because the act of slaughter is a devotion (qurbah) that only attains its sacred character within the Haram or at the prescribed time. The verse 'Do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place of slaughter' is cited as evidence; 'hady' specifically means what is sent to the Haram. A brief inter-madhhab dispute follows: Imam al-Shafi'i argued that specifying the Haram is not required because tahallul is a concession, and restrictions would defeat the purpose of alleviation. The Hanafi response is that the essence of alleviation is preserved, not its extremity; the concession still exists but within the sacred framework. Next, the type of animal is discussed: any animal valid for hady (sheep, cow, camel) suffices, and the lowest category (sheep) is permissible. Importantly, the muhsar may send the value of the animal rather than the animal itself, to buy it at the Haram. Finally, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that shaving or trimming hair is not obligatory (wajib) for the muhsar; only sending the hady is required. Abu Yusuf, citing the Prophet's action at Hudaybiyyah, considers it wajib, but with the concession that if omitted, nothing is due (i.e., it is sunnah). The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is a devotion tied to the completion of Hajj rites and thus cannot be performed before those rites. The Prophet's shaving was to demonstrate firm resolve, not a legal requirement.

Key Terms
ہدی (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for the purpose of tahallul during Hajj or Umrah.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head; part of the rites of Hajj/Umrah after completing the acts.
تقصیر (taqsir): Shortening the hair; alternative to shaving in the rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position on whether a muhsar must shave or trim his hair to become halal?
A) It is wajib, and if omitted, the tahallul is invalid.
B) It is not wajib; only sending the hady to the Haram is required.
C) It is wajib but can be substituted by sending extra hady.
D) It is optional; the muhsar may choose to shave or not.

Key Takeaway
For a muhsar, sending a hady to the Haram is wajib; shaving the head is not required according to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contra Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i on location.

The Muhsir's Hadi: Must It Be Sent to the Haram?
Presents Hanafi position on muhsir's hadi and rebuts Shafi'i objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on where the muhsir's hadi must be slaughtered and explain the proof from Quran 2:196, and then rebut the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The muhsir's hadi must reach the Haram because blood is worship only when tied to a specific place.

The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling that a muhsir must send a sacrificial animal to the Haram to become halal. This is rooted in the Quranic verse (2:196) and the principle that the shedding of blood is only an act of worship when connected to a specific time or place. Imam al-Shafi'i objects, arguing that the concession of ihsar should not be restricted. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi proof and the response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sending a hadi (sacrifice) for the muhsir. The ruling in the Hanafi school: wajib.
The hadi must be sent to the Haram.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:196: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' The word 'mahill' is interpreted as the Haram.
Also the linguistic meaning of 'hadi' is something sent to the Haram.
3
Interpret the linguistic and rational basis
The shedding of blood is only an act of worship when attached to a specific time (Day of Nahr) or place (Haram). Without specification, it is not worship and does not effect tahallul.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the hadi is a concession (rukhsah), and specifying the Haram defeats the alleviation. He allows slaughter anywhere.
His proof is the spirit of the law, not a specific text.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The basis of alleviation is observed (the muhsir is excused from completing Hajj), but the extreme limit of alleviation is not. The concession is that he becomes halal by sending a sacrifice; there is no further concession regarding location.
Thus the Haram remains required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى الحرم لأنَّ دَمَ الْإِحْصَارِ قُرُبَةٌ وَالْإِرَاقَةُ لَمْ تُعْرَتْ قُرْبَةً إِلَّا فِي زَمَانِ أَوْ مَكَانَ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فَلا يَقَعُ قُرُبَةٌ دُونَهُ فَلَا يَقَعُ بِهِ التَّحَلُلْ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تَخْلُقُوا رُءُ وَسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الهَدَى مَحِلَّهُ) فَإِنَّ الْهَدَى اِسْمٌ لِمَا يُهُدَى إِلَى الْحَرَمِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُتَوَّفَّتُ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ رُحْصَةً وَالتَّوْقِيتُ يَبْطُلُ التَّخْفِيفَ قُلْنَا الْمُرَاعِي أَصْلُ التَّخْفِيفِ لَا نِهَايَتُهُ وَيَجُوزُ الشَّاة لأنَّ المَنصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ الْهَدَى وَ الشَّاةُ أدْنَاهُ وَتُجْزِيْهِ الْبَقَرَةُ وَالْبُدْنَةُ كَمَا فِي الصّحَايَا وَلَيْسَ الْمُرَادُ بِمَا ذَكَرُنَا بَعْتُ الشَّاةِ بِعَيْنِهَا لأن ذَلِكَ قَدْ يَتَعَدَّرُ بَلْ لَهُ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِالْقِيمَةِ حَتَّى تُشْتَرى الشَّاةُ هُنَالِكَ وَتُذْبَحُ عَنْهُ وَقَوْلُهُ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلى أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَلْقُ أوِ التَّقْصِيرُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّد وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفٌ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَفْعَلُ لَا شَيْ ءٍ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حَلَقَ عَامَ الْحَدِيبِيَّةِ وَ كَانَ مُحَصَّرًا بِهَا وَأَمَرَ أَصْحَابَهُ بِذلِكَ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْحَلْقَ إِنَّمَا عُرِفَ قُرُبَةً مُرْتَبًا عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجَ فَلَا يَكُونُ نُسْكًا قَبْلَهَا وَفِعْلُ النّبي عَلَيْهِ السَّلام وَ أَصْحَابُهُ لِيُعْرَف استحكام عزيمتهم على الانصرام
ترجمہ اور جب اس کو حلال ہونا جائز ہو گیا تو اس کو کہا جائے گا کہ ایک بکری بھیج جو حرم میں ذبح کی جائے۔ اور جس کے ہاتھ ہندی بھیجے اس سے ایک متعین دن کا وعدہ ظہر الے کہ اسی دن وہ ہدی ذبح کرے گا پھر حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اور حرم میں اس لئے بھیجی جائے گی کہ احصار کی قربانی ایک عبادت ہے۔ اور خون بہانے کا عبادت ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا مگر زمانہ میں یا مکان میں ۔ جیسا کہ گذر چکا۔ پس بغیر زمان ومکان کے وہ عبادت نہ ہوگا۔ پس اس سے حلال ہونا بھی واقع نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرف باری تعالیٰ کے قول وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُؤْسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى مَحِلَّه میں اشارہ ہے کیونکہ ہدی اس کا نام ہے جس کو حرم میں بھیجا جائے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ہدی کی تعیین حرم کے ساتھ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی مشروعیت تو رخصت کے طور پر ہے۔ اور تعیین تخفیف کو باطل کر دیتی ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اصل تخفیف تو ملحوظ رکھی گئی ہے لیکن انتہائے تخفیف ملحوظ نہیں رکھی گئی اور بکری جائز ہے کیونکہ منصوص علیہ بدی ہے۔ اور بکری ہدی کا متر درجہ ہے۔ اور اس کو گائے اور اونٹ بھی کافی ہے جیسا کہ انحیہ واجبہ میں ہے۔ اور جو ہم نے ذکر کیا اس سے مراد متعین طور پر بکری کو بھیجنا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ کبھی مستعد رہوتا ہے بلکہ اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ قیمت بھیج دے تا کہ وہاں بکری خرید کر اس کو ذبح کرے۔ اور قدوری کا قول ثم تخلل اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اس پر حلق یا قصر واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ قول ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس پر یہ واجب ہے۔ اور گر اس نے یہ نہ کیا تو اس پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حدیبیہ کے سال حلق کیا ہے حالانکہ آپ حدیبیہ میں مصر تھے ۔ اور اپنے صحابہ کو بھی اس کا حکم دیا اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق کا عبادت ہوتا افعال حج پر مرتب ہو کر معلوم ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ افعال حج سے پہلے نسک نہ ہوگا۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ کا سرمنڈانا اس لئے تھا تا کہ واپس جانے پر ان کے عزم کا مستحکم ہونا معلوم ہو جائے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، جب عصر کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہو گیا تو محصر سے کہا جائے گا کہ ایک بکری بھیج دے تا کہ وہ حرم میں ذبح کی جائے اور جس کے ہاتھ ہدی بھیجے اس سے ایک دن معین کا وعدہ کر لے کہ اس دن ذبح کرے گا پھر حلال ہو جائے گا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ ہدی ذبیح کرنے کے لئے دن متعین کرنا ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار کے لئے کوئی دن متعین نہیں ہے پس دن متعین کرنے کار عده امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس لئے ہوگا تا کہ مصر کو اپنے حلال ہونے کا وقت معلوم ہو ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ دم احصار حج کے اندر یوم خر کے ساتھ متعین ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک دن متعین کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے ہاں البتہ عمرہ کے اندر ان کے
نزدیک بھی دن متعین کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی۔ محصر نے جب دم احصار بھیج دیا تو اب اس کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اسی جگہ ٹھہرا ر ہے یا وطن واپس چلا جائے پھر جب متعینہ دن آگیا اور اس کو یقین ہو گیا کہ ہدی ذبح کر دی گئی ہو گی تو اب اس کو وہ تمام امور کرنے کی اجازت ہے جو حلال کرتا ہے ۔
(البقرة: 4 )
بہر حال صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کا یہ جانور حرم میں بھیجا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دم احصار قربت وعبادت ہے۔ اور خون بہانے کا قربت ہونا اسی صورت میں معلوم ہوا ہے جبکہ وہ کسی زمان یا مکان کے ساتھ خاص ہو۔ پس بغیر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کے خون بہانا عبادت نہ ہوگا اور جب بغیر حرم کے خون بہانا عبادت نہیں ہوا تو اس سے مصر حلال بھی نہ ہوگا۔ قرآن پاک میں بھی مکان کی تعیین کی طرف اشارہ ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُهُ وَسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى مَحِلَّهُ (191) ۔ پھر حل کی تفسیر کی گئی چنانچہ فرمایا ثُمَّ مَحِلُّهَا إِلَى الْبَيْتِ الْعَتيق (الحج: ۳۵) اور مراد عین بیت نہیں ہے کیونکہ معین بیت میں خون نہیں بہایا جاتا۔ پس اس ہے مراد حرم ہو گا ۔ اب ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ سر منڈا کر حلال مت ہو یہاں تک کہ ہدی حرم میں پہنچ جائے ۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ ہدی کے جانور کا حرم کے اندر ذبح کرنا ضروری ہے۔ نیز قرآن میں لفظ ہدی آیا ہے اور ہدی اسی کو کہتے ہیں جس کو حرم میں پہنچادیا جائے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہدی کو حرم کے ساتھ خاص کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ہدی کا جانور بھیج کر حلال ہو جانا مصر کے لئے شریعت نے رخصت پیدا کی ہے۔ اور حرم کے ساتھ متعین کرنا اس تخفیف اور رخصت کو باطل کرتا ہے اس لئے ہدی حرم کے ساتھ متعین نہ ہوگی ، بلکہ حمل اور حرم ہر جگہ ذبح کی جاسکتی ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اصل تخفیف تو ملحوظ ہے مگر انتہائے تخفیف ملحوظ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی ایک تخفیف پیدا کر دی گئی کہ مصر ہدی کا جانور ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور اب اس کے بعد تخفیف نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کے اندر بکری جائز ہے کیونکہ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى ، آیت میں ہدی کا لفظ منصوص ہے۔ اور ہدی کا کمتر درجہ بکری ہے اس لئے بکری کا بھیجنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور پوری گائے اور پورا اونٹ بھی جائز ہے اور ان کا ساتواں حصہ بھی جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ بقر عید میں پوری گائے اور پورا اونٹ اور ان کا ساتواں حصہ جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خاص طور پر بکری کا بھیجنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر قیمت بھیج دی اور حرم میں اس سے بکری خرید کر ذبح کر دی تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ بسا اوقات بکری کا بھیجنا ستعد رہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ مصر پر حلال ہونے کے لئے حلق یا قصر کرانا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی طرفین کا قول ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ مصر پر یہ واجب ہے لیکن اگر حلق یا قصر نہ کرایا تو دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اگر چہ ترک واجب کا گناہ ہوا۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدیبیہ کے سال رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حلق کرایا ہے حالانکہ آپ حدیبیہ میں مخصر تھے اور صحا بہ گو بھی حلق کا امر فرمایا ہے ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حلال ہونے کے لئے ہدی ذبح کرنا کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ ذبح کے بعد حلق یا قصر کرانا بھی ضروری ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق ایسی قربت و عبادت ہے جو افعال حج پر مرتب ہوتی ہے۔ افعال حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے حلق حج کا
[The animal must be sent] to the Haram because the blood of ihsar is an act of worship, and the shedding of blood is not known to be an act of worship except in a specific time or place, as has passed. So it does not become an act of worship without that, and thus tahallul does not occur by it. And to this is the indication by His statement, the Exalted: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' For hadi is a name for what is sent to the Haram. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not specified with it (the Haram) because it was legislated as a concession, and specification nullifies the alleviation. We say: The basis of alleviation is observed, not its extreme. And the sheep is permissible because what is textually mentioned is hadi, and the sheep is its lowest. And the cow and the camel suffice, as in the sacrificial animals. And what we mentioned does not mean sending a specific sheep, because that may be difficult; rather, he may send its value so that a sheep is purchased there and slaughtered on his behalf. And his statement 'then he becomes halal' is an indication that shaving or trimming is not required upon him. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: That is required upon him, and if he does not do it, nothing is upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved in the year of Hudaybiyyah while he was a muhsir there, and he commanded his companions to do that. And for them both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is only known as an act of worship attached to the actions of Hajj, so it does not become a ritual before them. And the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions was to demonstrate the strength of their determination to depart.
Translation: And when becoming halal becomes permissible for him, he will be told to send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. And from the one with whom he sends the hadi, he takes a promise on a specific day that he will slaughter the hadi on that day, then he becomes halal. And it will be sent to the Haram because the sacrifice of ihsar is an act of worship. And shedding blood is not known to be worship except in a time or place, as has passed. So without time and place it will not be worship. Therefore, becoming halal by it will not occur. And to this is the indication in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place.' Because hadi is the name for what is sent to the Haram. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: Specifying the hadi with the Haram is not valid because its legislation is as a concession, and specification invalidates the alleviation. We say: The basis of alleviation is observed, but its extreme is not observed. And a sheep is permissible because what is textually mentioned is hadi, and the sheep is the lowest level of hadi. And a cow and a camel also suffice, as in obligatory sacrifices. And what we mentioned does not mean sending a specific sheep, because that may sometimes be difficult; rather, it is permissible for him to send the price so that a sheep is purchased there and slaughtered for him. And al-Quduri's statement 'then he becomes halal' indicates that shaving or trimming is not required upon him. And this is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: This is required upon him, and if he does not do it, nothing is upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved in the year of Hudaybiyyah while he was a muhsir there, and he commanded his companions to do that. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is known to be an act of worship only when attached to the actions of Hajj, so it will not be a ritual before them. And the shaving of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions was so that their determination to depart would be known to be strong.
Explanation of the issue: When becoming halal for the muhsir becomes permissible, the muhsir will be told to send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and from the one with whom he sends the hadi, he makes a promise on a specific day that he will slaughter on that day, then he becomes halal. Note that specifying a day for slaughtering the hadi is the statement of Abu Hanifa, because in his view there is no specific day for the blood of ihsar. So specifying a day in the view of Imam Sahib is so that the muhsir knows the time of his tahallul. And in the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since the blood of ihsar is specified with the Day of Nahr in Hajj, there is no need for specifying a day. However, in Umrah, even in their view, the need for specifying a day will arise. When the muhsir has sent the blood of ihsar, he has the choice to stay in that place or return to his homeland. Then when the specified day arrives and he is certain that the hadi has been slaughtered, he is permitted to do all the things that a halal person does.
In any case, the author of al-Hidayah says: This animal of hadi will be sent to the Haram, because the blood of ihsar is an act of worship and devotion. And shedding blood is known to be devotion only when it is specific to a time or place. So without either of these two, shedding blood is not worship. And when shedding blood without the Haram is not worship, then the muhsir will not become halal by it. In the Holy Quran also there is an indication of specifying the place, as He said: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' Then the explanation of the place was given, as He said: 'Then their place is to the Ancient House.' But the intended meaning is not the exact House, because blood is not shed inside the exact House. So the intended meaning is the Haram. Now the translation would be: Do not become halal by shaving your head until the hadi reaches the Haram. From this it is also known that it is necessary to slaughter the animal of hadi inside the Haram. Also, the word 'hadi' appears in the Quran, and 'hadi' is called what is delivered to the Haram. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Specifying the hadi with the Haram is not correct, because becoming halal by sending the animal of hadi is a concession created by Shariah for the muhsir. And specifying it with the Haram invalidates this alleviation and concession. Therefore, the hadi will not be specified with the Haram; rather, it can be slaughtered in both the Hill and the Haram. Our answer to this is that the basis of alleviation is observed, but its extreme is not observed. That is, one alleviation was created: that the muhsir becomes halal by slaughtering the animal of hadi, and after that there is no further alleviation. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the hadi, a sheep is permissible because in the verse 'whatever is available of the hadi' the word 'hadi' is mentioned, and the lowest level of hadi is a sheep, so sending a sheep is permissible. And a whole cow and a whole camel are also permissible, and a seventh share of them is also permissible, as in the Eid sacrifice, a whole cow and a whole camel and a seventh share are permissible. The author of al-Hidayah says that specifically sending a sheep is not necessary; rather, if he sends the price and a sheep is bought in the Haram and slaughtered, that is also permissible because sometimes sending a sheep is difficult. The author of al-Hidayah says that al-Quduri's statement 'then he becomes halal' indicates that for the muhsir to become halal, shaving or trimming is not required. And this is the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf says that this is required upon the muhsir, but if he does not shave or trim, nothing (like a dam) becomes required, although he sins for leaving a wajib.
The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that in the year of Hudaybiyyah, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had his head shaved while he was a muhsir in Hudaybiyyah, and he commanded his companions to shave. This shows that slaughtering the hadi is not sufficient for becoming halal; rather, after slaughter, shaving or trimming is also necessary. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is a devotion and worship that is attached to the actions of Hajj. Before performing the actions of Hajj, shaving [of Hajj]...

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings for a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah) and how he becomes halal (released from ihram). The central issue is the requirement of sending a sacrificial animal (hadi) to the Haram and whether shaving the head (halq) or trimming (taqsir) is also necessary. The commentary follows the order of the text:

1. The muhsir must send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. The reason given is that the blood of ihsar is an act of worship (qurbah), and shedding blood is only recognized as worship when tied to a specific time (the Day of Nahr) or place (the Haram). Without this specification, the shedding of blood does not constitute worship and thus does not effect tahallul. This is supported by the Quranic verse (2:196): 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' The word 'hadi' linguistically refers to what is sent to the Haram.

2. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the hadi should not be restricted to the Haram. He views the legislation of the hadi for the muhsir as a concession (rukhsah), and restricting it to the Haram would defeat the purpose of alleviation. The Hanafi response, given by the author of al-Hidayah, is that the basis of alleviation is observed (i.e., the muhsir is excused from completing Hajj), but the extreme limit of alleviation is not observed. In other words, the concession is that the muhsir can become halal by sending a sacrifice; there is no further concession regarding the location. Thus the sacrifice must be in the Haram.

3. The type of animal: a sheep suffices because it is the minimum mentioned in the Quran ('hadi'). A cow or camel, or even a seventh share of them, is also valid, analogous to sacrificial animals for Eid and obligatory sacrifices.

4. The muhsir may send the monetary value of a sheep instead of the animal itself, so that a sheep can be purchased and slaughtered on his behalf in the Haram. This is a practical concession to avoid difficulty in sending an animal.

5. The Hanafi ikhtilaf on halq/taqsir: The phrase 'thumma tahlala' (then he becomes halal) indicates that the muhsir does not need to shave or trim his hair. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their reasoning is that shaving is an act of worship connected to the actions of Hajj (like after completing the rituals); before those actions, shaving is not a valid ritual. The Prophet's and companions' shaving at Hudaybiyyah was not to effect tahallul but to demonstrate their resolve to return.

6. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that the muhsir must shave or trim after sending the sacrifice. He cites the action of the Prophet at Hudaybiyyah as evidence. However, he agrees that if the muhsir omits this, nothing (like a dam) is due; he simply sins.

7. Additional points: Abu Hanifa requires specifying a day for the slaughter of the hadi because in his view the blood of ihsar is not tied to a specific day. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, as they consider the blood of ihsar bound to the Day of Nahr in Hajj, but for Umrah they also require a specified day. Once the muhsir sends the sacrifice and the appointed day arrives, he has certainty that it was slaughtered and may then do all things permissible for a non-muhrim.

The passage is a clear example of the Hanafi method of combining textual evidence (Quran, Hadith) with rational argument (istihsan) and intra-madhhab reasoning.

Key Terms
إِحْصَارَ (ihsār): Being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other obstacle after entering ihram.
هَدْيَ (hady): A sacrificial animal (sheep, cow, camel) sent to the Haram as an offering, specifically for the muhsir or for tamattu'/qiran.
مُحْصَرُ (muḥṣar): A person who has entered ihram for Hajj or Umrah and is prevented from completing it due to enemy or overwhelming force.
تَحَلَّلْ (taḥallul): The state of being released from ihram, i.e., becoming halal (permitted to do what was prohibited in ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), where must the muhsir's hadi be slaughtered?
A) Anywhere the muhsir is located
B) Only in the Haram (Mecca and its sacred precincts)
C) In the nearest mosque
D) At the site of ihsar, regardless of location

Key Takeaway
The muhsir's hadi must be slaughtered in the Haram to effect tahallul; sending the value is allowed.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Is Halq (Shaving) Required for the Muhsir's Tahallul?
Presents intra-Hanafi dispute on whether halq/taqsir is required for the muhsir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether shaving is required for the muhsir, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Shaving is a ritual of Hajj completion; the muhsir becomes halal by sacrifice alone, not by shaving.

After discussing the hadi, al-Hidayah turns to whether the muhsir must shave or trim his hair. The phrase 'then he becomes halal' (from al-Quduri) indicates, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, that no hair removal is required. Abu Yusuf, however, holds it is wajib based on the Prophet's action at Hudaybiyyah. This lesson explores the reasoning of both sides and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: halq/taqsir is not required. The muhsir becomes halal by sending the hadi alone.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved at Hudaybiyyah while muhsir and commanded his companions to do so. This indicates halq is part of tahallul.
Abu Yusuf uses this as a textual proof.
3
Analyze the majority's response
Shaving is a ritual attached to the actions of Hajj; it cannot be performed before those actions. The Prophet's action was to demonstrate resolve, not as a ritual requirement.
The majority also notes that the Prophet's action is not a command in the sense of wujub.
4
Determine the practical consequence
According to the majority, the muhsir simply sends the hadi and becomes halal. According to Abu Yusuf, he must also shave, but if he omits, no dam is due, only sin.
The sin is for leaving a wajib, but no compensation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon view. It is simpler and avoids potential unnecessary ritual.
Fatwa is given on this view.

إلى الحرم لأنَّ دَمَ الْإِحْصَارِ قُرُبَةٌ وَالْإِرَاقَةُ لَمْ تُعْرَتْ قُرْبَةً إِلَّا فِي زَمَانِ أَوْ مَكَانَ عَلَى مَامَرَّ فَلا يَقَعُ قُرُبَةٌ دُونَهُ فَلَا يَقَعُ بِهِ التَّحَلُلْ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَلَا تَخْلُقُوا رُءُ وَسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الهَدَى مَحِلَّهُ) فَإِنَّ الْهَدَى اِسْمٌ لِمَا يُهُدَى إِلَى الْحَرَمِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لَا يُتَوَّفَّتُ بِهِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ رُحْصَةً وَالتَّوْقِيتُ يَبْطُلُ التَّخْفِيفَ قُلْنَا الْمُرَاعِي أَصْلُ التَّخْفِيفِ لَا نِهَايَتُهُ وَيَجُوزُ الشَّاة لأنَّ المَنصُوصَ عَلَيْهِ الْهَدَى وَ الشَّاةُ أدْنَاهُ وَتُجْزِيْهِ الْبَقَرَةُ وَالْبُدْنَةُ كَمَا فِي الصّحَايَا وَلَيْسَ الْمُرَادُ بِمَا ذَكَرُنَا بَعْتُ الشَّاةِ بِعَيْنِهَا لأن ذَلِكَ قَدْ يَتَعَدَّرُ بَلْ لَهُ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِالْقِيمَةِ حَتَّى تُشْتَرى الشَّاةُ هُنَالِكَ وَتُذْبَحُ عَنْهُ وَقَوْلُهُ ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلى أَنَّهُ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَلْقُ أوِ التَّقْصِيرُ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّد وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفٌ عَلَيْهِ ذَلِكَ وَلَوْ لَمْ يَفْعَلُ لَا شَيْ ءٍ عَلَيْهِ لأنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ حَلَقَ عَامَ الْحَدِيبِيَّةِ وَ كَانَ مُحَصَّرًا بِهَا وَأَمَرَ أَصْحَابَهُ بِذلِكَ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الْحَلْقَ إِنَّمَا عُرِفَ قُرُبَةً مُرْتَبًا عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجَ فَلَا يَكُونُ نُسْكًا قَبْلَهَا وَفِعْلُ النّبي عَلَيْهِ السَّلام وَ أَصْحَابُهُ لِيُعْرَف استحكام عزيمتهم على الانصرام
ترجمہ اور جب اس کو حلال ہونا جائز ہو گیا تو اس کو کہا جائے گا کہ ایک بکری بھیج جو حرم میں ذبح کی جائے۔ اور جس کے ہاتھ ہندی بھیجے اس سے ایک متعین دن کا وعدہ ظہر الے کہ اسی دن وہ ہدی ذبح کرے گا پھر حلال ہو جائے گا۔ اور حرم میں اس لئے بھیجی جائے گی کہ احصار کی قربانی ایک عبادت ہے۔ اور خون بہانے کا عبادت ہونا معلوم نہیں ہوا مگر زمانہ میں یا مکان میں ۔ جیسا کہ گذر چکا۔ پس بغیر زمان ومکان کے وہ عبادت نہ ہوگا۔ پس اس سے حلال ہونا بھی واقع نہ ہوگا۔ اور اسی طرف باری تعالیٰ کے قول وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُؤْسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى مَحِلَّه میں اشارہ ہے کیونکہ ہدی اس کا نام ہے جس کو حرم میں بھیجا جائے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ ہدی کی تعیین حرم کے ساتھ نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کی مشروعیت تو رخصت کے طور پر ہے۔ اور تعیین تخفیف کو باطل کر دیتی ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اصل تخفیف تو ملحوظ رکھی گئی ہے لیکن انتہائے تخفیف ملحوظ نہیں رکھی گئی اور بکری جائز ہے کیونکہ منصوص علیہ بدی ہے۔ اور بکری ہدی کا متر درجہ ہے۔ اور اس کو گائے اور اونٹ بھی کافی ہے جیسا کہ انحیہ واجبہ میں ہے۔ اور جو ہم نے ذکر کیا اس سے مراد متعین طور پر بکری کو بھیجنا نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ کبھی مستعد رہوتا ہے بلکہ اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ قیمت بھیج دے تا کہ وہاں بکری خرید کر اس کو ذبح کرے۔ اور قدوری کا قول ثم تخلل اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ اس پر حلق یا قصر واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ قول ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد کا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس پر یہ واجب ہے۔ اور گر اس نے یہ نہ کیا تو اس پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حدیبیہ کے سال حلق کیا ہے حالانکہ آپ حدیبیہ میں مصر تھے ۔ اور اپنے صحابہ کو بھی اس کا حکم دیا اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق کا عبادت ہوتا افعال حج پر مرتب ہو کر معلوم ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ افعال حج سے پہلے نسک نہ ہوگا۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ کا سرمنڈانا اس لئے تھا تا کہ واپس جانے پر ان کے عزم کا مستحکم ہونا معلوم ہو جائے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، جب عصر کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہو گیا تو محصر سے کہا جائے گا کہ ایک بکری بھیج دے تا کہ وہ حرم میں ذبح کی جائے اور جس کے ہاتھ ہدی بھیجے اس سے ایک دن معین کا وعدہ کر لے کہ اس دن ذبح کرے گا پھر حلال ہو جائے گا۔ یہ خیال رہے کہ ہدی ذبیح کرنے کے لئے دن متعین کرنا ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار کے لئے کوئی دن متعین نہیں ہے پس دن متعین کرنے کار عده امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس لئے ہوگا تا کہ مصر کو اپنے حلال ہونے کا وقت معلوم ہو ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک چونکہ دم احصار حج کے اندر یوم خر کے ساتھ متعین ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک دن متعین کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے ہاں البتہ عمرہ کے اندر ان کے
نزدیک بھی دن متعین کرنے کی ضرورت پیش آئے گی۔ محصر نے جب دم احصار بھیج دیا تو اب اس کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اسی جگہ ٹھہرا ر ہے یا وطن واپس چلا جائے پھر جب متعینہ دن آگیا اور اس کو یقین ہو گیا کہ ہدی ذبح کر دی گئی ہو گی تو اب اس کو وہ تمام امور کرنے کی اجازت ہے جو حلال کرتا ہے ۔
(البقرة: 4 )
بہر حال صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کا یہ جانور حرم میں بھیجا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ دم احصار قربت وعبادت ہے۔ اور خون بہانے کا قربت ہونا اسی صورت میں معلوم ہوا ہے جبکہ وہ کسی زمان یا مکان کے ساتھ خاص ہو۔ پس بغیر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کے خون بہانا عبادت نہ ہوگا اور جب بغیر حرم کے خون بہانا عبادت نہیں ہوا تو اس سے مصر حلال بھی نہ ہوگا۔ قرآن پاک میں بھی مکان کی تعیین کی طرف اشارہ ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُهُ وَسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدَى مَحِلَّهُ (191) ۔ پھر حل کی تفسیر کی گئی چنانچہ فرمایا ثُمَّ مَحِلُّهَا إِلَى الْبَيْتِ الْعَتيق (الحج: ۳۵) اور مراد عین بیت نہیں ہے کیونکہ معین بیت میں خون نہیں بہایا جاتا۔ پس اس ہے مراد حرم ہو گا ۔ اب ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ سر منڈا کر حلال مت ہو یہاں تک کہ ہدی حرم میں پہنچ جائے ۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ ہدی کے جانور کا حرم کے اندر ذبح کرنا ضروری ہے۔ نیز قرآن میں لفظ ہدی آیا ہے اور ہدی اسی کو کہتے ہیں جس کو حرم میں پہنچادیا جائے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہدی کو حرم کے ساتھ خاص کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ہدی کا جانور بھیج کر حلال ہو جانا مصر کے لئے شریعت نے رخصت پیدا کی ہے۔ اور حرم کے ساتھ متعین کرنا اس تخفیف اور رخصت کو باطل کرتا ہے اس لئے ہدی حرم کے ساتھ متعین نہ ہوگی ، بلکہ حمل اور حرم ہر جگہ ذبح کی جاسکتی ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اصل تخفیف تو ملحوظ ہے مگر انتہائے تخفیف ملحوظ نہیں ہے۔ یعنی ایک تخفیف پیدا کر دی گئی کہ مصر ہدی کا جانور ذبح کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور اب اس کے بعد تخفیف نہیں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہدی کے اندر بکری جائز ہے کیونکہ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى ، آیت میں ہدی کا لفظ منصوص ہے۔ اور ہدی کا کمتر درجہ بکری ہے اس لئے بکری کا بھیجنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور پوری گائے اور پورا اونٹ بھی جائز ہے اور ان کا ساتواں حصہ بھی جائز ہے۔ جیسا کہ بقر عید میں پوری گائے اور پورا اونٹ اور ان کا ساتواں حصہ جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ خاص طور پر بکری کا بھیجنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اگر قیمت بھیج دی اور حرم میں اس سے بکری خرید کر ذبح کر دی تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ بسا اوقات بکری کا بھیجنا ستعد رہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ مصر پر حلال ہونے کے لئے حلق یا قصر کرانا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی طرفین کا قول ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ مصر پر یہ واجب ہے لیکن اگر حلق یا قصر نہ کرایا تو دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اگر چہ ترک واجب کا گناہ ہوا۔
امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدیبیہ کے سال رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حلق کرایا ہے حالانکہ آپ حدیبیہ میں مخصر تھے اور صحا بہ گو بھی حلق کا امر فرمایا ہے ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حلال ہونے کے لئے ہدی ذبح کرنا کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ ذبح کے بعد حلق یا قصر کرانا بھی ضروری ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق ایسی قربت و عبادت ہے جو افعال حج پر مرتب ہوتی ہے۔ افعال حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے حلق حج کا
[The animal must be sent] to the Haram because the blood of ihsar is an act of worship, and the shedding of blood is not known to be an act of worship except in a specific time or place, as has passed. So it does not become an act of worship without that, and thus tahallul does not occur by it. And to this is the indication by His statement, the Exalted: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' For hadi is a name for what is sent to the Haram. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not specified with it (the Haram) because it was legislated as a concession, and specification nullifies the alleviation. We say: The basis of alleviation is observed, not its extreme. And the sheep is permissible because what is textually mentioned is hadi, and the sheep is its lowest. And the cow and the camel suffice, as in the sacrificial animals. And what we mentioned does not mean sending a specific sheep, because that may be difficult; rather, he may send its value so that a sheep is purchased there and slaughtered on his behalf. And his statement 'then he becomes halal' is an indication that shaving or trimming is not required upon him. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: That is required upon him, and if he does not do it, nothing is upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved in the year of Hudaybiyyah while he was a muhsir there, and he commanded his companions to do that. And for them both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is only known as an act of worship attached to the actions of Hajj, so it does not become a ritual before them. And the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions was to demonstrate the strength of their determination to depart.
Translation: And when becoming halal becomes permissible for him, he will be told to send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. And from the one with whom he sends the hadi, he takes a promise on a specific day that he will slaughter the hadi on that day, then he becomes halal. And it will be sent to the Haram because the sacrifice of ihsar is an act of worship. And shedding blood is not known to be worship except in a time or place, as has passed. So without time and place it will not be worship. Therefore, becoming halal by it will not occur. And to this is the indication in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place.' Because hadi is the name for what is sent to the Haram. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: Specifying the hadi with the Haram is not valid because its legislation is as a concession, and specification invalidates the alleviation. We say: The basis of alleviation is observed, but its extreme is not observed. And a sheep is permissible because what is textually mentioned is hadi, and the sheep is the lowest level of hadi. And a cow and a camel also suffice, as in obligatory sacrifices. And what we mentioned does not mean sending a specific sheep, because that may sometimes be difficult; rather, it is permissible for him to send the price so that a sheep is purchased there and slaughtered for him. And al-Quduri's statement 'then he becomes halal' indicates that shaving or trimming is not required upon him. And this is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: This is required upon him, and if he does not do it, nothing is upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) shaved in the year of Hudaybiyyah while he was a muhsir there, and he commanded his companions to do that. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is known to be an act of worship only when attached to the actions of Hajj, so it will not be a ritual before them. And the shaving of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions was so that their determination to depart would be known to be strong.
Explanation of the issue: When becoming halal for the muhsir becomes permissible, the muhsir will be told to send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and from the one with whom he sends the hadi, he makes a promise on a specific day that he will slaughter on that day, then he becomes halal. Note that specifying a day for slaughtering the hadi is the statement of Abu Hanifa, because in his view there is no specific day for the blood of ihsar. So specifying a day in the view of Imam Sahib is so that the muhsir knows the time of his tahallul. And in the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), since the blood of ihsar is specified with the Day of Nahr in Hajj, there is no need for specifying a day. However, in Umrah, even in their view, the need for specifying a day will arise. When the muhsir has sent the blood of ihsar, he has the choice to stay in that place or return to his homeland. Then when the specified day arrives and he is certain that the hadi has been slaughtered, he is permitted to do all the things that a halal person does.
In any case, the author of al-Hidayah says: This animal of hadi will be sent to the Haram, because the blood of ihsar is an act of worship and devotion. And shedding blood is known to be devotion only when it is specific to a time or place. So without either of these two, shedding blood is not worship. And when shedding blood without the Haram is not worship, then the muhsir will not become halal by it. In the Holy Quran also there is an indication of specifying the place, as He said: 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' Then the explanation of the place was given, as He said: 'Then their place is to the Ancient House.' But the intended meaning is not the exact House, because blood is not shed inside the exact House. So the intended meaning is the Haram. Now the translation would be: Do not become halal by shaving your head until the hadi reaches the Haram. From this it is also known that it is necessary to slaughter the animal of hadi inside the Haram. Also, the word 'hadi' appears in the Quran, and 'hadi' is called what is delivered to the Haram. Imam al-Shafi'i said: Specifying the hadi with the Haram is not correct, because becoming halal by sending the animal of hadi is a concession created by Shariah for the muhsir. And specifying it with the Haram invalidates this alleviation and concession. Therefore, the hadi will not be specified with the Haram; rather, it can be slaughtered in both the Hill and the Haram. Our answer to this is that the basis of alleviation is observed, but its extreme is not observed. That is, one alleviation was created: that the muhsir becomes halal by slaughtering the animal of hadi, and after that there is no further alleviation. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the hadi, a sheep is permissible because in the verse 'whatever is available of the hadi' the word 'hadi' is mentioned, and the lowest level of hadi is a sheep, so sending a sheep is permissible. And a whole cow and a whole camel are also permissible, and a seventh share of them is also permissible, as in the Eid sacrifice, a whole cow and a whole camel and a seventh share are permissible. The author of al-Hidayah says that specifically sending a sheep is not necessary; rather, if he sends the price and a sheep is bought in the Haram and slaughtered, that is also permissible because sometimes sending a sheep is difficult. The author of al-Hidayah says that al-Quduri's statement 'then he becomes halal' indicates that for the muhsir to become halal, shaving or trimming is not required. And this is the statement of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf says that this is required upon the muhsir, but if he does not shave or trim, nothing (like a dam) becomes required, although he sins for leaving a wajib.
The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that in the year of Hudaybiyyah, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had his head shaved while he was a muhsir in Hudaybiyyah, and he commanded his companions to shave. This shows that slaughtering the hadi is not sufficient for becoming halal; rather, after slaughter, shaving or trimming is also necessary. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that shaving is a devotion and worship that is attached to the actions of Hajj. Before performing the actions of Hajj, shaving [of Hajj]...
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the rulings for a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah) and how he becomes halal (released from ihram). The central issue is the requirement of sending a sacrificial animal (hadi) to the Haram and whether shaving the head (halq) or trimming (taqsir) is also necessary. The commentary follows the order of the text:

1. The muhsir must send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. The reason given is that the blood of ihsar is an act of worship (qurbah), and shedding blood is only recognized as worship when tied to a specific time (the Day of Nahr) or place (the Haram). Without this specification, the shedding of blood does not constitute worship and thus does not effect tahallul. This is supported by the Quranic verse (2:196): 'And do not shave your heads until the hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice].' The word 'hadi' linguistically refers to what is sent to the Haram.

2. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the hadi should not be restricted to the Haram. He views the legislation of the hadi for the muhsir as a concession (rukhsah), and restricting it to the Haram would defeat the purpose of alleviation. The Hanafi response, given by the author of al-Hidayah, is that the basis of alleviation is observed (i.e., the muhsir is excused from completing Hajj), but the extreme limit of alleviation is not observed. In other words, the concession is that the muhsir can become halal by sending a sacrifice; there is no further concession regarding the location. Thus the sacrifice must be in the Haram.

3. The type of animal: a sheep suffices because it is the minimum mentioned in the Quran ('hadi'). A cow or camel, or even a seventh share of them, is also valid, analogous to sacrificial animals for Eid and obligatory sacrifices.

4. The muhsir may send the monetary value of a sheep instead of the animal itself, so that a sheep can be purchased and slaughtered on his behalf in the Haram. This is a practical concession to avoid difficulty in sending an animal.

5. The Hanafi ikhtilaf on halq/taqsir: The phrase 'thumma tahlala' (then he becomes halal) indicates that the muhsir does not need to shave or trim his hair. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Their reasoning is that shaving is an act of worship connected to the actions of Hajj (like after completing the rituals); before those actions, shaving is not a valid ritual. The Prophet's and companions' shaving at Hudaybiyyah was not to effect tahallul but to demonstrate their resolve to return.

6. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that the muhsir must shave or trim after sending the sacrifice. He cites the action of the Prophet at Hudaybiyyah as evidence. However, he agrees that if the muhsir omits this, nothing (like a dam) is due; he simply sins.

7. Additional points: Abu Hanifa requires specifying a day for the slaughter of the hadi because in his view the blood of ihsar is not tied to a specific day. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, as they consider the blood of ihsar bound to the Day of Nahr in Hajj, but for Umrah they also require a specified day. Once the muhsir sends the sacrifice and the appointed day arrives, he has certainty that it was slaughtered and may then do all things permissible for a non-muhrim.

The passage is a clear example of the Hanafi method of combining textual evidence (Quran, Hadith) with rational argument (istihsan) and intra-madhhab reasoning.

Key Terms
حَلْقَ (halq): Shaving the head, which is normally a ritual act of tahlil (leaving ihram) after completing Hajj. Here discussed whether it is required for the muhsir.
تَقْصِيرُ (taqsīr): Trimming the hair (a shorter length than shaving), an alternative to halq for tahlil.
مُحْصَرُ (muḥṣar): A person who has entered ihram for Hajj or Umrah and is prevented from completing it due to enemy or overwhelming force.
تَحَلَّلْ (taḥallul): The state of being released from ihram, i.e., becoming halal (permitted to do what was prohibited in ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is required for a muhsir to become halal?
A) Sending a hadi to the Haram and shaving the head
B) Sending a hadi to the Haram; shaving is not required
C) Only shaving the head, without sending a hadi
D) Fasting three days instead of sending a hadi

Key Takeaway
The muhsir does not need to shave or trim; he becomes halal by the sacrifice alone.

Sending Hadi to Haram for the Muhsar
Ruling that Muhsar must send Hadi to Haram, with proof and response to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where the Muhsar must slaughter his Hadi, derive it from Quranic evidence, and respond to the Shafi'i objection.

Core Idea
The Muhsar's Hadi must be slaughtered in the Haram—worship through blood requires specification by place.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the Muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj). The central question is: where must the sacrificial animal (Hadi) be slaughtered? The Hanafi school requires it to be within the Haram (sacred precincts of Makkah), based on Quranic verses and the principle that expiatory blood requires a specified time or place. We will unpack the proof, address the Shafi'i objection, and see the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position: the Muhsar must send his Hadi to the Haram and it must be slaughtered there. This is a condition (wajib) for becoming halal (exiting ihram).
The ruling is not that the animal must reach the Kaaba itself, but the Haram.
2
Understand the Usul Principle
The blood of ihsaar (dam al-ihsaar) is an act of worship (qurbah). Worship through bloodshed requires specification with either a time (like Eid al-Adha) or a place (like the Haram). Since no specific time is mentioned for ihsaar, the place becomes decisive.
This is a Hanafi usul principle: 'al-qurbah bi al-dam tuhtaju ila ta'yin al-zaman aw al-makan'.
3
Locate the Quranic Proofs
Two verses: (2:196) "Do not shave your heads until the Hadi reaches its place of sacrifice" and (22:33) "Then their place of sacrifice is at the Ancient House." The Hanafis interpret 'Ancient House' as the Haram. The imperative indicates obligation (wujub).
فمَحِلّهُ refers to the place of sacrifice, explicitly tied to the House.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i Objection and Hanafi Response
Shafi'i argues that restricting to Haram contradicts the concession (rukhsah) granted to the Muhsar. Hanafi response: the concession is preserved (the Muhsar becomes halal by sending the Hadi), but extreme facilitation (slaughtering anywhere) is not intended; Shariah set a limit.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if slaughtered outside Haram, Hanafi says not halal; Shafi'i says halal.
5
Apply the Details on Valid Animals and Price
A goat is the minimum, but cow, camel, or one-seventh share are valid (like Udhiyah). One may send the price to have an animal purchased and sacrificed in the Haram, as sending the animal may be difficult.
The permissibility of sending value is a facilitation within the Hanafi framework.

Nevertheless, the author of Hidayah says: This animal of Hadi will be sent to the Haram. Because the blood of ihsaar is an act of worship and devotion. And the devotional nature of shedding blood is known only when it is specified with a time or a place. So without one of these two, shedding blood is not worship, and when shedding blood without the Haram is not worship, then the Muhsar will not become halal through it. In the Holy Quran there is also an indication towards the specification of place, as the verse says: 'And do not shave your heads until the Hadi reaches its place of sacrifice' (2:196). Then the place of sacrifice was explained, as He said: 'Then their place of sacrifice is at the Ancient House' (22:33). And the intended meaning is not the exact House, because blood is not shed in the exact House. So the intended meaning is the Haram. Now the translation is: Do not become halal by shaving your head until the Hadi reaches the Haram. From this it is also understood that it is necessary to slaughter the Hadi animal inside the Haram. Also the word 'Hadi' appears in the Quran, and Hadi is only that which is brought to the Haram. Imam Shafi'i said: Specifying the Hadi with the Haram is not correct, because the Shariah created a concession for the Muhsar to become halal by sending the Hadi animal. And specifying it with the Haram nullifies this facilitation and concession. Therefore, the Hadi is not specified with the Haram, rather it can be slaughtered anywhere, halal or haram. Our response is: The original facilitation is observed, but the extreme of facilitation is not observed. That is, one facilitation was created: the Muhsar becomes halal by slaughtering the Hadi animal. And now after that there is no further facilitation. The author of Hidayah says: It is not necessary to specifically send a goat; rather if one sends its price and a goat is bought in the Haram and slaughtered, that is also permissible because sometimes sending a goat is difficult.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah regarding the Hadi (sacrificial animal) sent by the Muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj). The author establishes that the animal must be sent to the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah) and slaughtered there. The reasoning is that the blood of ihsaar is an act of worship, and worship through bloodshed requires specification with either time or place. Since no specific time is mentioned for this blood, it must be specified with place—the Haram. Two Quranic verses are cited: Surah al-Baqarah 2:196 prohibits shaving until the Hadi reaches its place of sacrifice, and Surah al-Hajj 22:33 states that the place of sacrifice is 'the Ancient House,' interpreted by the Hanafis as the Haram. The passage then presents the Shafi'i objection that specifying the Hadi with the Haram contradicts the very concession (rukhsah) granted to the Muhsar. The Hanafi response is that the concession is preserved in allowing the Muhsar to become halal at all, but there is no further concession to allow slaughter outside the Haram. The remainder of the passage details what animals are valid for Hadi: a goat is the minimum, and a cow or camel (or one-seventh share of each) are also valid, analogous to Udhiyah (Eid sacrifice). Moreover, one may send the price of an animal rather than the animal itself, provided the animal is purchased and slaughtered in the Haram.

Key Terms
دم احصار (dam al-ihsaar): The sacrificial animal (Hadi) required from a Muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) to exit ihram.
محصر (muhsar): A person in ihram for Hajj or Umrah who is prevented from reaching the sacred precincts by an enemy, illness, or other obstacle.
ہدی (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram as an offering; in this context specifically the dam al-ihsaar.

Is Shaving Wajib for the Muhsar?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether Muhsar must shave/cut hair for tahallul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on whether shaving is wajib for the Muhsar and evaluate the proof from the Hudaybiyyah incident.

Core Idea
For the Muhsar, the Hadi alone suffices for tahallul—shaving is not wajib, as it is contingent on completing Hajj rites.

In this passage, the author of Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessity of shaving for the Muhsar. While Abu Yusuf argues from the Prophet's example at Hudaybiyyah, the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that shaving is not obligatory because it is a ritual that follows the completion of Hajj actions. This lesson will walk through the proofs and the thamarah (practical consequence) of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the contested ruling: Is shaving (halq/qasr) wajib for the Muhsar to become halal? Note that the majority (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) say no, while Abu Yusuf says yes but with no dam penalty.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof from Hudaybiyyah
Abu Yusuf cites the Prophet's shaving at Hudaybiyyah while being a Muhsar and his command to the Companions to shave as evidence that shaving is part of tahallul for the Muhsar.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof).
3
Examine the majority's proof: shaving contingent on Hajj acts
The majority argue that shaving is a devotional act (nusuk) that is contingent upon performing the actions of Hajj. Since the Muhsar has not performed those actions, shaving is not a ritual for him and thus not wajib.
This reasoning is based on qiyas: shaving is normally a Hajj rite, but the Muhsar lacks the prerequisite rites.
4
Analyse the majority's response to the Hudaybiyyah incident
The majority respond that the Prophet's shaving at Hudaybiyyah was a political act to demonstrate acceptance of the treaty, not a ritual requirement for tahallul. Thus, it does not establish a general rule for all Muhsar.
This shows the importance of context when interpreting prophetic actions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The majority view is mufta bihi: the Muhsar becomes halal by slaughtering the Hadi without shaving. The thamarah (practical difference) is that according to Abu Yusuf, if one does not shave, he commits a sin but no dam; according to the majority, there is no sin and no need to shave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول ثُمَّ تَحَلَّلَ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ ہے کہ محصر پر حلال ہونے کے لئے حلق یا قصر کرانا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اور یہی طرفین کا قول ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ محصر پر یہ واجب ہے لیکن اگر حلق یا قصر نہ کرایا تو دم وغیرہ کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اگر چہ ترک واجب کا گناہ ہوا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حدیبیہ کے سال رسول اللہ ﷺ نے حلق کرایا ہے حالانکہ آپ حدیبیہ میں محصر تھے اور صحابہ کو بھی حلق کا امر فرمایا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حلال ہونے کے لئے ہدی ذبح کرنا کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ ذبح کے بعد حلق یا قصر کرانا بھی ضروری ہے۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حلق ایسی قربت و عبادت ہے جو افعال حج پر مرتب ہوتی ہے۔ افعال حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے حلق حج کا کوئی فعل نہ ہوگا۔ اور محصر چونکہ افعال حج ادا کئے ہوئے نہیں ہوتا اس لئے حلق اس کے واسطے کوئی نسک ہو کر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور رہا آنحضور ﷺ اور صحابہ کا حلق کرانا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ حدیبیہ کے سال مشرکین اور مومنین کے درمیان اس بات پر صلح واقع ہوئی تھی کہ مسلمان امسال بغیر عمرہ کئے واپس چلے جائیں۔ اور مسلمانوں نے اس کو منظور بھی کر لیا تھا۔ اب مسلمانوں نے کفار کو یہ دکھلانے کے لئے کہ ان کا واپسی کا مستحکم ارادہ ہو چکا ہے اپنے سروں کو منڈوایا۔ اور یہ اس لئے کیا تاکہ کفار مسلمانوں سے اپنے آپ کو مامون سمجھیں۔ اور ان کے ساتھ کوئی مکر و فریب کا معاملہ نہ کریں۔ بہر حال رسول اللہ ﷺ اور صحابہ کا یہ حلق اس مقصد کے لئے تھا نہ کہ احرام سے نکلنے کے لئے۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ محصر پر حلال ہونے کے لئے حلق یا قصر کرانا واجب نہیں ہے۔
The author of Hidayah says: Al-Quduri's statement 'thumma tahlala' indicates that for the Muhsar, shaving or cutting hair is not obligatory for becoming halal. And this is the view of the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf says that it is obligatory upon the Muhsar, but if he does not shave or cut, then no blood or anything becomes obligatory, although he commits a sin for leaving an obligation. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that in the year of Hudaybiyyah, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ shaved his head while he was a Muhsar in Hudaybiyyah, and he commanded the Companions to shave. From this it is understood that slaughtering the Hadi is not sufficient for becoming halal; rather, after slaughter, shaving or cutting is also necessary. The proof of the two sides is that shaving is an act of devotion that is contingent upon performing the actions of Hajj. Before performing the actions of Hajj, shaving is not an act of Hajj. And since the Muhsar has not performed the actions of Hajj, shaving would not be a ritual (nusuk) for him and thus not obligatory. As for the shaving of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions, the reason is that in the year of Hudaybiyyah, a peace treaty was made between the polytheists and the believers on the condition that the Muslims would return that year without performing Umrah. The Muslims accepted this. So, to show the disbelievers that they had a firm intention to return, they shaved their heads. This was done so that the disbelievers would feel secure from the Muslims and would not deal with them treacherously. Thus, the shaving of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions was for this purpose, not for exiting ihram. Therefore, it is said that shaving or cutting hair is not obligatory for the Muhsar to become halal.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the Muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) must shave (halq) or shorten (qasr) his hair as part of tahallul (exiting ihram). The author of Hidayah cites Al-Quduri's matn where the word 'thumma tahlala' indicates that simply sending the Hadi suffices for tahallul without shaving. The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that shaving is not wajib for the Muhsar. However, Abu Yusuf holds that it is wajib, but if omitted, no compensatory dam is required, though the person commits a sin for leaving a wajib. Abu Yusuf's proof is the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions shaved after being prevented from entering Makkah. The majority's response is that the shaving at Hudaybiyyah was a political act to demonstrate to the polytheists that the Muslims accepted the treaty and were returning home, not a ritual requirement for tahallul. The majority's own proof is that shaving is a devotional act that comes after completing the rites of Hajj, such as standing at Arafah. Since a Muhsar has not performed these rites, shaving is not a nusuk for him.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely; a ritual act in Hajj and Umrah for exiting ihram.
قصر (qasr): Cutting a portion of the hair; an alternative to halq for tahallul.
طرفین (tarfayn): In this context, the 'two sides' refer to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (as opposed to Abu Yusuf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on shaving for the Muhsar?
A) It is wajib, and if omitted requires a dam
B) It is wajib, but if omitted no dam is required
C) It is not wajib; the Hadi alone suffices
D) It is sunnah and recommended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that the Muhsar becomes halal by slaughtering the Hadi alone; shaving (halq/qasr) is not wajib for him.
