Qarin Must Send Two Animals for Ihsaar
Ruling that a Qarin sends two sacrificial animals for ihsaar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Qarin in ihsaar and explain why two animals are required.

Core Idea
A Qarin must send two animals for ihsaar because he is exiting from two ihrams simultaneously.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: when a person performing Hajj and Umrah together (Qarin) is prevented from completing the rituals. The ruling clarifies the obligation to send two sacrificial animals and the consequence of sending only one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and situation
The passage speaks about a Qarin who is muhsar (prevented). Recognize that this person has combined Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.
2
State the ruling
He must send two animals (damayn) – one for each ihram component.
3
Explain the rationale
Because he needs to become halal from two ihrams: one for Hajj and one for Umrah. Each requires its own expiation.
Hanafi principle: each component ihram treated separately for exiting.
4
Analyze the incorrect attempt
If he sends only one animal with the intention of exiting only Hajj, he does not become halal from either. Tahallul from both must occur simultaneously.
The textual evidence: 'because becoming halal from both is prescribed in a single state.'
5
Summarize the legal principle
The Qarin's two ihrams are linked for exiting; they cannot be exited separately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ كَانَ قَارِنًا بَعَثَ بِدَمَيْنِ لِاحْتِيَاجِهِ إِلَى التَّحَلُّلِ عَنْ إِحْرَامَيْنِ فَإِنْ بَعَثَ بِهَدْيٍ وَاحِدٍ لِيَتَحَلَّلَ عَنِ الْحَجِّ وَيَبْقَى فِي إِحْرَامِ الْعُمْرَةِ لَمْ يَتَحَلَّلْ عَنْ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا لِأَنَّ التَّحَلُّلَ مِنْهُمَا شُرِعَ فِي حَالَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ۔ ترجمہ: کہا اور اگر ہو قارن ہو تو دو دم بھیجے کیونکہ دو احراموں میں سے حلال ہونے کی طرف محتاج ہے۔ پس اگر ایک ہدی بھیجا تاکہ حج کے احرام سے حلال ہو جائے اور عمرہ کے احرام میں رہے تو ان دونوں میں سے کسی سے حلال نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایک ہی حالت میں دونوں سے حلال ہونا مشروع ہوا ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
He said: If he is a Qarin, he sends two blood (animals) because he needs to become halal from two ihrams. If he sends only one Hadi intending to become halal from Hajj and remain in the ihram of Umrah, he does not become halal from either of them, because becoming halal from both is prescribed in a single state. Translation: He said: And if he is a Qarin, he sends two bloods (animals) because he needs to become halal from two ihrams. So if he sends one Hadi to become halal from the ihram of Hajj and remain in the ihram of Umrah, he will not become halal from either of them, because becoming halal from both is prescribed in one state. The explanation is clear.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the text regarding the Qarin (one who performs Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram). Since he has combined two intentions (Hajj and Umrah) into one ihram, he is considered to be in two ihrams for the purpose of exiting. Expiation (dam) for ihsaar is required per ihram. Therefore, if a Qarin is prevented (muhsar) and sends his Hadi, he must send two animals—one for each ihram. Sending only one animal with the intention of exiting only the Hajj ihram while remaining in Umrah ihram is ineffective; tahallul from both must occur simultaneously. This is because the shariah has prescribed that the two ihrams are exited together in one state.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): A person who performs Hajj and Umrah together in one state of ihram, combining both intentions.
دم (dam): Literally 'blood'; refers to the sacrificial animal (Hadi) required for exiting ihram in cases like ihsaar or tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Qarin who is prevented (muhsar) sends only one Hadi, what is the result?
A) He becomes halal from Hajj only
B) He becomes halal from Umrah only
C) He becomes halal from both
D) He does not become halal from either

Key Takeaway
A Qarin in ihsaar must send two animals; sending only one renders him still muhrim from both ihrams.

Timing of Slaughter for the Muhsar: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of dam al-ihsaar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa allows the Muhsar of Hajj to slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr while the Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr, based on the distinction between dam kaffarah and dam nusuk.

Core Idea
Dam al-ihsaar is kaffarah (expiation), not nusuk (ritual) — place-bound, not time-bound.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on when the Muhsar (a person prevented from completing Hajj) may slaughter his sacrificial animal. The core question is whether the dam al-ihsaar is an expiatory offering (kaffarah) governed by the general rules of expiation, or a ritual sacrifice (nusuk) governed by the specific timing of Hajj. Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ sharply, and their arguments will sharpen your understanding of how the Hanafi school categorizes sacrificial blood.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa: the Muhsar of Hajj may slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr. Then identify the disagreement of the Sahibayn: slaughter is only valid on Yawm al-Nahr for the Hajj Muhsar.
Both agree slaughter must be in the Haram.
2
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn analogize dam al-ihsaar to the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran, which are slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr. They also analogize it to shaving (halq) because both are tahlil (acts that make one halal).
This is a qiyas argument: the Sahibayn treat the dam as a ritual sacrifice.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the dam al-ihsaar by its legal nature: it is a blood of expiation (dam kaffarah), from which the offerer may not eat. Therefore, it is specified by place (Haram) but not by time, like all other kaffarah bloods.
Abu Hanifa uses the rule that expiatory blood is only place-specific, not time-specific, unlike ritual blood which has a fixed time.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a Muhsar of Hajj slaughters before Yawm al-Nahr, according to Abu Hanifa he becomes halal immediately. According to the Sahibayn, such a slaughter is invalid and must be repeated on Yawm al-Nahr.
This affects pilgrims who may become impatient or face travel constraints.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ الْإِحْصَارِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَرَمِ وَيَجُوزُ ذَبْحُهُ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ لِلْمُحْصِرِ بِالْحَجِّ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُحْصِرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ مَتَى شَاءَ اعْتِبَارًا بِهَدْيِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ وَرُبَّمَا يُعْتَبَرُ أَنَّهُ بِالْحَلْقِ إِذْ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا مُحَلَّلٌ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ دَمُ كَفَّارَةٍ حَتَّى لَا يَجُوزُ الْأَكْلُ مِنْهُ فَيُخْتَصُّ بِالْمَكَانِ دُونَ الزَّمَانِ كَسَائِرِ دِمَاءِ الْكَفَّارَاتِ بِخِلَافِ دَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكٍ وَبِخِلَافِ الْحَلْقِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي أَوَانِهِ لِأَنَّ مُعْظَمَ أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ وَهُوَ الْوُقُوفُ يَنْتَهِي بِهِ۔ ترجمہ: اور جائز نہیں ہے دم احصار کو ذبح کرنا مگر حرم میں اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو یوم نحر سے پہلے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ محصر بالحج کے لئے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یوم نحر میں۔ اور محصر بالعمرہ کے لئے جائز ہے کہ جب چاہے ذبح کرے۔ ہدی تمتع اور ہدی قران پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور بسا اوقات صاحبین دم احصار کو حلق پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک محلل ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ دم کفارہ ہے حتی کہ اس میں سے کھانا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ دم مکان یعنی حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا نہ کہ زمان یعنی یوم نحر کے ساتھ۔ جیسے کفارات کے دوسرے دم ہیں۔ برخلاف دم تمتع اور دم قران کے اس لئے کہ وہ دم نسک ہے اور بر خلاف حلق کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت میں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ افعال حج میں سے بزرگ فعل اور وہ وقوف عرفہ ہے اسی حلق کے ساتھ پورا ہوتا ہے۔
It is not permissible to slaughter the blood of ihsaar except in the Haram. And it is permissible to slaughter it before Yawm al-Nahr according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Slaughtering is not permissible for the Muhsar of Hajj except on Yawm al-Nahr. And for the Muhsar of Umrah, slaughter is permissible whenever he wishes, by analogy with the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran. And sometimes the two analogize the blood of ihsaar with shaving (halq), because each of them is a tahlil (means of becoming halal). And Abu Hanifa's proof is that it is a blood of expiation (dam kaffarah), such that eating from it is not permissible, so it is specified with place (the Haram) not with time (Yawm al-Nahr), like all other bloods of expiation. Unlike the blood of Tamattu' and Qiran because those are blood of ritual (dam nusuk), and unlike shaving because it is in its proper time, since the greatest action of Hajj, which is standing at Arafah, ends with it.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the timing of slaughter for the dam al-ihsaar (sacrifice of the one prevented). All agree that slaughter must be in the Haram. The disagreement is about timing: Abu Hanifa permits slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah), while the Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr for the Muhsar of Hajj. For the Muhsar of Umrah, both allow slaughter anytime. The Sahibayn analogize to the Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran, which are slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr, and also to halq (shaving) which is itself a tahlil (means of becoming halal) and occurs at its proper time. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that dam al-ihsaar is a blood of expiation (kaffarah), like kaffarah for hunting or shaving, which are specified by place (Haram) but not by time. Thus it can be slaughtered whenever it reaches the Haram, before Yawm al-Nahr. The Sahibayn's counterargument is that it is analogous to dam at-tamattu' and dam al-qiran, which are ritual sacrifices (nusuk) specified to Yawm al-Nahr, and to halq which is a direct tahlil. The passage thus distinguishes between dam of expiation (general, place-specific only) and dam of ritual (time-specific).

Key Terms
دم کفارہ (dam kaffarah): A sacrificial animal offered as expiation for a violation or prevention in Hajj, from which the offerer may not eat.
دم نسک (dam nusuk): A sacrificial animal offered as a ritual act of worship for tamattu' or qiran, from which the offerer may eat.
یوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The Day of Sacrifice, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is slaughtering dam al-ihsaar before Yawm al-Nahr permissible?
A) Because it is analogous to dam at-tamattu'
B) Because it is a blood of expiation (kaffarah), specified by place not time
C) Because the Muhsar may choose any day within Hajj days
D) Because it can be slaughtered anytime in the Haram after ihram

Key Takeaway
Dam al-ihsaar is an expiatory offering (kaffarah), not a ritual sacrifice (nusuk), so its timing is flexible before Yawm al-Nahr, according to Abu Hanifa.

Timing of Dam al-Ihsar: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of dam al-ihsar slaughter for muhsir bi'l-hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of dam al-ihsar, explain each proof, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) for a muhsir bi'l-hajj.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: dam al-ihsar is kaffarah, timeless in Haram; Sahibayn: qiyas to tamattu' and halq requires Yawm al-Nahr.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over when the sacrifice of the muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj) must be offered. All authorities agree it must be in the Haram, but they differ on whether it must be on Yawm al-Nahr. Understanding these proofs and their underlying principles is essential for proper application.

Guided Path
1
Identify points of agreement and disagreement
All agree dam al-ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram. Disagreement is about timing for muhsir bi'l-hajj; for muhsir bi'l-umrah, no dispute.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa permits before Yawm al-Nahr; Sahibayn restrict to Yawm al-Nahr for muhsir bi'l-hajj.
For muhsir bi'l-umrah, both allow anytime.
3
Analyze the proofs of the Sahibayn
Two qiyas: to dam al-tamattu'/qiran (restricted to Haram and Yawm al-Nahr) and to halq (shaving, also on Yawm al-Nahr). The illa: each is a cause of tahlil.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Distinguishes dam al-ihsar as dam kaffarah (expiatory), not nusuk, so restricted only to place (Haram), not time. Eating from it is prohibited, unlike dam nusuk.
Also rejects qiyas to halq because halq occurs at its proper time after standing at Arafat.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a muhsir bi'l-hajj slaughters before Yawm al-Nahr, it is valid per Abu Hanifa but not per Sahibayn; they would require a repeat sacrifice on Yawm al-Nahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دم احصار کو حرم میں ہی ذبح کرنا لازم ہے اور یوم النحر سے پہلے ذبح کرنا بھی جائز ہے وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ الْإِحْصَارِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَرَمِ وَيَجُوزُ ذَبْحُهُ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ للْمُحْصِرِ بِالْحَقِّ إِلا فِى يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُحْصِرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ مَتَى شَاءَ اِعْتِبَارًا بِهَدْيِ الْمُتَعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ وَرُبَمَا دِمَاءِ الْكَفَّارَاتِ بِخِلَافِ دَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكِ وَبِخِلَافِ الْحَلَقِ لِأَنَّهُ فِى أوَانِه لِأَنَّ مُعْظَمَ أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ وَهُوَ الْوُقُوفُ يَنتَهَى بِه ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہے دم احصار کو ذبح کرنا مگر حرم میں اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس کو یوم نحر سے پہلے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مصر بالج کے لئے ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر یوم نحر میں ۔ اور محصر بالعمرہ کے لئے جائز ہے کہ جب چاہے ذبح کرے۔ ہدی متعہ اور ہدی قرآن پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور بسا اوقات صاحبین بدی احصار کو حلق پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک محلل ہے۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ دم کفارہ ہے حتی کہ اس میں سے کھانا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ دم مکان یعنی حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا نہ کہ زمان یعنی یوم نحر کے ساتھ ۔ جیسے کفارات کے دوسرے دم ہیں۔ برخلاف دم تمتع اور دم قران کے اس لئے کہ وہ دم نسک ہے اور بر خلاف حلق کے کیونکہ وہ اپنے وقت میں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ افعال حج میں سے بزرگ فعل اور وہ وقوف عرفہ ہے اسی حلق کے ساتھ پورا ہوتا ہے۔ اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ۵۰۵ کتاب الحج تشریح مسئلہ، دم احصار کا فقط حرم میں ذبح کرنا جائز ہے حرم کے علاوہ میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یوم نحر سے پہلے دم احصار کا ذبح کرنا جائز ہے اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ مصر بالج کے لئے دم احصار کو ذبح کرنا صرف یوم نحر میں جائز ہے اس سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک دم احصار حرم کے ساتھ تو خاص ہے مگر یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک حرم اور یوم نحر دونوں کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اور مصر بالعمر ہ بالا تفاق جب چاہے دم احصار کو ذبح کرے۔ اس کے لئے کسی وقت کی تعین نہیں ہے۔ محصر بالج کے لئے دم احصار کا ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے علاوہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس بارے میں صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انہوں نے دم احصار کو دم تمتع اور دمِ قرآن پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ پس جس طرح دم تمتع اور دم قران حرم اور یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اسی طرح : مِ احصار بھی حرم اور یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہو گا۔ صاحبین نے دم احصار کے ذبح کو حلق پر بھی قیاس کیا ہے۔ پس جس طرح حلق یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہے اسی طرح دم احصار کا ذبح کرنا بھی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا۔ وجہ قیاس یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک محلل ہے یعنی احترام سے نکالنے والا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ دم احصار دم کفارہ اور دم جنایت ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ دم احصار میں سے کچھ کھانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ بلکه به فقراء کا حق ہے اور کفارات کی قربانیاں بالاتفاق مکان یعنی حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہیں اور زمانہ یعنی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے دم احصار کا ذبح کرنا بھی حرم کے ساتھ تو خاص ہو گا مگر یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہ ہوگا، بر خلاف دم تمتع اور دم قرآن کے کیونکہ یہ دونوں دم نسک ہیں اور دم شکر ہیں۔ اور دم نسک یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بھی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص ہوں گے۔ اور برخلاف حلق کے کیونکہ حلق اپنے وقت پر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ افعال حج میں معظم فضل یعنی وقوف عرفہ اسی حلق کے ساتھ پورا ہوتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ تمحلل کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک وہ محلل جو اپنے وقت پر ہوتا ہے۔ اور ایک وہ محلل جو وقت سے پہلے ہوتا ہے۔ پس حلق محلل ہے اپنے وقت پر اور دمِ احصار کو ذبح کرنا ملل ہے وقت سے پہلے ۔ پس اس فرق کی صورت میں دم احصار کو حلق پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہوگا۔
It is necessary to slaughter the dam al-ihsar only in the Haram, and it is permissible to slaughter it before Yawm al-Nahr according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Slaughter for the muhsir bi'l-hajj is not permissible except on Yawm al-Nahr. And for the muhsir bi'l-umrah, it is permissible whenever he wishes, by analogy to the sacrifice of tamattu' and qiran. And sometimes they analogize it to shaving, since each of them is a cause of tahlil. And for Abu Hanifa, it is a blood of expiation such that eating from it is not permissible, so it is restricted to the place (Haram) not the time (Yawm al-Nahr), like other expiatory bloods, unlike the blood of tamattu' and qiran because they are sacrificial bloods, and unlike shaving because it is in its own time, since the major act of Hajj, which is standing at Arafat, is completed with it. Translation: And it is not permissible to slaughter the dam al-ihsar except in the Haram. And according to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible to slaughter it before Yawm al-Nahr. And the Sahibayn said: For the muhsir bi'l-hajj, slaughter is not permissible except on Yawm al-Nahr. And for the muhsir bi'l-umrah, it is permissible whenever he wishes, by analogy to the sacrifice of tamattu' and qiran. And sometimes the Sahibayn analogize it to shaving, because each of them is a cause of tahlil. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that this is an expiatory blood, so it is restricted to the place (Haram) and not to the time (Yawm al-Nahr), like other expiatory bloods, unlike tamattu' and qiran blood because they are sacrificial bloods, and unlike shaving because it is in its own time, since the major act of Hajj, which is standing at Arafat, is completed with it. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 3, page 505, Book of Hajj. Explanation of the issue: Slaughter of dam al-ihsar is only permissible in the Haram; outside the Haram it is not permissible. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, slaughter of dam al-ihsar before Yawm al-Nahr is permissible, and the Sahibayn said that for the muhsir bi'l-hajj, slaughter of dam al-ihsar is only permissible on Yawm al-Nahr, not before. The conclusion is that according to Imam Sahib, dam al-ihsar is restricted to the Haram but not to Yawm al-Nahr, while according to the Sahibayn, it is restricted to both the Haram and Yawm al-Nahr. For the muhsir bi'l-umrah, by consensus, he may slaughter whenever he wishes; there is no fixed time. For the muhsir bi'l-hajj, slaughter of dam al-ihsar is not permissible other than on Yawm al-Nahr. In this regard, the proof of the Sahibayn is that they analogize dam al-ihsar to dam al-tamattu' and dam al-qiran. Just as dam al-tamattu' and dam al-qiran are restricted to the Haram and Yawm al-Nahr, similarly dam al-ihsar will be restricted to the Haram and Yawm al-Nahr. The Sahibayn also analogize the slaughter of dam al-ihsar to shaving. Just as shaving is restricted to Yawm al-Nahr, similarly the slaughter of dam al-ihsar will be restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. The basis of analogy is that each of them is a cause of tahlil, i.e., a means of exiting ihram. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that dam al-ihsar is an expiatory blood and a blood of penalty. That is why eating from it is not permissible; rather it is the right of the poor. And expiatory sacrifices are by consensus restricted to the place (Haram) and not restricted to the time (Yawm al-Nahr). Therefore, the slaughter of dam al-ihsar will be restricted to the Haram but not to Yawm al-Nahr, contrary to dam al-tamattu' and dam al-qiran because these two are sacrificial bloods (dam nusuk) and bloods of gratitude, and sacrificial bloods are restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. So these will also be restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. And contrary to shaving because shaving is in its own time, since the major act of Hajj, which is standing at Arafat, is completed with it. The conclusion: There are two types of tahlil (cause of exit): one that occurs at its proper time, and one that occurs before its time. Shaving is a cause of exit at its proper time, while slaughtering dam al-ihsar is a cause of exit before its time. So how can analogizing dam al-ihsar to shaving be correct given this difference?
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the timing for slaughtering the dam al-ihsar (the sacrifice offered by one who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah). All agree that this sacrifice must be slaughtered within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). The disagreement is about the time: Abu Hanifa holds that it may be slaughtered any time after the ihsar (prevention) and before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah), while the Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr itself for the muhsir bi'l-hajj. However, for the muhsir bi'l-umrah (one prevented from completing Umrah), all agree he may slaughter at any time. The Sahibayn base their view on qiyas (analogy): they compare dam al-ihsar to dam al-tamattu' and dam al-qiran (which are restricted to Yawm al-Nahr) and also to halq (shaving the head), which is also a cause of tahlil and is performed on Yawm al-Nahr. Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, argues that dam al-ihsar is a dam kaffarah (expiatory blood) — like other expiatory sacrifices, it is restricted only to the Haram but not to a specific time. Eating from it is prohibited, unlike dam al-tamattu' and al-qiran which are 'blood of worship' (dam nusuk). Also, shaving is different because it is an act that occurs at its natural time (after standing at Arafat), whereas dam al-ihsar may be sent before the time of standing. The commentary emphasizes the key distinction: one type of tahlil occurs at its proper time (shaving), another occurs before its proper time (dam al-ihsar), so analogizing them is flawed according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-iḥṣār): The sacrificial animal that must be offered by a person prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah in order to exit ihram.
محصر (muḥṣir): One who is prevented from completing the rituals of Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other obstacles.
يوم النحر (yawm al-naḥr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice during Hajj.
حلق (ḥalq): Shaving the head, one of the acts of tahlil (exiting ihram) and a wajib act of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when must a muhsir bi'l-hajj slaughter his dam al-ihsar?
A) Any time before Yawm al-Nahr
B) Only on Yawm al-Nahr
C) Within ten days after prevention
D) At the time of exiting ihram regardless of day

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa classifies dam al-ihsar as expiatory (kaffarah), thus not time-bound; the Sahibayn analogize it to worship sacrifices (nusuk) and shaving, restricting it to Yawm al-Nahr.

Muhsir Bi'l-Hajj Must Perform Qada Hajj and Umrah
Ruling with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muhsir bi'l-hajj must perform both qada Hajj and qada Umrah after becoming halal, and explain the proof from the hadith of fa'it al-hajj using qiyas.

Core Idea
A muhsir must make up both Hajj and Umrah, like the one who misses Hajj.

When someone is prevented from completing Hajj (muhsir) and releases himself from ihram by sending a sacrifice, he is not free from obligation. According to the Hanafi school, he must later perform both a makeup Hajj and a makeup Umrah. This ruling is derived from the case of the one who misses the standing at Arafat (fa'it al-hajj), for whom the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed both Umrah and a future Hajj. The muhsir is legally analogous.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? What is the hukm (level) for the muhsir after tahlil?
The act is performing qada Hajj and qada Umrah; the ruling is wajib.
2
Locate the primary dalil
What is the main textual evidence cited? Identify the hadith and the companion narrations.
The hadith of fa'it al-hajj and the narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
3
Trace the qiyas analogy
How is the muhsir analogized to fa'it al-hajj? What is the common effective cause (illa)?
Both have validly commenced Hajj and are unable to complete it; hence both must make up Hajj and Umrah.
4
Confirm the scope of obligation
Does the obligation include both Hajj and Umrah? Why is Umrah specifically required?
The hadith explicitly commands Umrah for fa'it al-hajj, so it is included by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
محصر بالج جب حلال ہو جائے تو اس پر حج اور عمرہ لازم ہے قَالَ وَالْمُحْصَرُ بِالْحَجِّ إِذَا تَحَلَّلَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَةٌ هَكَذَا رُوِيَ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسَ وَابْنِ عُمَرَ وَلِأَنَّ الْحَجَّةَ يَجِبُّ قَضَاؤُهَا لِصِحَّةِ الشُّرُوعِ وَالْعُمْرَةُ لِمَا أنَّه فِى مَعْنَى فَائِتِ الْحَجّ ترجمہ اور محصر بالج حلال ہو گیا تو اس پر حج اور عمرہ واجب ہے۔ ایسا ہی ابن عباس اور ابن عمر سے مروی ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ حج کی قضاء شروع صحیح ہونے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے اور عمرہ اس لئے کہ وہ فائت الج کے معنی میں ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص حج کرنے سے روک دیا گیا پھر وہ ہدی بھیج کر حلال ہو گیا تو اس پر حج اور عمرہ دونوں واجب ہیں۔ ایسا ہی ابن عباس اور ابن عمرؓ سے مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ دونوں نے فرمایا ہے قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَةً بِلَيْل فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَج فَليحلل بِعُمْرَةٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِل یعنی رسول ہاشمی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کہا کہ جس کا رات میں وقوف عرفہ فوت ہو گیا اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا پس وہ عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور اس پر اگلے سال حج فرض ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ فَائِتُ الْحَج پر حج اور عمرہ دونوں ہیں اور محصر بھی چونکہ فائت احج کے معنی میں ہے اس لئے اس پر بھی دونوں واجب ہوں گے۔
When the muhsir bi'l-hajj becomes halal, Hajj and Umrah are obligatory upon him. He said: The muhsir bi'l-hajj, when he becomes halal, then upon him is a Hajj and an Umrah. Thus it is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And because the qada of Hajj is obligatory due to the validity of the commencement, and the Umrah because it is in the meaning of one who misses Hajj. Translation: And the muhsir bi'l-hajj, when he becomes halal, then upon him Hajj and Umrah are wajib. This is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And because the qada of Hajj is obligatory due to the validity of having started it, and the Umrah because it is in the meaning of fa'it al-hajj (one who misses Hajj). Explanation of the issue: If a person is prevented from performing Hajj, then he sends a sacrifice and becomes halal, then both Hajj and Umrah are wajib upon him. This is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Both of them said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever misses Arafat at night, then he has missed Hajj, so let him perform Umrah and become halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' This hadith indicates that upon the fa'it al-hajj, both Hajj and Umrah are wajib, and the muhsir also is in the meaning of fa'it al-hajj, so both are wajib upon him.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a person who is prevented (muhsir) from completing Hajj and who becomes halal by sending a sacrifice must subsequently perform both a qada Hajj and a qada Umrah. The proof is twofold: first, a narration from the Companions Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that this is required; second, a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding the one who misses Hajj (fa'it al-hajj): he must perform Umrah to exit ihram and perform Hajj the next year. The muhsir is analogized to this: he too has started Hajj (intending it) and is now prevented, so he must make up both Hajj and Umrah. The reasoning: Hajj qada is wajib because he validly commenced it (shuru' sahih), even though he did not complete it. Umrah qada is wajib because he is in the meaning of 'one who misses Hajj' (fa'it al-hajj), who must do both. The Urdu commentary explains that the hadith directly applies to fa'it al-hajj, and the muhsir is legally similar, so the same rule applies.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣir): One prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah.
فائت الحج (fā'it al-ḥajj): One who misses the key rite of Hajj (standing at Arafat) and thus does not complete that year's Hajj.
قضاء (qaḍā'): A makeup performance of an obligatory act that was missed or invalidated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only a makeup Hajj
B) Only a makeup Umrah
C) Both a makeup Hajj and a makeup Umrah
D) He is free of any obligation

Key Takeaway
A muhsir bi'l-hajj must perform both qada Hajj and qada Umrah, based on the hadith of fa'it al-hajj and the analogy between the two cases.

Ihsar Applies to Umrah: Hanafi vs Maliki
Dispute on applying ihsar to Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that ihsar applies to Umrah and distinguish it from the Maliki position, citing the Prophetic precedent.

Core Idea
Ihsar applies to Umrah because the Prophet was prevented at Hudaybiyyah while performing Umrah.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute: does the ruling of ihsar (prevention from completing pilgrimage) apply to Umrah? The Hanafi school affirms it, while Imam Malik denies it. We will explore the Hanafi proofs from the Hudaybiyyah incident and the rationale of removing hardship, and understand the practical difference in rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: ihsar applies to Umrah, requiring qada upon tahallul.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik disagrees: Umrah is not time-bound, so ihsar does not apply.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik argues that since Umrah does not have a specific time limit like Hajj, it cannot be 'lost' and thus ihsar is irrelevant.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi rebuts with the Prophet's example at Hudaybiyyah – he and his companions were performing Umrah and were prevented. Also, the rationale for tahallul (removing hardship) is present in Umrah ihram.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
A Hanafi follower must perform qada Umrah if prevented; a Maliki follower is not obliged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الْقَضَاءُ وَالْإِحْصَارُ عَنْهَا يَتَحَقَّقُ عِندَنَا وَ قَالَ مَالِكُ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ لِأَنَّهَا لَا تَتَوَفَّتُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ [النَّبِيَّ]؟ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَأَصْحَابَهُ أُحْصِرُوا بِالْحُدَيْبِيَةِ وَكَانُوا عُمَّارًا وَلِأَنَّ شَرْعَ التَّحَلُّلِ لِدَفْعِ الْحَرَجِ وَهَذَا مَوْجُودٌ فِي إِحْرَامِ الْعُمْرَةِ وَإِذَا تَحَقَّقَ الْإِحْصَارُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْقَضَاءُ إِذَا تَحَلَّلَ كَمَا فِي الْحَجِّ
And upon the one prevented from Umrah, the qada (compensation) is due. And ihsar regarding it is realized according to us, and Malik said it is not realized because it (Umrah) is not time-bound. And our proof is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, and his companions were prevented at Hudaybiyyah while they were performing Umrah, and because the legislation of tahlul (emergency exit from ihram) is to remove hardship, and this exists in the state of ihram for Umrah. And when ihsar is realized, then qada is obligatory upon him when he exits (ihram), just as in Hajj.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding ihsar (prevention from completing pilgrimage rites) in relation to Umrah. The Hanafi position, stated first, holds that ihsar does apply to Umrah, meaning that if one begins Umrah and is then prevented from completing it, the rulings of ihsar apply, including the obligation of qada (compensatory Umrah) upon tahallul. Imam Malik disagrees, arguing that Umrah is not time-bound (mutawaffat) like Hajj, so it cannot be 'lost' (fawat), hence ihsar does not apply. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: first, the historical precedent of the Prophet and his companions at Hudaybiyyah, where they were prevented while in the state of Umrah and later performed qada; second, the general rationale behind the legislation of tahallul—to alleviate hardship—which is equally present in Umrah ihram. Since the cause (hardship) exists, the ruling applies. Thus, in Hanafi fiqh, the muhsar bil-umrah (one prevented from completing Umrah) is obligated to offer qada just like the muhsar bil-hajj.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy or legitimate barrier.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Compensatory performance of a missed or invalidated pilgrimage (Hajj or Umrah).
تحلل (tāḥallul): Exit from ihram due to necessity, allowed with sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does ihsar apply to Umrah?
A) Because Umrah is time-bound.
B) Because the Prophet and his companions were prevented during Umrah at Hudaybiyyah.
C) Because Imam Malik said so.
D) Because Umrah is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Ihsar applies to Umrah in the Hanafi school due to the Prophetic precedent at Hudaybiyyah, requiring qada upon tahallul, contra the Maliki view.

Qarin Muhsar: Qada Obligations
Specifies the qada obligations for a qarin muhsar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qada obligations of a qarin muhsar and explain why two Umrahs are owed.

Core Idea
A qarin muhsar must compensate with one Hajj and two Umrahs because both ihrams were started but not completed.

When a pilgrim enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah (qarin) and is then prevented from completing the rites (muhsar), he must make up (qada) both pilgrimages. But how many? The ruling specifies one Hajj and two Umrahs. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each component.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
Recognize that the ruling applies to a qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram) who becomes muhsar (prevented from completing). The qada is: one Hajj and two Umrahs.
The term qarin is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may define it differently.
2
Understand the basis for the single Hajj
The single Hajj compensates the originally intended Hajj, which was invalidated due to ihsar. Only one Hajj was intended, so only one is owed.
This mirrors the ruling for a mufrid (one performing Hajj only) who is muhsar.
3
Understand the basis for two Umrahs
The first Umrah compensates the Umrah that was intended and invalidated. The second Umrah is required because the qarin validly entered the state of ihram for Umrah (as part of the combined intention) and then exited it without completing due to ihsar; that act of entering creates an obligation to complete or compensate, even if the original Umrah was already accounted for.
The second Umrah is not redundant; it is a separate obligation arising from the nature of qiran in Hanafi law.
4
Distinguish from other types of pilgrims
Contrast this with a mufrid (owes only one Hajj) or a mutamatti (owes one Umrah and one Hajj separately). The qarin’s double Umrah obligation is unique to the combined ihram.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى الْقَارِنِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ أَمَّا الْحَجُّ فَوَاحِدَةٌ لِمَا بَيَّنَا وَالثَّانِيَةُ لِأَنَّهُ خَرَجَ مِنْهَا بَعْدَ صِحَّةِ الشُّرُوعِ
And upon the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) is one Hajj and two Umrahs. As for the Hajj, it is one, for what we have explained. And the second (Umrah) because he exited from it after the validity of commencement.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This is a concise ruling statement regarding the qada obligations of a qarin (one who entered ihram for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously) who is then prevented (muhsar). The ruling states that he owes one Hajj and two Umrahs as compensation. The single Hajj corresponds to the one he initially intended, as explained earlier in the text. The two Umrahs are required because he had combined them: the first Umrah is the one he invalidated, and the second Umrah is because he had entered the state of ihram for it as well (with validity) and then exited it due to ihsar. Thus, the qada includes compensating for both the invalidated Hajj and the invalidated Umrah. This ruling is specific to the qarin case in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A pilgrim who combines Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram.
مُحْصَر (muḥṣar): A pilgrim prevented from completing the pilgrimage after entering ihram, e.g., by enemy or illness.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Compensatory performance of a missed or invalidated worship act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many Hajj and Umrah qada are required for a qarin muhsar?
A) One Hajj and one Umrah
B) One Hajj and two Umrahs
C) Two Hajj and one Umrah
D) Two Hajj and two Umrahs

Key Takeaway
A qarin muhsar must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs because the valid commencement of both acts in one ihram creates separate qada obligations.

Qarin Muhsar with Hadi: Obligation after Ihsar Removal
Ruling for a qarin muhsar after ihsar removal with a pre-sent Hadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a qarin muhsar who sent a Hadi and then ihsar is removed, distinguishing the two scenarios based on ability to reach the Hajj and the Hadi.

Core Idea
A qarin's obligation to proceed after ihsar removal depends on whether he can still perform Hajj himself — inability revives the substitute, ability revives the original duty.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj jurisprudence: a qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) who, due to a barrier (ihsar), sends a sacrificial animal (Hadi) ahead to be slaughtered on a specified day. What happens if the barrier is lifted before that day? The Hanafi school provides a conditional ruling based on whether the person can still catch the Hajj and the Hadi in time. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating how the concepts of inability (ʿajz) and substitution (khalaf) interact with the revival of the original obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial situation
The qarin sent a Hadi with a specific promise (mawʿid) that it be slaughtered on a particular day. He is muhsar (prevented from entering Mecca).
This is the baseline scenario before the barrier is lifted.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios after ihsar removal
After the barrier is lifted, the ruling bifurcates based on whether the qarin can reach both the Hajj (the pilgrimage rites) and the Hadi (i.e., the appointed slaughter time).
The text explicitly contrasts 'cannot reach' vs. 'can reach'.
3
State the ruling for inability to reach both
If he cannot reach the Hajj and the Hadi, proceeding to Mecca is not obligatory (lā yalzamu). He should wait until the Hadi is slaughtered, which effects tahallul. He may optionally proceed to perform Umrah, as he is now considered one who missed the Hajj (fāʾit al-ḥajj).
The purpose of proceeding (performing rites) is missed, so the substitute stands.
4
State the ruling for ability to reach both
If he can reach both the Hajj and the Hadi, then proceeding becomes obligatory (yalzamu) upon him. The inability (ʿajz) that justified the substitute has been removed before the purpose was achieved by the substitute.
Original obligation revives because the condition for the substitute no longer exists.
5
Identify the underlying legal rationale
The ruling is based on the removal of inability (ʿajz). When ability returns, the primary obligation is reinstated; the substitute (Hadi) was only valid as long as the inability persisted.
This is a manifestation of the principle that necessity (ḍarūra) is measured by its extent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن بَعَثَ الْقَارِنُ هَدْيًا وَوَاعَدَهُمْ أَنْ يَذْبَحُوهُ فِي يَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ ثُمَّ زَالَ الْإِحْصَارُ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ وَالْهَدْيَ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ أَنْ يَتَوَجَّهَ بَلْ يَصْبِرُ حَتَّى يَتَحَلَّلَ بِنَحْرِ الْهَدْيِ لِفَوَاتِ الْمَقْصُودِ مِنَ التَّوَجُّهِ وَهُوَ أَدَاءُ الْأَفْعَالِ وَإِنْ تَوَجَّهَ لِيَتَحَلَّلَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ لَهُ ذَلِكَ وَلِأَنَّهُ فَائِتُ الْحَجِّ وَإِن كَانَ يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ وَالْهَدْيَ لَزِمَهُ التَّوَجُّهُ لِزَوَالِ الْعَجْزِ قَبْلَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِالْخَلَفِ
If the qarin sends a Hadi (sacrificial animal) and appoints them to slaughter it on a specific day, then the ihsar is removed: if he cannot reach the Hajj and the Hadi, it is not obligatory upon him to proceed (to Mecca); rather, he waits until he becomes halal (exits ihram) by the slaughter of the Hadi, because the purpose of proceeding (which is performing the rites) is missed. And if he proceeds to become halal by the rites of Umrah, he may do so, because he is one who missed the Hajj. And if he can reach the Hajj and the Hadi, then proceeding becomes obligatory upon him, because the inability (that prevented him) has been removed before the purpose was achieved by the substitute (the Hadi).
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling concerning a qarin who had sent a Hadi (sacrificial animal) to be slaughtered on his behalf on a specific day, but then the barrier (ihsar) is lifted before that day. The text outlines two scenarios explicitly. First scenario: If, after the removal of ihsar, he cannot reach Mecca in time to perform the Hajj rites nor can he catch the Hadi (i.e., the appointed slaughter time has passed), then he is not obligated to proceed to Mecca. Instead, he should remain in place and await the slaughter of the Hadi (by the appointed agents), which will effect his tahallul (exit from ihram). The reason given is that the purpose of proceeding—performing the actual Hajj rites—has become impossible (fawat). However, if he voluntarily proceeds to Mecca to complete a valid Umrah and thus become halal, he is permitted to do so, because he is now considered to have missed the Hajj (fa'it al-hajj), and the ruling for one who missed the Hajj is that he may exit ihram through Umrah. Second scenario: If he can still reach both the Hajj and the Hadi (i.e., there is enough time), then proceeding becomes obligatory upon him. The reason is that the inability (al-ajz) that justified the initial sending of the Hadi and the plan to exit through it has been removed before the purpose (the actual Hajj) was achieved by the substitute (the Hadi). Since he can now perform the rites himself, the original obligation revives. This ruling balances the principles of necessity (dhurura) and ability (istita'a) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
خلف (khalaf): A substitute; here, the Hadi sent acts as a substitute for personal performance.
فائت الحج (fāʾit al-ḥajj): One who missed the Hajj (due to failure to reach Arafat in time).
عجز (ʿajz): Inability, the condition that justifies alternative means like sending Hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a qarin muhsar sent a Hadi and then the barrier is removed, under which condition is proceeding to Mecca wajib?
A) When he cannot reach the Hajj.
B) When he can reach both Hajj and Hadi.
C) When he can reach the Hadi but not the Hajj.
D) Always, because the Hadi was sent as a substitute.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to proceed after ihsar removal is conditional on the ability to reach both the Hajj and the Hadi; inability to reach both removes the obligation.

The Fourth Scenario for Qarin Muhsar: Reaching Hajj but Not the Hadi
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the fourth scenario for qarin muhsar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the fourth scenario of the qarin muhsar and evaluate the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
Reaching Hajj does not automatically mean reaching the hadi — Abu Hanifa permits halal by istihsan, while the Sahibayn say it's impossible.

We previously covered three scenarios for the qarin muhsar. The fourth is more nuanced: what if he can perform Hajj but his sacrificial animal (hadi) is lost? Abu Hanifa allows him to become halal without proceeding, based on istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve his wealth. The Sahibayn, however, argue that the very possibility cannot arise because the dam of ihsar is fixed to Yawm al-Nahr, so anyone who reaches Hajj can slaughter on that day. This intra-Hanafi dispute illustrates how underlying principles like the timing of an obligation can lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourth scenario
The fourth scenario is: a qarin muhsar can reach the rites of Hajj (i.e., he can get to Mecca in time) but cannot reach his hadi (the animal sent ahead). The text asks: what is the ruling?
This scenario is only possible if the hadi is lost or inaccessible despite the pilgrim being able to travel.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa says the muhsar may become halal (i.e., exit ihram) even without proceeding, based on istihsan. The reasoning: the hadi is the pilgrim's property; forcing him to proceed would waste his wealth, and the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life.
The istihsan overrides the default qiyas that would obligate proceeding.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its basis
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the fourth scenario cannot occur. Their basis: the dam (sacrificial blood) for ihsar is fixed exclusively to Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul-Hijjah). Therefore, anyone who reaches Hajj can also slaughter the hadi on that day, so it is impossible to reach Hajj without access to the hadi.
Their view depends on a rule that the dam is time-bound, which Abu Hanifa does not accept.
4
Trace the root of the dispute
The core difference is whether dam al-ihsar is tied to Yawm al-Nahr. The Sahibayn say it is, so the scenario collapses. Abu Hanifa says it is not, so the scenario is possible. This difference leads to opposite conclusions about the muhsar's options.
The dispute also affects the case of a muhrim for Umrah alone, where the dam is not fixed to a day by agreement, so the division applies uniformly.
5
Apply the usul principle: qiyas vs. istihsan
The passage explicitly contrasts qiyas (Zufar's view, also implicit as default) and istihsan (the Hanafi relied-upon view). Qiyas would obligate proceeding because the pilgrim can perform the original (Hajj) before the substitute (hadi) achieves its purpose. Istihsan overrides because wealth preservation is a stronger consideration.
The muhsar is given a choice: wait for the hadi to be slaughtered or proceed to perform Hajj (the latter being better as it fulfills his pledge).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا أَدْرَكَ هَدْيَهُ صَنَعَ بِهِ مَاشَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ مِلْكُهُ وَقَدْ كَانَ عَيَّنَهُ لِمَقْصُودِ اسْتَغْنَى عَنْهُ. وَ إِنْ كَانَ يُدْرِكَ الْهَدَى دُونَ الْحَجِّ يَتَحَلَّلَ لِعَجْزِهِ عَنِ الْأَصْلِ. وَإِنْ كَانَ يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ دُونَ الْهَدْيِ جَازَ لَهُ التَحَلَّلُ اسْتِحْسَانًا وَهذَا التَّفْسِيمُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا فِي الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْحَجِّ لِأَنَّ دَمَ الْإِحْصَارِ عِنْدَهُمَا يَتَوَقَّتُ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَمَنْ يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ يُدْرِكُ الْهَدَى وَإِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ فِى الْمُحْرِمِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ يَسْتَقِيمُ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لِعَدَمِ تَوَقُّتِ الدَّمِ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ. وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ أنَّهُ قَدَرَ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ وَهُوَ الْحَجُّ قَبْلَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِالْبَدَلِ وَهُوَ الْهَدَى. وَوَجْهُ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّا لَوْ الْزَمْنَاهُ التَوَجَّهَ لَضَاعَ مَالَهُ لِأَنَّ الْمَبْعُوثَ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ الْهُدَى لِيَذْبَحُهُ وَلَا يَحْصُلُ مَقْصُودُهُ وَحُرْمَةُ الْمَالِ كَحُرْمَةِ النَّفْسِ. وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِنْ شَاءَ صَبَرَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْمَكَانِ أَو فِي غَيْرِهِ لِيُذْبَحَ عَنْهُ فَيَتَحَلَّلَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَوَجَّهَ لِيُؤَدِّيَ النُّسُكَ الَّذِى الْتَزَمَهُ بِالْإِحْرَامِ وَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الْوَفَاءِ بِمَا وَعَدَ.
And when he finds his hadi, he may do with it whatever he wishes, because it is his property, and he had designated it for a purpose for which he no longer needs it. And if he can reach the hadi but not the Hajj, he becomes halal because he is incapable of the original. And if he can reach the Hajj but not the hadi, becoming halal is permissible for him by istihsan. And this division is not correct according to the two (Sahibayn) in the case of one muhsar in Hajj, because the blood of ihsar according to them is fixed to the Day of Nahr; so whoever reaches the Hajj reaches the hadi. Rather, it is correct according to Abu Hanifa. And in the case of one in ihrām for Umrah, it is correct by agreement, because the blood is not fixed to the Day of Nahr. The face of qiyas (Zufar's view) is that he gained ability over the original (Hajj) before the purpose was achieved by the substitute (hadi). The face of istihsan is that if we made it obligatory for him to proceed, his wealth would be wasted, because the hadi sent with him is to be slaughtered, and his purpose would not be achieved, and the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. And he has the choice: if he wishes, he may wait in that place or another for it to be slaughtered on his behalf and thus become halal; and if he wishes, he may proceed to perform the ritual that he obligated upon himself by ihrām, and this is better because it is closer to fulfilling what he pledged.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage completes the four scenarios for the qarin muhsar. Third scenario: He reaches the hadi but not Hajj. Since he is unable to perform Hajj, he becomes halal by the slaughter of the hadi. Fourth scenario: He reaches Hajj but not the hadi (i.e., he can get to Mecca in time for Hajj but his sacrificial animal cannot be brought to him). According to istihsan, he may become halal (i.e., he is not obliged to proceed) because if we forced him to proceed, his wealth (the hadi) would be wasted; the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. However, this fourth scenario is only valid according to Abu Hanifa, not the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The Sahibayn hold that the dam for ihsar (the sacrificial blood) is fixed to the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), so if one can reach Hajj, he can also slaughter the hadi on that day, making the fourth scenario impossible. Abu Hanifa holds that the dam is not fixed to that day, so it is possible to reach Hajj without the hadi. For someone in ihrām for Umrah alone, the division applies by agreement of all scholars because there is no fixed day. The passage then contrasts qiyas (Zufar's view that proceeding is obligatory since he can do the original) with istihsan (which permits not proceeding due to wealth preservation). The person has a choice: wait to become halal via the hadi, or proceed to perform the Hajj (which is better as it fulfills his obligation).

Key Terms
دم الأحصار (dam al-iḥṣār): The sacrificial animal required due to being blocked (muhsar) from completing Hajj or Umrah.
استحسان (istiḥsān): A juristic preference that abandons qiyas in favor of a stronger legal consideration; here, preservation of wealth overrides the analogy.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the root cause of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the fourth scenario?
A) Whether the muhsar can proceed voluntarily.
B) Whether dam al-ihsar is fixed to Yawm al-Nahr.
C) Whether the hadi must be a sheep.
D) Whether the qarin can separate Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa permits the qarin muhsar who reaches Hajj but not his hadi to become halal without proceeding, based on istihsan preserving his wealth, while the Sahibayn deny the scenario because they tie the dam to Yawm al-Nahr.

Three Scenarios for the Muhsir Finding Hadya or Hajj
Three rulings for a muhsir regarding hadya and Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for a muhsir who finds his hadya or the Hajj, and identify the ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
A muhsir's hadya becomes optional if Hajj is now reachable, but necessary if Hajj remains unattainable.

The Hidayah presents three distinct situations for a muhsir who has sent a hadya ahead and later finds either the animal or the possibility of completing Hajj. Each situation has a different ruling based on the muhsir's ability to reach the original Hajj. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the rules of ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three cases: (a) finds hadya, (b) finds hadya but not Hajj, (c) finds Hajj but not hadya.
The text describes these explicitly.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For (a): he may do whatever he wishes with the hadya. For (b): he becomes halal by the hadya. For (c): it is permissible to become halal by istihsan.
Istihsan means juristic preference; it will be analyzed later.
3
Understand the underlying logic
For (a): the hadya was designated for tahallul due to ihsar, but since the obstacle is removed, that purpose no longer exists. For (b): he is incapable of the original (Hajj), so the substitute suffices. For (c): he is capable of Hajj but would lose his hadya wealth if forced to proceed.
Protection of wealth (hifz al-mal) is a key consideration.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text notes that this threefold division is valid according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the Sahibayn for a muhsir of Hajj, because they tie dam al-ihsar to Yawm al-Nahr. The reason for the disagreement will be explored in the next lesson.
This dispute only affects scenario (c).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر ہدی کو پالے جو چاہے اس کے ساتھ کرے وَإِذَا أَدْرَكَ هَدْيَهُ صَنَعَ بِهِ مَاشَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ مِلْكُهُ وَقَدْ كَانَ عَيَّنَهُ لِمَقْصُودِ اسْتَغْنَى عَنْهُ ترجمہ اور جب وہ اپنے بدی کو پائے تو اس کے ساتھ جو چاہے کرے کیونکہ یہ اس کی ملک ہے اور اس نے اس کو ایسے مقصود کے واسطے اور وہ بدی اسکے ساتھ یہ کی ملکہے نامزد کیا تھا جس کی ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں گذشتہ صورت کا تمہ ہے یعنی جب اس نے اپنے ہدی کو پایا تو وہ اس کو جو چاہے کرے خواہ فروخت کرے خواہ صدقہ کر دے کیونکہ یہ ہدی اس کی ملک ہے اور اس نے اس ہدی کو ایسے مقصد کے لئے متعین کیا تھا جس کی ضرورت نہیں رہی یعنی اس کو متعین کر دیا گیا تھا کہ محصر اسکے ذبح ہونے سے پہلے حلال ہو جائے۔ لیکن جب احصار زائل ہو گیا اور حج کو پانے کا امکان ہے اور یہ فریضہ حج ادا کرنے کے لئے مکہ چلا بھی گیا تو اب اس بدی کی اس مقصد میں کیا ضرورت رہی اور جب اس کی ضرورت نہ رہی تو اس کا جو چاہے کرے۔ ہدی کو پا سکے نہ کہ حج کو تو حلال ہو جائے وَ إِنْ كَانَ يُدْرِكَ الْهَدَى دُونَ الْحَج يَتَحَلَّلَ لِعِجْزِهِ عَنِ الْأَصْلِ ترجمہ اور اگر وہ ہنی کو پا سکتا ہے نہ کہ حج کو تو حلال ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ اصل یعنی حج سے عاجز ہے۔ تشریح اس تیسری صورت میں ہدی ذبح ہونے پر حلال ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ شخص اصل یعنی حج سے تو عاجز ہی ہے۔ پس بدی کو ذبح ہونے دے تاکہ حلال ہونے کا فائدہ حاصل ہو۔ حج کو پالے نہ کہ ہدی کو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے وَإِنْ كَانَ يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ دُونَ الْهَدْيِ جَازَلَهُ التَحَلَّلُ اسْتِحْسَانًا وَهذَا التَّفْسِيمُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا فِي الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْحَقِّ لِأَنَّ دَمَ الأحْصَارِ عِنْدَهُمَا يَتَوَفَّتُ يَومِ النَّحْرَ فَمَنْ يُدْرِكُ الْحَيَّ يُدْرِكُ الْهَدَى وَإِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ فِى الْمُحْرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ يَسْتَقِيمُ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لِعَدَمِ تَوَفَّتِ الدَّمِ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَجُهُ الْقِيَاسِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ أنَّهُ قَدْرَ عَلَى الْأصل وَهُوَ الْحَيُّ قَبْلَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِالْبَدَلِ وَهُوَ الْهَدَى وَوَجهُ الإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَا لَوْ الْزَمْنَاهُ التَوَجَّهَ لَضَاعَ مَالَهُ لِأَنَّ الْمَبْعُوثُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ الْهُدَى لِيَذْبَحُهُ وَلَا يَحْصُلُ مَقْصُوده و حُرْمَةُ المَالِ كَحُرُمَةِ النَّفْسَ وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِنْ شَاءَ صَبَرَ فِى ذَلِكَ الْمَكَانِ أَو فِي غَيْرِهِ لِيُذْبَحَ عَنْهُ فَيْتَحَلَّلَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَوَجَّه لِيُؤَدِّيَ النُّسُكَ الَّذِى التَزَمَةَ بِالإحْرَامِ وَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الوَفَاءِ بِمَا وَعَدَ ود ترجمہ اور اگر وہ حج پا سکتا ہو نہ کہ ہدی تو اس کے لئے استحسانا حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے قول کی بناء پر محصر بالج کے حق میں یہ تقسیم درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ پس جو شخص حج کو پائے گا وہ ہدی بھی پائے گا۔ اور اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ۵۰۹ کتاب المجمد ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے اور محصر بالعمرہ کے حق میں بالا تفاق درست ہے کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی کو ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور قیاس کی وجہ یہی امام زفر کا قول ہے کہ وہ اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا بدل یعنی بدی کے ساتھ مقصود کو حاصل کرنے سے پہلے ۔ اور وجه استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس محصر کے ذمہ مکہ کی طرف جانا لازم کریں تو اس کا مال ضائع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جسکے ہاتھوں اس نے ہدی بھیجی ہے وہ اس کو ضرور ذبح کر دے گا اور اس کا مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور مال کی حرمت جیسے جان کی حرمت ہے۔ اور اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے اس جگہ یا دوسری جگہ صبر کرے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبح کر دے اور اگر چاہے متوجہ ہوتا کہ وہ نسک ادا کرے جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے۔ اور یہ افضل ہے کیونکہ وفائے وعدہ سے قریب تر ہے۔ تشریح چوتھی صورت یعنی محصر بالج اگر ج پا سکتا ہوگر ہی نہ پا سکتا ہو تو استحسانا اس کے لئے حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ مکہ کو جا کر افعال حج ادا کرے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مصر بالج کے حق میں صاحبین کے قول پر یہ قسم درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ پس جو حج کو پاسکے گا وہ ہدی کو بھی پائے گا۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ یوم نحر سے پہلے بھی اس کو ذبح کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ کوئی شخص حج کو تو پا لے مگر ہدی کو نہ پائے۔ اور مصر بالعمرہ میں بالا تفاق درست ہے۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ پس ہوسکتا ہے کہ مصر بالعمرہ، عمرہ کو تو پالے مگر ہدی کو نہ پاسکے۔ وجہ قیاس جو امام زفر کا قول بھی ہے، یہ ہے کہ محصر ، بدل یعنی ہدی کے ساتھ مقصود حاصل ہونے سے پہلے اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا ہے اور ایسی صورت میں بدل اور خلیفہ سے مقصود حاصل نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ اصل کو ادا کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے یہ بھی حج کے ارکان ادا کرے اور بدی ذبح کر کے حلال نہ ہو۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس مصر کے ذمہ مکہ جانا لازم کر دیں تو اس کا مال یعنی بدی ضائع ہو گا یعنی وہ کسی مصرف کی نہ رہے گی اور آدمی پر جس طرح جان کی حفاظت ضروری ہے اسی طرح مال کی حفاظت بھی ضروری ہے۔ اب اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اسی جگہ یا دوسری جگہ ٹھہرا رہے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبیح ہو جائے اور یہ حلال ہو جائے اور اگر چاہے تو مکہ چلا جائے ۔ تا کہ وہ نسک یعنی حج یا عمرہ جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے اس کو ادا کرے اور یہی افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اللهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ میں جس کا وعدہ کیا تھا یہ اس کو پورا کرنے سے قریب تر ہے۔
If he finds his hadya, he may do with it whatever he wishes, because it is his property and he had designated it for a purpose from which he is now free. And if he finds the hadya but not the Hajj, he becomes halal due to his incapacity for the original. And if he finds the Hajj but not the hadya, it is permissible for him to become halal by istihsan. This division is not valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) for the muhsir of Hajj, because according to them the dam al-ihsar is tied to Yawm al-Nahr; whoever finds the Hajj will find the hadya. It is valid according to Abu Hanifa and by consensus for the muhsir of Umrah because the blood is not tied to Yawm al-Nahr. The basis of qiyas (and the view of Zufar) is that he became capable of the original (Hajj) before obtaining the purpose through the substitute (hadya). The basis of istihsan is that if we oblige him to proceed, his wealth would be wasted, and the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. He has the choice: if he wishes, he may stay in that place or another so that the hadya is sacrificed on his behalf and he becomes halal; if he wishes, he may proceed to perform the ritual (nusk) which he obligated himself to by ihram, and this is better because it is closer to fulfilling his vow.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah and presents three rulings concerning a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah) who had sent a hadya (sacrificial animal) ahead. The first ruling: if the muhsir later finds his hadya (the animal reaches him), he may do whatever he wishes with it – sell, give as charity, etc. – because the specific purpose for which it was designated (to be sacrificed to allow tahallul before the removal of ihsar) is no longer needed; he is now able to complete Hajj. The second ruling: if he finds the hadya but cannot reach the Hajj (the time or opportunity for Hajj is lost), then he becomes halal (released from ihram) simply by the sacrifice of the hadya, because he is incapable of the original act (Hajj). The third ruling: if he finds the Hajj (can reach it) but does not find the hadya, it is permissible for him to become halal by istihsan (juristic preference). The author then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: this division of cases is not valid according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) for a muhsir of Hajj, because they hold that the blood (dam al-ihsar) is determined (mutawaqqit) to Yawm al-Nahr; therefore, whoever can reach Hajj will also be able to find the hadya on that day. It is valid according to Abu Hanifa because he holds that the blood is not restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. For a muhsir of Umrah, the division is valid by consensus because Umrah's hadya is not tied to a specific day. The text then presents qiyas (analogy) – the view of Imam Zufar – which would require the muhsir to proceed to Hajj and not become halal by the hadya, since he became capable of the original before the substitute fulfilled its purpose. However, istihsan overrides this qiyas because obliging him to go to Makkah would cause loss of his hadya (it would be sacrificed and he would not benefit from it), and protecting wealth is similar to protecting life. He is given a choice: either stay and let the hadya be sacrificed to become halal, or proceed to perform the Hajj, which is better as it fulfills the commitment made in the talbiyah.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣir): A person in ihram who is prevented from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah by an enemy or illness.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhrim, either as a qurban or as a penalty for ihsar.
تحلل (taḥallul): The act of leaving ihram and becoming halal (permitted to do previously prohibited acts).
دم احصار (dam al-iḥṣār): The blood (sacrifice) required from a muhsir to become halal.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason, such as preventing harm (hifz al-mal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a muhsir of Hajj finds the Hajj but not his hadya, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) He must proceed to Hajj and cannot become halal without the hadya.
B) It is permissible for him to become halal by staying for the hadya to be sacrificed, and proceeding to Hajj is better.
C) He must wait until the hadya arrives even if he misses Hajj.
D) The hadya becomes void and he must send another.

Key Takeaway
A muhsir who finds Hajj but not hadya has the option to become halal by istihsan, and proceeding to Hajj is better.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Istihsan vs Qiyas for the Muhsir of Hajj
Intra-Hanafi dispute over validity of division for muhsir of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the muhsir of Hajj who finds Hajj but not hadya, and evaluate the role of istihsan in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
Istihsan overrides qiyas when protecting wealth equals protecting life, giving the muhsir a choice.

While the previous lesson outlined the three scenarios, this lesson delves into the specific disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples regarding the third scenario. The passage also introduces qiyas (Zufar's view) and the istihsan-based response. Understanding the interplay between qiyas and istihsan is key to mastering Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of dispute
The dispute is about whether the threefold division (especially scenario 3) is valid for a muhsir of Hajj. Abu Hanifa says yes; the Sahibayn say no.
2
Understand the reasoning of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn hold that dam al-ihsar is tied to Yawm al-Nahr. Therefore, a muhsir who can reach Hajj on that day will inevitably find his hadya (since it must be sacrificed that day). Hence, scenario 3 (finding Hajj but not hadya) does not occur.
This eliminates the need for a separate ruling.
3
Understand the reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa does not tie dam al-ihsar to Yawm al-Nahr; it can be sacrificed anytime. Therefore, a muhsir might find Hajj but his hadya could be lost or delayed, so scenario 3 is possible.
4
Analyze the qiyas (Zufar's view)
Qiyas would require the muhsir to proceed to Hajj because he became capable of the original before the substitute achieved its purpose. This view is ascribed to Zufar.
5
Understand the istihsan argument
Istihsan overrides qiyas because forcing the muhsir to proceed would waste his hadya (wealth). The sanctity of wealth is compared to that of life. He is given a choice; proceeding is better (afdal).
This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

کہ حج کو تو حلال ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ یہ اصل یعنی حج سے عاجز ہے۔ تشریح اس تیسری صورت میں ہدی ذبح ہونے پر حلال ہو جائے گا کیونکہ یہ شخص اصل یعنی حج سے تو عاجز ہی ہے۔ پس بدی کو ذبح ہونے دے تاکہ حلال ہونے کا فائدہ حاصل ہو۔ حج کو پالے نہ کہ ہدی کو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے وَإِنْ كَانَ يُدْرِكُ الْحَجَّ دُونَ الْهَدْيِ جَازَلَهُ التَحَلَّلُ اسْتِحْسَانًا وَهذَا التَّفْسِيمُ لَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلَى قَوْلِهِمَا فِي الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْحَقِّ لِأَنَّ دَمَ الأحْصَارِ عِنْدَهُمَا يَتَوَفَّتُ يَومِ النَّحْرَ فَمَنْ يُدْرِكُ الْحَيَّ يُدْرِكُ الْهَدَى وَإِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ عَلى قَوْلِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ فِى الْمُحْرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ يَسْتَقِيمُ بِالْاِتِّفَاقِ لِعَدَمِ تَوَفَّتِ الدَّمِ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَجُهُ الْقِيَاسِ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ أنَّهُ قَدْرَ عَلَى الْأصل وَهُوَ الْحَيُّ قَبْلَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ بِالْبَدَلِ وَهُوَ الْهَدَى وَوَجهُ الإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَا لَوْ الْزَمْنَاهُ التَوَجَّهَ لَضَاعَ مَالَهُ لِأَنَّ الْمَبْعُوثُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ الْهُدَى لِيَذْبَحُهُ وَلَا يَحْصُلُ مَقْصُوده و حُرْمَةُ المَالِ كَحُرُمَةِ النَّفْسَ وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِنْ شَاءَ صَبَرَ فِى ذَلِكَ الْمَكَانِ أَو فِي غَيْرِهِ لِيُذْبَحَ عَنْهُ فَيْتَحَلَّلَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَوَجَّه لِيُؤَدِّيَ النُّسُكَ الَّذِى التَزَمَةَ بِالإحْرَامِ وَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ لأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَى الوَفَاءِ بِمَا وَعَدَ ود ترجمہ اور اگر وہ حج پا سکتا ہو نہ کہ ہدی تو اس کے لئے استحسانا حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے قول کی بناء پر محصر بالج کے حق میں یہ تقسیم درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ پس جو شخص حج کو پائے گا وہ ہدی بھی پائے گا۔ اور اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم ۵۰۹ کتاب المجمد ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے اور محصر بالعمرہ کے حق میں بالا تفاق درست ہے کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی کو ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور قیاس کی وجہ یہی امام زفر کا قول ہے کہ وہ اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا بدل یعنی بدی کے ساتھ مقصود کو حاصل کرنے سے پہلے ۔ اور وجه استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس محصر کے ذمہ مکہ کی طرف جانا لازم کریں تو اس کا مال ضائع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جسکے ہاتھوں اس نے ہدی بھیجی ہے وہ اس کو ضرور ذبح کر دے گا اور اس کا مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور مال کی حرمت جیسے جان کی حرمت ہے۔ اور اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے اس جگہ یا دوسری جگہ صبر کرے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبح کر دے اور اگر چاہے متوجہ ہوتا کہ وہ نسک ادا کرے جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے۔ اور یہ افضل ہے کیونکہ وفائے وعدہ سے قریب تر ہے۔ تشریح چوتھی صورت یعنی محصر بالج اگر ج پا سکتا ہوگر ہی نہ پا سکتا ہو تو استحسانا اس کے لئے حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ مکہ کو جا کر افعال حج ادا کرے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مصر بالج کے حق میں صاحبین کے قول پر یہ قسم درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ پس جو حج کو پاسکے گا وہ ہدی کو بھی پائے گا۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ یوم نحر سے پہلے بھی اس کو ذبح کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ کوئی شخص حج کو تو پا لے مگر ہدی کو نہ پائے۔ اور مصر بالعمرہ میں بالا تفاق درست ہے۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ پس ہوسکتا ہے کہ مصر بالعمرہ، عمرہ کو تو پالے مگر ہدی کو نہ پاسکے۔ وجہ قیاس جو امام زفر کا قول بھی ہے، یہ ہے کہ محصر ، بدل یعنی ہدی کے ساتھ مقصود حاصل ہونے سے پہلے اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا ہے اور ایسی صورت میں بدل اور خلیفہ سے مقصود حاصل نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ اصل کو ادا کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے یہ بھی حج کے ارکان ادا کرے اور بدی ذبح کر کے حلال نہ ہو۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس مصر کے ذمہ مکہ جانا لازم کر دیں تو اس کا مال یعنی بدی ضائع ہو گا یعنی وہ کسی مصرف کی نہ رہے گی اور آدمی پر جس طرح جان کی حفاظت ضروری ہے اسی طرح مال کی حفاظت بھی ضروری ہے۔ اب اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اسی جگہ یا دوسری جگہ ٹھہرا رہے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبیح ہو جائے اور یہ حلال ہو جائے اور اگر چاہے تو مکہ چلا جائے ۔ تا کہ وہ نسک یعنی حج یا عمرہ جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے اس کو ادا کرے اور یہی افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اللهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ میں جس کا وعدہ کیا تھا یہ اس کو پورا کرنے سے قریب تر ہے۔
If he finds his hadya, he may do with it whatever he wishes, because it is his property and he had designated it for a purpose from which he is now free. And if he finds the hadya but not the Hajj, he becomes halal due to his incapacity for the original. And if he finds the Hajj but not the hadya, it is permissible for him to become halal by istihsan. This division is not valid according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) for the muhsir of Hajj, because according to them the dam al-ihsar is tied to Yawm al-Nahr; whoever finds the Hajj will find the hadya. It is valid according to Abu Hanifa and by consensus for the muhsir of Umrah because the blood is not tied to Yawm al-Nahr. The basis of qiyas (and the view of Zufar) is that he became capable of the original (Hajj) before obtaining the purpose through the substitute (hadya). The basis of istihsan is that if we oblige him to proceed, his wealth would be wasted, and the sanctity of wealth is like the sanctity of life. He has the choice: if he wishes, he may stay in that place or another so that the hadya is sacrificed on his behalf and he becomes halal; if he wishes, he may proceed to perform the ritual (nusk) which he obligated himself to by ihram, and this is better because it is closer to fulfilling his vow.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Hidayah and presents three rulings concerning a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah) who had sent a hadya (sacrificial animal) ahead. The first ruling: if the muhsir later finds his hadya (the animal reaches him), he may do whatever he wishes with it – sell, give as charity, etc. – because the specific purpose for which it was designated (to be sacrificed to allow tahallul before the removal of ihsar) is no longer needed; he is now able to complete Hajj. The second ruling: if he finds the hadya but cannot reach the Hajj (the time or opportunity for Hajj is lost), then he becomes halal (released from ihram) simply by the sacrifice of the hadya, because he is incapable of the original act (Hajj). The third ruling: if he finds the Hajj (can reach it) but does not find the hadya, it is permissible for him to become halal by istihsan (juristic preference). The author then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: this division of cases is not valid according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) for a muhsir of Hajj, because they hold that the blood (dam al-ihsar) is determined (mutawaqqit) to Yawm al-Nahr; therefore, whoever can reach Hajj will also be able to find the hadya on that day. It is valid according to Abu Hanifa because he holds that the blood is not restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. For a muhsir of Umrah, the division is valid by consensus because Umrah's hadya is not tied to a specific day. The text then presents qiyas (analogy) – the view of Imam Zufar – which would require the muhsir to proceed to Hajj and not become halal by the hadya, since he became capable of the original before the substitute fulfilled its purpose. However, istihsan overrides this qiyas because obliging him to go to Makkah would cause loss of his hadya (it would be sacrificed and he would not benefit from it), and protecting wealth is similar to protecting life. He is given a choice: either stay and let the hadya be sacrificed to become halal, or proceed to perform the Hajj, which is better as it fulfills the commitment made in the talbiyah.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣir): A person in ihram who is prevented from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah by an enemy or illness.
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhrim, either as a qurban or as a penalty for ihsar.
تحلل (taḥallul): The act of leaving ihram and becoming halal (permitted to do previously prohibited acts).
دم احصار (dam al-iḥṣār): The blood (sacrifice) required from a muhsir to become halal.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason, such as preventing harm (hifz al-mal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a muhsir of Hajj finds the Hajj but not his hadya, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) He must proceed to Hajj and cannot become halal without the hadya.
B) It is permissible for him to become halal by staying for the hadya to be sacrificed, and proceeding to Hajj is better.
C) He must wait until the hadya arrives even if he misses Hajj.
D) The hadya becomes void and he must send another.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on the muhsir of Hajj highlights how ikhtilaf arises from differing views on the timing of dam al-ihsar, and istihsan overrides qiyas to protect wealth.
