Defining the Muhsir: After Wuquf, No Ihsar
Defines the legal boundaries of ihsar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who is considered a muhsir and apply it to scenarios involving prevention after Wuquf or from Tawaf.

Core Idea
After Wuquf, prevention does not make you muhsir—the Hajj is locked in.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the precise definition of a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj). It distinguishes between prevention after the essential pillar of Wuquf and prevention before it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining whether the special rulings of ihsar apply, including sending a sacrifice and becoming halal.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario of prevention after Wuquf
The passage first says if someone stood at Arafah then is prevented, they are not muhsir because they are secure from fawat (total loss of Hajj).
Fawat is avoided once Wuquf is performed.
2
State the scenario of prevention from both Tawaf and Wuquf
If prevented from both, they are muhsir because completion of Hajj is impossible. This is analogous to being prevented in the hill (outside Haram).
The analogy uses qiyas: like being prevented outside Haram.
3
Analyze the partial ability exception
If able to perform one of the two, not muhsir. For Tawaf, the reason is that the one who misses Hajj becomes halal through Tawaf and the blood (sacrifice) is a substitute for tahallul. For Wuquf, the reason is as previously stated.
The text gives separate reasoning for each.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is mentioned, but the text states the correct position is the detailed explanation provided.
The exact view of Abu Yusuf is not specified.
5
Apply the ruling to new cases
Use the thamarah: a person after Wuquf does not have to send a sacrifice for ihsar; they must complete rites when able. A person prevented from both can send a sacrifice and become halal.
This is the practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ ثُمَّ أَحْصِرَ لَا يَكُونُ مُحْصَرًا لِوُقُوعِ الأمَنِ عَنِ الْفَوَاتِ وَمَنْ أَحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنِ الطَّوَافِ وَالْوُقُوفِ فَهُوَ مُحْصَرُ الأَنَّهُ تَعَدَّرَ عَلَيْهِ الإِثْمَامُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَحْصَرَ فِى الْحِلِ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَرٍ أَمَّا عَلَى الطَّوَافِ فَلِأَنَّ فَايْتَ الْحَجّ يَتَحَلَّلُ بِهِ وَالدَّمُ بَدَل عَنْهُ فِى التَّحَلُّلِ وَأَمَّا عَلَى الْوُقوفِ فَلِمَا بَيَّنَا وَقَدْ قِيلَ فِى هَذِهِ المَسَئَلَةِ خِلافُ بَيْنَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَالصَّحِيحُ مَا أَعْلَمُتُكَ مِنَ التَّفْصِيل تر جمہ ... اور جوشخص عرفات کا وقوف کر چکا پھر وہ مصر ہوا تو وہ مصر نہیں : گا۔ کیونکہ حج فوت ہونے سے امن ہو چکا۔ اور جوشخص مکہ
And whoever has stood at Arafah then is prevented, he is not a muhsir because he is secure from the loss (of Hajj having occurred). And whoever is prevented in Makkah and is prevented from Tawaf and Wuquf, he is a muhsir because the completion (of Hajj) is impossible for him, so it becomes as if he were prevented in the non-sanctuary. And if he is able to perform one of them (Tawaf or Wuquf), he is not a muhsir. As for Tawaf, because the one who misses Hajj becomes halal through it (Tawaf al-ifadha?) and the blood is a substitute for it in tahallul. As for Wuquf, according to what we stated. And it has been said in this issue there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the detailed explanation I have informed you.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage defines the legal status of a muhsir (one prevented from completing the rites) in two key situations. First: if a person has already performed the standing at Arafah (Wuquf) and then becomes prevented from completing the remaining rites, he is not considered a muhsir. The reason is that Wuquf is the essential pillar of Hajj; once performed, there is security from fawat (total loss of Hajj) – he has already earned the reward and the obligation is fulfilled, though he may need to complete the rest. Second: if a person is in Makkah and is prevented from both Tawaf (the circumambulation) and Wuquf, he is a muhsir, because he is unable to complete the Hajj at all. This is analogous to being prevented outside the Haram. However, if he is able to perform either one of them, he is not a muhsir. The text then notes a reported difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding this ruling, but states that the correct position is the detailed explanation given (presumably the one just outlined). The Urdu translation (partially preserved) reiterates that after Wuquf, one is not muhsir because safety from fawat is achieved.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣir): A person in ihram prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah by an obstacle such as an enemy.
وقوف عرفة (wuqūf 'Arafah): The standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.
فوات (fawāt): The loss of Hajj by missing Wuquf before dawn on the 10th.
طواف (ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah; one of the obligatory acts of Hajj.
تحلل (taḥallul): The state of exiting ihram after completing the rites or due to ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who has performed Wuquf at Arafah and then becomes prevented from completing the remaining rites?
A) He is considered a muhsir and must send a hadya.
B) He is not considered a muhsir because he is secure from fawat.
C) He must repeat Hajj the next year.
D) He becomes halal immediately without sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
After performing Wuquf, a pilgrim is no longer considered a muhsir even if prevented from subsequent rites; muhsir status applies only when both Tawaf and Wuquf are impossible.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Muhsar bil-Hajj: Sending Hadi vs. Performing Hajj
Explanation of the fourth scenario of ihsar and the ruling on sending hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muhsar who can reach Hajj but not his hadi, and explain the istihsan argument that permits becoming halal by sending the hadi.

Core Idea
A muhsar can become halal by sending a hadi even if he can reach Makkah — istihsan protects property from waste.

This lesson unpacks the fourth scenario of ihsar (prevention) in Hajj: a pilgrim in ihram can physically reach the rites but his sacrificial animal (hadi) is delayed or inaccessible. The Hanafi school, through Imam Abu Hanifa, permits such a person to become halal by sending a hadi by proxy, based on istihsan. The Sahibayn and Imam Zufar disagree, arguing that if he can reach Hajj, he must perform it and cannot rely on a substitute. Understanding this dispute highlights the Hanafi methodology of balancing textual commitment with practical mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Fourth Scenario of Ihsar
Recognize the specific case: a muhsar (prevented pilgrim) can reach the rites of Hajj (e.g., Wuquf, Tawaf) but cannot bring his hadi to the Haram on time. The ruling differs from other scenarios.
This scenario is unique because the pilgrim is not completely blocked from Hajj, yet his hadi is unavailable.
2
State the Positions
Abu Hanifa: permissible to send a hadi and become halal. Sahibayn: not valid because hadi is tied to Day of Nahr. Zufar: qiyas requires performing original Hajj.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, not inter-madhhab.
3
Examine the Proofs
Sahibayn use the tie between hadi and Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). Zufar uses qiyas: ability to perform original makes substitute unnecessary. Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: forcing him to go wastes his property (hadi), and property is sacred.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here to prevent loss.
4
Extract the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the pilgrim can become halal immediately by arranging a hadi. Under Sahibayn/Zufar, he must go to Makkah or delay until the next year.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as presented in the text.
5
Note the Better Option
Although sending a hadi is permissible, going personally to perform Hajj is afdal (better) because it fulfills his vow and is closer to the original intent.
The text recommends performing the rites if possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
۵۰۹
کتاب المجمد ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے اور محصر بالعمرہ کے حق میں بالا تفاق درست ہے کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی کو ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین نہیں ہے۔ اور قیاس کی وجہ یہی امام زفر کا قول ہے کہ وہ اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا بدل یعنی بدی کے ساتھ مقصود کو حاصل کرنے سے پہلے ۔ اور وجه استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس محصر کے ذمہ مکہ کی طرف جانا لازم کریں تو اس کا مال ضائع ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جسکے ہاتھوں اس نے ہدی بھیجی ہے وہ اس کو ضرور ذبح کر دے گا اور اس کا مقصود حاصل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور مال کی حرمت جیسے جان کی حرمت ہے۔ اور اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے اس جگہ یا دوسری جگہ صبر کرے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبح کر دے اور اگر چاہے متوجہ ہوتا کہ وہ نسک ادا کرے جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے۔ اور یہ افضل ہے کیونکہ وفائے وعدہ سے قریب تر ہے۔
تشریح چوتھی صورت یعنی محصر بالج اگر ج پا سکتا ہوگر ہی نہ پا سکتا ہو تو استحسانا اس کے لئے حلال ہو جانا جائز ہے۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ مکہ کو جا کر افعال حج ادا کرے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مصر بالج کے حق میں صاحبین کے قول پر یہ قسم درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک دم احصار یوم نحر کے ساتھ متعین ہے۔ پس جو حج کو پاسکے گا وہ ہدی کو بھی پائے گا۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول پر درست ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے بلکہ یوم نحر سے پہلے بھی اس کو ذبح کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ممکن ہے کہ کوئی شخص حج کو تو پا لے مگر ہدی کو نہ پائے۔ اور مصر بالعمرہ میں بالا تفاق درست ہے۔ کیونکہ عمرہ کی ہدی یوم نحر کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ پس ہوسکتا ہے کہ مصر بالعمرہ، عمرہ کو تو پالے مگر ہدی کو نہ پاسکے۔
وجہ قیاس جو امام زفر کا قول بھی ہے، یہ ہے کہ محصر ، بدل یعنی ہدی کے ساتھ مقصود حاصل ہونے سے پہلے اصل یعنی حج پر قادر ہو گیا ہے اور ایسی صورت میں بدل اور خلیفہ سے مقصود حاصل نہیں کیا جاتا بلکہ اصل کو ادا کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے یہ بھی حج کے ارکان ادا کرے اور بدی ذبح کر کے حلال نہ ہو۔
اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ہم اگر اس مصر کے ذمہ مکہ جانا لازم کر دیں تو اس کا مال یعنی بدی ضائع ہو گا یعنی وہ کسی مصرف کی نہ رہے گی اور آدمی پر جس طرح جان کی حفاظت ضروری ہے اسی طرح مال کی حفاظت بھی ضروری ہے۔ اب اس کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو اسی جگہ یا دوسری جگہ ٹھہرا رہے تا کہ اس کی طرف سے ہدی ذبیح ہو جائے اور یہ حلال ہو جائے اور اگر چاہے تو مکہ چلا جائے ۔ تا کہ وہ نسک یعنی حج یا عمرہ جس کا احترام سے التزام کیا ہے اس کو ادا کرے اور یہی افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اللهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ میں جس کا وعدہ کیا تھا یہ اس کو پورا کرنے سے قریب تر ہے۔
The fourth scenario: Muhsar bil-J (prevented from completing Hajj) if he can reach Hajj but cannot reach the hadi, then it is permissible by istihsan for him to become halal by sending the hadi. However, it is better that he goes to Makkah to perform the rites of Hajj. The author of Hidayah states: According to the Sahibayn, this type (of becoming halal by sending hadi) is not valid for the muhsar bil-J, because in their view, the dam of ihsar is tied to the Day of Nahr. Thus whoever can reach Hajj will also reach the hadi. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is valid, because in his view, the hadi is not specific to the Day of Nahr; it can be slaughtered before. So it is possible that a person can reach Hajj but not the hadi. For the muhsar bil-umrah, it is valid by consensus, because the hadi of Umrah is not specific to the Day of Nahr. The basis of qiyas, which is also the view of Imam Zufar, is that the muhsar has become able to perform the original (Hajj) before achieving the aim through the substitute (hadi). In such a case, the aim is not achieved through the substitute; rather, the original is performed. So he should perform the rites of Hajj and not become halal by slaughtering the hadi. The basis of istihsan is that if we oblige this muhsar to go to Makkah, his property (the hadi) will be wasted, as the person to whom he sent the hadi will slaughter it, and his aim will not be achieved. And the sanctity of property is like the sanctity of life. He has the choice: if he wishes, he can remain in that place or another until his hadi is slaughtered and he becomes halal; if he wishes, he can go to Makkah to perform the rites (Hajj or Umrah) which he has committed to, and this is better, because it is closer to fulfilling his promise when he said 'O Allah, I intend Hajj'.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on the fourth scenario of ihsar (prevention) in Hajj. It deals with the case where a person is prevented from completing Hajj but can still physically reach Makkah for the rites, yet his sacrificial animal (hadi) is not with him. The key debate is between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad). According to the Sahibayn, the hadi must be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), so if a person can reach Hajj, he can also slaughter his hadi on time; thus sending a hadi by proxy does not allow him to become halal before reaching the hadi. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the hadi can be slaughtered any time after the Ihram, not specifically on the Day of Nahr, so it is possible for a person to reach Hajj but his hadi to be delayed; in such a case, he may send a hadi and become halal by proxy. The commentary then contrasts the qiyas (analogical reasoning) of Imam Zufar, who says that since the person can perform the original Hajj, the substitute (hadi) is abandoned, so he must perform Hajj and cannot become halal by the hadi. The istihsan (juristic preference) of Abu Hanifa is presented: obliging him to go to Makkah would waste his hadi (since the proxy will slaughter it anyway), and property is sacred like life, so he has a choice to wait for his hadi or go personally. The better option is to go and fulfill his vow.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣar): A person in the state of ihram who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
ہدی (hadī): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhsar or a pilgrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does Imam Abu Hanifa permit the muhsar bil-Hajj to become halal by sending a hadi even if he can reach Makkah?
A) Because the hadi can only be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr
B) Because forcing him to go would waste his property, and property is sacred
C) Because he has already performed Wuquf at Arafah
D) Because the Sahibayn agreed with this ruling

Key Takeaway
When a muhsar can reach the rites but not his hadi, Abu Hanifa's istihsan permits him to become halal by sending a hadi, though going personally is better.

Effect of Wuquf at Arafah on Ihsar and Prevention in Makkah
Ruling on who performs Wuquf then becomes prevented, and prevention in Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on ihsar for someone who performs wuquf and for someone prevented in Makkah, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
After standing at Arafah, one is secure from missing Hajj, so later prevention does not make one muhsar.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a critical nuance in the law of ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj). The key distinction is whether the essential act of wuquf at Arafah has already been performed. The author also addresses a scenario of prevention within Makkah itself, with a noted disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this ruling helps the student grasp the priority of wuquf in Hajj and the conditions that trigger ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Locate the two cases discussed: the pilgrim who performs wuquf then is prevented, and the pilgrim who is prevented in Makkah from both tawaf and wuquf. Note the ruling for each.
The passage begins with 'Man waqafa' and then 'Man uhsiro bi Makkah'.
2
Analyze the first ruling
For the one who stood at Arafah then becomes prevented: the text says he is not muhsar. Identify the reason: there is security from fawat (missing Hajj) because wuquf has been performed.
The author references a hadith that wuquf completes the Hajj.
3
Analyze the second ruling
For the one prevented in Makkah: if prevented from both tawaf and wuquf, he is muhsar because completion is impossible. If able to do one of them, he is not muhsar.
The text explains the rationale for each case: tawaf substitutes for missed Hajj; wuquf secures Hajj.
4
Examine the dalil
The implied dalil is a hadith: 'Whoever stands at Arafah has completed his Hajj.' This proves that wuquf is the essence, removing the possibility of fawat.
The hadith is mentioned in the commentary, not verbatim in the matn.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the case of being prevented in Makkah but able to do one act. The text deems the detailed view (if prevented from both, muhsar; if from one, not) as correct.
The tarjih is from the author of Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ ثُمَّ أَحْصِرَ لَا يَكُونُ مُحْصَرًا لِوُقُوعِ الأمَنِ عَنِ الْفَوَاتِ وَمَنْ أَحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنِ الطَّوَافِ وَالْوُقُوفِ فَهُوَ مُحْصَرُ الأَنَّهُ تَعَدَّرَ عَلَيْهِ الإِثْمَامُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَحْصَرَ فِى الْحِلِ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَرٍ أَمَّا عَلَى الطَّوَافِ فَلِأَنَّ فَايْتَ الْحَجّ يَتَحَلَّلُ بِهِ وَالدَّمُ بَدَل عَنْهُ فِى التَّحَلُّلِ وَأَمَّا عَلَى الْوُقوفِ فَلِمَا بَيَّنَا وَقَدْ قِيلَ فِى هَذِهِ المَسَئَلَةِ خِلافُ بَيْنَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَالصَّحِيحُ مَا أَعْلَمُتُكَ مِنَ التَّفْصِيل
And whoever has stood at Arafah then becomes prevented, he is not considered muhsar because there is security from the loss (of Hajj). And whoever is prevented in Makkah while being prevented from tawaf and wuquf, then he is muhsar because completion has become impossible for him, so he becomes like one who is prevented in the hall. And if he is able to do one of them, then he is not muhsar. As for tawaf, because the one who misses Hajj becomes halal through it, and the blood (dam) is a substitute for it in becoming halal. And as for wuquf, for the reason we have stated. And it has been said that in this issue there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the correct is the detail which I have informed you.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage presents two key rulings. First, if a person has performed the standing (wuquf) at Arafah and then is prevented from completing the remaining rites, he is not considered muhsar because the essential part of Hajj has been secured; the fear of missing Hajj (fawat) is removed. The author references a hadith that 'whoever stands at Arafah has completed his Hajj.' Thus, he does not have the option of becoming halal through sending a hadi for ihsar. However, Imam Abu Hanifa states that such a person still owes four dam (blood sacrifices) for missing other obligations: standing at Muzdalifah, throwing the stones, delaying tawaf al-ziyarah, and delaying halq. The Sahibayn hold that no dam is required for delaying tawaf and halq. Second, if a person is prevented in Makkah from both tawaf and wuquf (i.e., he cannot do either), then he is considered muhsar, as completion is impossible, similar to being prevented outside the Haram (hall). If he is able to perform one of them, he is not muhsar: if he can do tawaf, he becomes halal by it (as a substitute for the missed Hajj), and the dam (hadi) becomes unnecessary; if he can do wuquf, he has completed Hajj and is secure from fawat. The passage mentions a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa reportedly said that one prevented in Makkah but able to do either tawaf or wuquf is not muhsar, while Abu Yusuf held that such a person might still be muhsar. The text declares the correct view is the detailed one: if prevented from both, he is muhsar; if able to do one, he is not.

Key Terms
فوات (fawāt): The loss or missing of Hajj by failing to perform wuquf at Arafah in time.
حصر (ḥaṣr): Prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other obstacles.
طواف زیارت (ṭawāf al-ziyārah): The obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba that is a pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, who is considered muhsar?
A) Someone who has stood at Arafah then becomes prevented
B) Someone prevented in Makkah from both tawaf and wuquf
C) Someone prevented from tawaf only
D) Someone prevented from wuquf only

Key Takeaway
After performing wuquf at Arafah, a pilgrim is secure from missing Hajj and is not considered muhsar if prevented later; within Makkah, ihsar only applies if both tawaf and wuquf are impossible.

Muhsar in the Haram: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on muhsar in the Haram with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise conditions under which a person prevented in the Haram is considered muhsar according to the Hanafi school, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding this issue.

Core Idea
A person prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram is muhsar; preventing one does not suffice for ihsar.

This passage completes the discussion on ihsar by addressing a specific scenario: a person prevented inside the Haram. It presents a dispute between the school's founding imams and offers a detailed reconciliation that is relied upon in fatwa. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the rules of ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
First, understand that the passage focuses on a person in ihram who is prevented from performing both tawaf (circumambulation) and wuquf (standing at Arafah) while inside the Haram. This is a specific case of ihsar.
2
Understand the general ruling
The text states: if prevented from both, he is muhsar; if able to do either one, he is not muhsar. This is the foundational rule.
The reasoning is that the cause of ihsar is the fear of missing Hajj entirely, which is removed if one can still perform wuquf (the main pillar) or tawaf (the substitute for missing Hajj).
3
Trace the reasoning for ability to do one rite
If able to do tawaf but not wuquf, the person is fayit al-hajj and becomes halal through tawaf; sending a hadi is unnecessary because the original substitute is available. If able to do wuquf, his Hajj is complete and tawaf can be performed later, so no ihsar.
The hadith 'Whoever stands at Arafah has completed his Hajj' is cited to support the latter case.
4
Examine the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Some scholars report that Abu Hanifa considers the person prevented from both in the Haram as not muhsar, while Abu Yusuf considers him muhsar. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies that the correct view is the detailed one: both prevented → muhsar; one possible → not muhsar, and this is the statement of all Imams.
The dispute may have arisen from different interpretations of the term 'muhsar' or the application of qiyas.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects whether the person must send a hadi to become halal. According to the mufta bihi view, if both rites are impossible, he sends a hadi; if one is possible, he does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں روک دیا گیا درانحالیکہ وہ طواف اور وقوف سے ممنوع ہوا تو وہ محصر ہے کیونکہ اس پر پورا کرنا معذور ہو گیا بس ایسا ہوگیا جیسا کہ حل میں روکا گیا ہو۔ اور اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک پر قادر ہو گیا تو وہ محصر نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال جب طواف پر قادر ہوا تو اس لئے کہ فائت الحج طواف سے حلال ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ہدی بھیجنا حلال ہونے میں اس کا بدل ہے۔ اور بہر حال جب وقوف پر قادر ہوا تو اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ۔ اور کہا گیا کہ اس مسئلہ میں ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔ اور صحیح یہ تفصیل ہے جس سے میں نے تجھ کو آگاہ کیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، جس شخص نے عرفہ کا وقوف کیا پھر وہ اگلے ارکان ادا کرنے سے روک دیا گیا تو وہ محصر نہیں کہلائے گا۔ کیونکہ احصار کا سبب خوف فوات ہے حالانکہ وقوف عرفہ کے بعد اس سے امن ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے مَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَجُّهُ پس جب سبب احصار موجود نہیں رہا تو احصار بھی باقی نہ رہے گا۔ ہاں اتنی بات ہے کہ اس شخص پر امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک چار دم واجب ہوں گے۔ (1) وقوف مزدلفہ کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ (2) رمی جمار کو ترک کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ (3) طواف زیارت کو مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ (4) حلق کو مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک طواف زیارت اور حلق کو مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور جس شخص کو حرم میں اس حال میں روک دیا گیا کہ وہ نہ طواف کر سکا اور نہ وقوف عرفہ کر سکا تو وہ محصر کہلائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس پر حج کو پورا کرنا متعذر ہو گیا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کہ محل میں روک دیا گیا ہو۔ اب اگر شخص طواف اور وقوف میں سے کسی ایک پر قادر ہو گیا تو یہ محصر نہیں ہے یعنی ایسا محصر نہیں جو ہدی بھیج کر حلال ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر فقط طواف پر قادر ہوا نہ کہ وقوف عرفہ پر حتی کہ حج فوت ہو گیا تو یہ شخص فائت الحج ہوا۔ اور فائت الحج طواف سے حلال ہو جاتا ہے اور ہدی بھیجنا حلال ہونے میں اس کا بدل ہے۔ پس جب اصل پر قادر ہو گیا تو بدل بیکار ہے اور اگر وقوف عرفہ پر قادر ہے تو محصر نہ ہونا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ وقوف عرفہ سے حج مل گیا۔ اور فوت ہونے کا خوف نہ رہا۔ کیونکہ طواف تو جب چاہے کر لے، آخر عمر تک کر سکتا ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ اس مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کے درمیان اختلاف ہے۔ یعنی جو حرم میں طواف اور وقوف سے روک دیا گیا وہ ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک محصر نہیں ہے اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک محصر ہے۔ اور صحیح یہ ہے کہ یہ تفصیل سب کا قول ہے کہ اگر وقوف اور طواف دونوں سے ممنوع ہو تو محصر ہے۔ اور اگر ایک پر قادر ہو تو محصر نہیں ہے۔
He was prevented while he was prevented from tawaf and wuquf, so he is muhsar because completing (hajj) became impossible for him, so it became as if he was prevented in the Hal. And if he becomes able to do one of them, then he is not muhsar. In any case, when he becomes able to do tawaf, it is because the one who misses hajj becomes halal through tawaf, and sending a hadi is its substitute in becoming halal. And in any case, when he becomes able to do wuquf, it is due to the proof we mentioned. And it was said that in this issue there is a difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And the correct is this detail that I have informed you of. Explanation of the issue: A person who performed wuquf at Arafah and then was prevented from performing the remaining rites – he will not be called muhsar, because the cause of ihsar is fear of missing (hajj) while after wuquf at Arafah, that fear is removed. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stands at Arafah has completed his hajj.' So when the cause of ihsar no longer exists, ihsar will also not remain. However, in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, four dams become wajib upon this person: (1) due to leaving wuquf at Muzdalifah, (2) due to leaving ramy al-jimar, (3) due to delaying tawaf al-ziyarah, (4) due to delaying halq. And in the view of the Sahibayn, nothing becomes wajib due to delaying tawaf al-ziyarah and halq. And the person who is prevented in the Haram in such a way that he could neither perform tawaf nor wuquf at Arafah – he will be called muhsar, because completing hajj becomes impossible for him. So this becomes as if he was prevented in the Hal. Now if the person becomes able to do one of tawaf and wuquf, then he is not muhsar, i.e., not the muhsar who becomes halal by sending a hadi. Thus, if he becomes able only to do tawaf and not wuquf at Arafah, such that hajj is missed, then this person is fayit al-hajj. And the one who misses hajj becomes halal through tawaf, and sending a hadi is its substitute in becoming halal. So when he becomes able to do the original, the substitute is useless. And if he becomes able to do wuquf at Arafah, then he is not muhsar because hajj is attained through wuquf at Arafah and there is no fear of missing it, because tawaf can be done whenever he wishes – he can do it until the end of his life. Some scholars said that in this issue there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: the one prevented from tawaf and wuquf in the Haram is not muhsar according to Abu Hanifa but is muhsar according to Abu Yusuf. And the correct is that this detail is the statement of all: if he is prevented from both wuquf and tawaf, he is muhsar; and if he is able to do one, he is not muhsar.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute within the chapter on Ihsar. It begins by stating the general ruling: if a person in ihram is prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram, he is considered muhsar and can become halal by sending a hadi. However, if he can perform either one, he is not muhsar. The author then clarifies that if he can do tawaf, he is fayit al-hajj and becomes halal through tawaf; if he can do wuquf, his hajj is complete. The dispute arises in a specific scenario: a person who does wuquf at Arafah but is then prevented from the remaining rites. According to Abu Hanifa, he is not muhsar because the fear of missing hajj is gone, but he owes four dams for leaving wajibat. According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he owes only two dams (for leaving wuquf Muzdalifah and ramy) because delaying tawaf al-ziyarah and halq does not require a dam. Another scenario discussed is the person prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram: Abu Hanifa says he is not muhsar because he can still do one of them? Actually the text says according to some, Abu Hanifa says he is not muhsar, while Abu Yusuf says he is muhsar. But the author concludes that the correct view is the detailed one: if prevented from both, he is muhsar; if able to do one, he is not. This aligns with the main ruling. The passage teaches the precise conditions for ihsar and the differences between the imams in applying the rules.

Key Terms
محصر (muhsar): A person in ihram prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah by an enemy or illness, specifically when prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram for this scenario.
احصار (ihsar): The state of being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to external factors, here discussed within the Haram.
فائت الحج (fayit al-hajj): One who has missed the Hajj entirely (by missing wuquf at Arafah) but can still perform tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the text, if a person in ihram is prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram, what is his status?
A) He is muhsar only if he cannot do tawaf.
B) He is muhsar.
C) He is not muhsar under any circumstance.
D) He is fayit al-hajj.

Key Takeaway
A person prevented from both tawaf and wuquf in the Haram is muhsar; if able to do one, he is not muhsar.

Ruling on One Who Misses Wuquf at Arafah (Fawat al-Hajj)
Beginning of the Fawat chapter: ruling and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who misses wuquf at Arafah, explain the proof, and apply the distinction between fawat and ihsar.

Core Idea
Missing wuquf at Arafah invalidates Hajj; must do Umrah and qada, no dam.

This lesson opens the chapter on Fawat al-Hajj. We learn the critical distinction between being prevented (ihsar) and missing the essential rite (fawat). The passage provides the ruling and its proof from hadith, along with the reasoning that Umrah substitutes for the sacrifice required in ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is missing wuquf at Arafah until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr. The ruling is that the Hajj is invalidated (fayit).
This is the core ruling.
2
Locate the required actions
The person must perform tawaf and sa'y as an Umrah to exit ihram, and must make up the Hajj the following year. No dam is required.
These actions are wajib.
3
Examine the dalil
The dalil is a hadith: 'Whoever misses Arafah by night has missed Hajj; let him become halal by Umrah, and upon him is Hajj the following year.'
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati dalala).
4
Understand the reasoning
Valid ihram can only be exited by completing one of the two rites (Hajj or Umrah). Since Hajj is impossible, Umrah becomes obligatory. Umrah substitutes for the blood sacrifice that would be required in ihsar.
This is an application of necessity and analogy with ihram mubham.

Chapter of Fawat. Translation: This chapter is about expressing the occurrence of hajj fawat. Explanation: Ihsar is like a singular, and fawat is like a compound, because ihsar is the state of ihram without performing the rites, while fawat is the performance of ihram and the rites. The one who tied ihram for hajj and his wuquf at Arafah was missed until the dawn of Yawm al-Nahr rose – his hajj is missed. And whoever enters into ihram for hajj and misses wuquf at Arafah until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr rises – indeed his hajj is missed, because we mentioned that the time for wuquf extends to that. And upon him is to perform tawaf and sa'y and become halal, and to make up the hajj the following year, and there is no blood (sacrifice) upon him, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'Whoever misses Arafah by night has indeed missed hajj; let him become halal by Umrah, and upon him is the hajj the following year.' And Umrah is nothing but tawaf and sa'y. And because the ihram, after having been validly contracted, there is no way to exit it except by performing one of the two rites, as in the ambiguous ihram. And here he is incapable of hajj, so Umrah becomes determined upon him. And there is no blood upon him because the tahallul occurred by the actions of Umrah, so in the case of the one who missed hajj, it is like the blood in the case of the muhsar, so they are not combined. And upon him is wajib to perform tawaf and sa'y and become halal. And if wuquf at Arafah is missed by night, then his hajj is missed, so he becomes halal by performing Umrah, and upon him is hajj the following year. And Umrah is only the name of tawaf and sa'y. And because after the ihram is validly contracted, there is no way to exit from it except by performing one of the two rites, as in the ambiguous ihram. And here he is unable to do hajj, so Umrah becomes determined. And there is no blood upon him because becoming halal occurs by performing the actions of Umrah. So for the one who missed hajj, performing Umrah is like the blood for the muhsar, so both Umrah and sacrifice are not combined. Explanation of the issue: A person tied ihram for hajj and wuquf at Arafah was missed from him until the dawn of Yawm al-Nahr rose, then his hajj is missed. Because we have previously explained that the time of wuquf at Arafah lasts until the true dawn of Yawm al-Nahr – it does not remain after that. And it has also been explained that the one whose wuquf at Arafah is missed – his hajj is missed. Now upon him it is wajib to become halal by performing Umrah. And to make up that hajj the following year, and no blood is wajib upon him as expiation. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever misses wuquf at Arafah by night – his hajj is missed. So he should become halal by Umrah, and upon him performing hajj the following year is necessary.' And Umrah...
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Fawat al-Hajj (missing Hajj). It begins by distinguishing between ihsar (prevention) and fawat (missing the wuquf). Ihsar is likened to a singular term because it involves ihram without performing any rites, while fawat is like a compound because it involves ihram and performing some rites but missing the essential wuquf. The core ruling is stated: if a person in ihram for Hajj misses wuquf at Arafah until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), his Hajj is considered missed (fayit). The time for wuquf extends until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr; after that, it is lost. The person must then: (1) perform tawaf and sa'y to exit ihram (as an Umrah), (2) make up the missed Hajj the following year, and (3) no dam (sacrificial animal) is required because the Umrah acts serve the same purpose as the dam for a muhsar. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever misses Arafah by night has indeed missed Hajj; let him become halal by Umrah, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' The reasoning is that valid ihram cannot be exited except by completing either Hajj or Umrah; since he is unable to complete Hajj, Umrah becomes obligatory to break the ihram. The dam is not combined with Umrah because the Umrah itself suffices as compensation. The commentary emphasizes that wuquf at Arafah is the pillar (rukn) of Hajj; missing it invalidates the Hajj entirely. The time for wuquf is from the afternoon of 9th Dhul Hijjah until dawn of 10th; if one misses this entire window, the Hajj is invalidated.

Key Terms
فوات (fawat): Missing the essential rite (wuquf at Arafah) of Hajj, thereby invalidating the Hajj.
فائت الحج (fayit al-hajj): A person whose Hajj has been invalidated due to missing wuquf at Arafah.
قضاء (qada): Making up the missed or invalidated Hajj in a subsequent year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary proof for the ruling that a fayit al-hajj must perform Umrah and not a dam?
A) Qiyas on ihsar
B) The hadith: 'Whoever misses Arafah by night...'
C) Ijma of the companions
D) The Quranic verse on completing Hajj

Key Takeaway
Missing wuquf at Arafah until dawn of Yawm al-Nahr invalidates the Hajj, and the remedy is to perform Umrah to exit ihram and make up the Hajj the following year, with no dam required.

The Hanafi Ruling on a Missed Hajj (Fawāt al-Hajj) and the Dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i
Ruling on missing wuqūf ‘Arafah and required actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person whose Hajj becomes fā’it, explain the proof from ḥadīth, and evaluate the Shafi'i argument for requiring a dam.

Core Idea
Missing 'Arafah turns your Hajj into 'Umrah—no dam needed because the 'Umrah itself is the compensation.

This passage from the Chapter of Fawāt in Kitāb al-Ḥajj presents a clear ruling with a built-in madhhab dispute. You will see how the Ḥanafī school derives the obligation to perform 'Umrah and make up the Ḥajj, and why it rejects the analogy to the muḥṣar (one prevented) that leads the Shāfi'ī school to require a dam. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main ruling: what must the fā’it al-ḥajj do? What is not required? Use the source text to list the required actions (ṭawāf, sa‘ī, taḥallul, qaḍā’) and note the absence of dam.
The ruling is clear: no dam, only 'Umrah and make-up.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (against whom the argument is directed) holds that a dam is required, analogizing to the muḥṣar. This is an inter-madhhab ikhtilāf.
The opposing view is based on qiyās.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i proof: they compare the one who missed (fā’it) to the one prevented (muḥṣar). Both have a valid iḥrām but cannot complete Ḥajj; therefore a dam should be wajib.
This analogy seems strong at first glance.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response breaks the analogy: the muḥṣar cannot perform 'Umrah (because he is prevented from entering Makkah), so he needs a dam. The fā’it can perform 'Umrah, so the 'Umrah acts replace the dam. The text says: 'the taḥallul is achieved by the actions of 'Umrah, so it is like the dam for the muḥṣar; thus they are not combined.'
The key distinction is the ability to do 'Umrah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Ḥanafī muftī will not require a dam, while a Shāfi‘ī will. The Ḥanafī position is muftā bihī (relied upon) in the Ḥanafī school.
This has financial and ritual consequences for the pilgrim.

باب الفوات
وَمَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ وَفَاتِهِ الْوُقُوفُ بِعَرَفَةَ حَتَّى طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ لِمَا ذَكَرَنَا أَنَّ وَقْتَ الْوُقُوفِ يَمْتَدُّ إِلَيْهِ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ وَيَسْعَى وَيَتَحَلَّلَ وَيَقْضِيَ الْحَجَّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَلَا دَمَ عَلَيْهِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: مَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَةُ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَلْيَتَحَلَّلْ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَالْعُمْرَةُ لَيْسَتْ إِلَّا الطَّوَافُ وَالسَّعْيُ وَلِأَنَّ الْإِحْرَامَ بَعْدَمَا انْعَقَدَ صَحِيحًا لَا طَرِيقَ لِلْخُرُوجِ عَنْهُ إِلَّا بِأَدَاءِ أَحَدِ النُّسُكَيْنِ كَمَا فِي الْإِحْرَامِ الْمُبْهَمِ وَهُنَا عَجَزَ عَنِ الْحَجِّ فَتَتَعَيَّنُ عَلَيْهِ الْعُمْرَةُ وَلَا دَمَ عَلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ التَّحَلُّلَ وَقَعَ بِأَفْعَالِ الْعُمْرَةِ فَكَانَتْ فِي حَقِّ فَائِتِ الْحَجِّ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الدَّمِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُحْصَرِ فَلَا يُجْمَعُ بَيْنَهُمَا
Chapter of Missing (Hajj). Whoever enters Ihram for Hajj and misses the standing at 'Arafah until dawn of the Day of Sacrifice breaks, then his Hajj is lost because the time of standing extends to that. He must perform Tawaf and Sa'i, become halal (by shaving/trimming), and perform the make-up Hajj next year, and there is no blood sacrifice upon him due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever misses 'Arafah at night has missed Hajj, so let him become halal by an 'Umrah, and he must perform Hajj next year.' 'Umrah is nothing but Tawaf and Sa'i. And because the Ihram, once validly contracted, there is no way out of it except by performing one of the two rites, as in the ambiguous Ihram. Here he is unable to perform Hajj, so 'Umrah becomes determined for him. There is no blood sacrifice upon him because the halal (release) occurs by the actions of 'Umrah, so it is in the case of the one who missed Hajj like the blood sacrifice in the case of the one prevented (muhsar); thus both are not combined.
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter of Fawāt (Missing) in Kitāb al-Hajj presents the Hanafi ruling for one whose Ḥajj becomes fā’it (lost) by missing the standing at ‘Arafah. The ruling: if one enters iḥrām for Ḥajj and misses the wuqūf at ‘Arafah until the dawn of the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), then the Ḥajj is considered lost. He must perform ‘Umrah (tawāf and sa‘ī), become ḥalāl (by shaving or trimming), and make up the Ḥajj the following year. No dam (sacrificial animal) is required. The proof is the ḥadīth: “Whoever misses ‘Arafah at night has missed Ḥajj, so let him become ḥalāl by ‘Umrah, and he must perform Ḥajj next year.” The reasoning continues: since the iḥrām was validly contracted, one can only exit by performing either Ḥajj or ‘Umrah; inability to complete Ḥajj necessitates ‘Umrah. No dam is required because the acts of ‘Umrah themselves serve as compensation, analogous to the dam for the muḥṣar (one prevented from continuing Ḥajj), so both are not combined. The passage also implicitly addresses the Shāfi‘ī view that a dam is required, analogizing fā’it al-ḥajj to muḥṣar. The Hanafī response is that the analogy fails because the muḥṣar cannot perform ‘Umrah, whereas the one who missed Ḥajj can, so the acts of ‘Umrah substitute for the dam. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is the Hanafī view.

Key Terms
الفوات (al-fawāt): Missing the essential pillar (wuqūf 'Arafah) by the end of its time, resulting in loss of Hajj.
المحصر (al-muḥṣar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or 'Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other obstacles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do if he misses the standing at 'Arafah and his Hajj becomes fā’it?
A) Offer a dam and make up the Hajj next year.
B) Perform 'Umrah, become halal, and make up the Hajj next year with no dam.
C) Do nothing; the Hajj is invalid and no compensation needed.
D) Perform 'Umrah and offer a dam as compensation.

Key Takeaway
Missing the standing at 'Arafah renders the Ḥajj lost; the pilgrim must perform 'Umrah, become ḥalāl, and make up the Ḥajj the following year without offering a dam.

Disliked Days for 'Umrah and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on when 'Umrah is valid and disliked days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five days on which 'Umrah is disliked, explain the proof and reasoning, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the Day of 'Arafah.

Core Idea
Umrah is valid all year except five Hajj days – performing it then is valid but disliked.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hajj chapter: although 'Umrah is not time-bound, the Hanafi school identifies five days when performing it is discouraged. We will explore the textual evidence, the underlying rationale, and a notable difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the Day of 'Arafah. This case exemplifies how later Hanafi authorities resolve internal ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and exception
Identify that 'Umrah is permissible all year except five days, and list those days.
The five days: Day of 'Arafah, Day of Nahr, three Days of Tashreeq.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
Understand the evidence: the practice of 'Aisha (ra) and the principle that these days are dedicated to Hajj.
The hadith is a companion action, not a direct prophetic command.
3
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
The dislike is to magnify Hajj and keep its days exclusive.
The dislike is not due to inherent defect in 'Umrah but out of reverence.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that on the Day of 'Arafah before noon it is not disliked because the wuquf time begins after noon.
This is a dispute within the school; the matn gives the relied-upon position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text declares the azhar (more apparent) position is the general dislike for all five full days.
The mufta bihi is the general dislike, not Abu Yusuf's exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعُمْرَةُ لَا تَفُوتُ وَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ إِلَّا خَمْسَةَ أَيَّامٍ يُكْرَهُ فِيهَا فِعْلُهَا وَهِيَ يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ وَيَوْمُ النَّحْرِ وَأَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا كَانَتْ تَكْرَهُ الْعُمْرَةَ فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ الْخَمْسَةِ وَلِأَنَّ هَذِهِ أَيَّامُ الْحَجِّ فَكَانَتْ مُتَعَيِّنَةً لَهُ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يُكْرَهُ فِي يَوْمِ عَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ الزَّوَالِ لِأَنَّ دُخُولَ وَقْتِ رُكْنِ الْحَجِّ بَعْدَ الزَّوَالِ لَا قَبْلَهُ وَالْأَظْهَرُ مِنَ الْمَذْهَبِ مَا ذَكَرْنَاهُ وَلَكِنْ مَعَ هَذَا لَوْ أَدَّاهَا فِي هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ صَحَّ وَيَبْقَى مُحْرِمًا بِهَا فِيهَا لِأَنَّ الْكَرَاهَةَ لِغَيْرِهَا وَهُوَ تَعْظِيمُ أَمْرِ الْحَجِّ وَتَخْلِيصُ وَقْتِهِ لَهُ فَيَصِحُّ الشُّرُوعُ
And 'Umrah is not lost (time-bound); it is permissible throughout the entire year except for five days during which performing it is disliked. They are: the Day of 'Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq. Because it is reported from 'Aisha that she disliked 'Umrah on these five days, and because these are the days of Hajj, so they are determined for it. And from Abu Yusuf that it is not disliked on the Day of 'Arafah before noon because the entry of the time of the pillar of Hajj is after noon, not before. The more apparent (azhar) of the school is what we have mentioned. However, despite this, if one performs it on these days, it is valid and he remains in Ihram for it in them because the dislike is for something else, which is magnifying the matter of Hajj and dedicating its time to it; thus the commencement is valid.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Hajj discusses the temporal validity of 'Umrah. It states that 'Umrah is not time-bound (lā tafūt) and is permissible throughout the year except for five days when performing it is disliked: the Day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and the three Days of Tashreeq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah). The proof is the practice of 'Aisha (ra) who disliked 'Umrah on these days, and the reasoning that these days are specifically dedicated to the rites of Hajj. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf: Abu Yusuf holds that it is not disliked on the Day of 'Arafah before noon, because the time for the Hajj rite (wuqūf of 'Arafah) begins after zawāl (noon). However, the most apparent (al-aẓhar) position of the school is that the dislike applies throughout the entire day (from dawn). Despite this dislike, if one performs 'Umrah on these days, it is valid and one remains in ihrām because the dislike is not due to an inherent defect in 'Umrah, but rather to show reverence for Hajj and to keep those times dedicated to it. Thus the commencement is valid.

Key Terms
أيام التشريق (ayyām al-tashrīq): The three days following the Day of Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah).
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike (makruh tanzih), a category less than prohibition; the act is valid but discouraged.
يَوْمُ النَّحْرِ (yawm al-naḥr): The Day of Sacrifice, the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, when Hajj pilgrims perform the sacrifice.
يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ (yawm 'arafah): The 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of standing at 'Arafah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On how many days is performing 'Umrah disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only the Day of 'Arafah.
B) Five days: Day of 'Arafah, Day of Nahr, and three Days of Tashreeq.
C) All days of Dhul Hijjah.
D) Only the Day of Nahr.

Key Takeaway
'Umrah is valid throughout the year; on the five days of Hajj it is makruh tanzih but not invalid.

Missing Hajj: 'Umrah Required, No Dam Needed
Explains ruling for one who misses Hajj and must perform Umrah, with no dam required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for one who misses Hajj (fā'it al-ḥajj) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on capability.

Core Idea
Missing Hajj requires 'Umrah to exit ihram; no dam is needed because the person is capable of performing it.

When a pilgrim enters ihram for Hajj but misses the standing at Arafat, the Hajj is invalid for that season. The Hanafi school rules that such a person must perform 'Umrah to become halal, with no additional sacrifice. However, Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes this to a prevented pilgrim (muḥṣar), who must offer a dam. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi distinction based on capability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the ruling for fā'it al-ḥajj according to the Hanafi school? Identify the required action and whether a dam is obligatory.
The text states 'no dam is wajib' and that 'Umrah suffices.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school disagrees, and what do they hold? State Imam al-Shafi'i's position on the same case.
Imam al-Shafi'i requires a dam in addition to 'Umrah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What evidence does Imam al-Shafi'i use? Identify the analogy (qiyas) to muhsar.
The Shafi'i argument: just as a muhsar must offer a dam, so must the fā'it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the analogy? What is the key distinction?
The fā'it is capable of 'Umrah, while the muhsar is not. Therefore, the 'illa (cause) differs, and the analogy fails.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings between the two schools?
Hanafi: only 'Umrah required; Shafi'i: 'Umrah plus an animal sacrifice (dam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
۵۱۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم
علاوہ
طواف وسعی کا نام ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ احرام تو صحیح طور پر منعقد ہو چکا۔ اب اس کے بعد احرام سے نکلنے کا کوئی راستہ نہیں علیا اس کے کہ ارکان حج ادا کرے یا ارکان عمرہ ادا کرے۔ جیسے کسی نے مبہم احرام باندھا یعنی احرام تو باندھا مگر حج یا عمرہ کی نیت نہیں کی تو اس صورت میں اس پر کسی ایک کو ادا کرنا ضروری ہے اسی طرح یہاں بھی ایک کو ادا کرنا ضروری ہوگا، لیکن حج فوت ہونے سے حج سے تو عاجز ہو گیا پس اس پر عمرہ متعین ہو گیا۔
اس پر ہمارے نزدیک دم واجب نہیں ہے۔ البتہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک دم واجب ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فوات حج کو مخصر پر قیاس کیا ہے۔ پس جس طرح مصر پر دم واجب ہوتا ہے اسی طرح حج فوت ہونے کی صورت میں بھی دم واجب ہوگا ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ فائت الحج افعال عمرہ ادا کر کے حلال ہوتا ہے۔ پس فائت المج کے حق میں افعال عمرہ کا ادا کرنا ایسا ہے جس طرح محصر کے حق میں دم ہے۔ پس دونوں کو جمع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ یعنی حلال ہونے کے لئے اصل تو عمرہ ہے مگر چونکہ مصر عمرہ پر قادر نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے اس کے عوض میں ہدی لازم ہے پس محصر ارکان عمرہ ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہے اور فائت الج قادر ہے ۔ دونوں کے درمیان تباین ہے اس لئے ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔
The Book of Hajj. 512. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume three. In addition, it is the name of tawaf and sa'y. The second proof is that the ihram has been validly initiated. After that, there is no way to exit the ihram until one performs the pillars of Hajj or the pillars of 'Umrah. For example, if someone ties a vague ihram, i.e., he ties ihram but does not intend Hajj or 'Umrah, then in that case it is necessary for him to perform one of them. Similarly here, it will be necessary to perform one. But since Hajj is missed, he becomes incapable of Hajj, so 'Umrah becomes specified for him. According to us, no dam (blood sacrifice) is wajib. However, according to Imam Shafi'i, dam is wajib. Imam Shafi'i analogizes fawat al-hajj (missing Hajj) to muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj). So just as dam is wajib for muhsar, similarly in the case of missing Hajj, dam will be wajib. Our proof is that the fā'it al-hajj (one who missed Hajj) becomes halal by performing the actions of 'Umrah. So for the fā'it al-hajj, performing the actions of 'Umrah is like the dam for the muhsar. Therefore, both will not be combined. That is, the original for becoming halal is 'Umrah, but since the muhsar is not capable of 'Umrah, a hady (sacrificial animal) is required instead. So the muhsar is incapable of performing the actions of 'Umrah, while the fā'it is capable. There is a disparity between the two, so it is not correct to analogize one to the other.
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling for a person who enters ihram for Hajj but misses the Hajj (e.g., fails to stand at Arafat on time). The Hanafi school rules that such a person must perform 'Umrah to exit ihram, and no dam (blood sacrifice) is required. Imam Shafi'i holds that a dam is wajib, analogizing the situation to that of a muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj by enemy or illness), for whom a dam is wajib. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the two cases: the fā'it al-hajj is capable of performing 'Umrah, while the muhsar is not. Therefore, for the fā'it, 'Umrah itself suffices for becoming halal, and there is no need for a dam. The analogy fails because the underlying cause ('illa) is different: the muhsar cannot perform 'Umrah, so compensation (dam) is required; the fā'it can, so the dam is not required. This reasoning is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference). The passage emphasizes that both (Umrah and dam) cannot be combined because each serves the same purpose of releasing from ihram.

Key Terms
فائت الحج (fā'it al-ḥajj): One who has entered ihram for Hajj but misses the Hajj (e.g., fails to perform the standing at Arafat on time), making Hajj invalid for that season.
محصر (muḥṣar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or 'Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other valid obstruction after entering ihram.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required as compensation for certain omissions or violations during Hajj or 'Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a person who misses Hajj (fā'it al-ḥajj)?
A) He must perform 'Umrah and offer a dam.
B) He must perform 'Umrah only, no dam required.
C) He must offer a dam only, without 'Umrah.
D) He must repeat Hajj the next year in ihram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes fā'it al-ḥajj from muhsar based on capability for 'Umrah, so only 'Umrah is required, no dam.

The Legal Status of 'Umrah: Sunnah Not Fard
Hanafi rejection of Shafi'i obligation claim for 'Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah, explain the evidence, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A contradiction in transmitted proofs prevents obligation — 'Umrah remains sunnah not fard.

The status of 'Umrah has been debated between schools. While the Shafi'is and Hanbalis consider it obligatory once in a lifetime, the Hanafi school holds it as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). This lesson examines the textual and rational evidence that leads to the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school rules regarding 'Umrah: it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard nor wajib.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold 'Umrah to be fard (obligatory).
The Shafi'i position is based on a different hadith.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i proof: the hadith 'Umrah is fard like Hajj is fard.'
This is a direct textual claim of obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school counters: they cite the hadith 'Hajj is fard and 'Umrah is tatawwu' and add rational signs (no fixed time, can be intended for another) indicating nafl. They reinterpret the Shafi'i hadith as measuring actions, not obligation.
Contradiction in transmitted proofs prevents establishing obligation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
See the practical difference: Hanafi — performing 'Umrah is recommended, leaving it not sinful; Shafi'i — must do it once, omission is sinful.
This affects one's religious obligations and accountability.

وَالْعُمْرَةُ سُنَّةٌ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فَرِيضَةٌ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْعُمْرَةُ فَرِيضَةٌ كَفَرِ يُضَةِ الْحَجّ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْحَجُّ فَرِيضَةٌ وَالْعُمْرَةُ تَطَوُّعَ وَلَأنَّهَا غَيْرُ مُوَفَّتَةٍ بِوَقْتِ وَ تَنَادَى بِنِيَّةِ غَيْرِهَا كَمَا فِي فَائِتِ الْحَجَ وَهَذِهِ أَمَارَةُ النَّفْلِيَّةِ وَ تَاوِيلُ مَارَوَاهُ أَنَّهَا مُقَدَّرَةٌ بِاَعْمَالِ الْحَجَ إِذَلَا تَثْبُتُ الْفَرْضِيَّةُ مَعَ التَّعَارُضِ فِي الْآثَارِ قَالَ وَهِيَ الطَّوَافُ وَالسَّعَى وَ قَدْ ذَكَرْنَاهُ فِى بَابِ التَّمَتَّعِ وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَابِ
And 'Umrah is sunnah. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is fard (obligatory) because of his (the Prophet's) statement: 'Umrah is fard like Hajj is fard.' Our proof is his statement: 'Hajj is fard and 'Umrah is tatawwu' (supererogatory). And because it is not restricted to a specific time, and it is fulfilled by the intention of another (as in the case of one who misses Hajj), and these are signs of being nafl (supererogatory). And the interpretation of what he (al-Shafi'i) narrated is that it is measured by the actions of Hajj, for obligation is not established when there is contradiction in the traditions. He said: it is tawaf and sa'y, and we have mentioned it in the chapter of tamattu'. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 514

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the legal status of 'Umrah. The Hanafi school holds that 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), not obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that it is fard (obligatory). The Shafi'i proof is the hadith: 'Umrah is fard like Hajj is fard. The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'Hajj is fard and 'Umrah is tatawwu'.' The Hanafi school adds two rational proofs: (1) 'Umrah is not tied to a specific time, whereas obligations usually have fixed times; (2) 'Umrah can be fulfilled with the intention of another act, as in the case of one who misses Hajj (fā'it al-ḥajj) where the person intends Hajj but performs 'Umrah instead. Both of these are signs of supererogatory (nafl) acts. The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i hadith is that it means 'Umrah is measured with the actions of Hajj and is analogous in form, not that it shares the same obligation. Furthermore, when narrations contradict, obligation cannot be established. The passage concludes that 'Umrah consists of tawaf and sa'y, as previously mentioned.

Key Terms
عمرہ (ʿUmrah): The lesser pilgrimage consisting of tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or cutting hair; in this text, it is discussed as sunnah.
سنت (sunnah): A recommended act; here specifically sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) that the Prophet consistently performed.
تطوع (taṭawwuʿ): Voluntary, supererogatory act of worship; used in the hadith to describe 'Umrah's status.

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah's legal status?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah)
C) It is mubah (permissible but not recommended)
D) It is haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules 'Umrah as sunnah mu'akkadah due to contradictory hadith and rational signs, placing it as a recommended but not obligatory act.
